Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
The Essential Eschatological Beliefs
The poem enumerates required beliefs about the afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific eschatological beliefs that a Muslim must have faith in according to this poem.

Core Idea
Faith requires belief in the afterlife details: Reckoning, Gathering, Path, Balance, and more.

This poem begins by listing the essential articles of faith concerning the afterlife (samiyyat). These are matters known by revelation, and the poet enumerates them in a compact form. Let us examine each item.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic lines listing the beliefs. Notice the sequence: general events, then specific items, then beings.
The poet uses 'thumma' (then) to connect some items.
2
Identify each belief
Go through the list: Reckoning, Gathering, Punishment, Reward, Scattering, Path, Balance, Pond, Fire, Gardens, Jinn, Angels, Prophets, Huris, Youth, Saints. Understand each term.
Some terms like 'nashr' (scattering) refer to resurrection.
3
Reflect on the comprehensiveness
Consider why the poet includes both physical items (Path, Balance) and spiritual beings (Jinn, Angels, Saints).
All are part of the unseen (ghayb) that must be believed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَلْزَمُ الإِيْمَانُ بِالحِسَابِ وَالحَشْرِ وَالعِقَابِ وَالثَّوَابِ وَالنَّشْرِ وَالصِّرَاطِ وَالمِيزَانِ وَالحَوْضِ وَالنِّيرَانِ وَالجِنَانِ وَالجِنِّ وَالأَمْلاَكِ ثُمَّ الأَنْبِيَا وَالحُوْرِ وَالوِلْدَانِ ثُمَّ الأَوْلِيَا وَبِكُلِّ مَا جَاءَ عَنِ البَشِيْرِ مِنْ كُلِّ حُكْمِ صَارَ كَالضَّرُوْرِي وَيَنْطَوِي فِي كِلْمَةِ الإِسْلَامِ مَا قَدْ مَضَى مِنْ سَائِرِ الأَحْكَامِ فَأَكْثِرَنْ مِنْ ذِكْرِهَا بِالأَدَبِ تَرْقَى بِهَذَا الذِّكْرِ أَعْلَى الرُّتَبِ وَغَلِّبِ الخَوْفَ عَلَى الرَّجَاءِ وَسِرْ لِمَوْلاَكَ بِلاَ تَنَاءِ وَجَدِّدِ التَّوْبَةَ لِلأَوْزَارِ لاَ تَيْأَسَنْ مِنْ رَحْمَةِ الغَفَّارِ وَكُنْ عَلَى آلائِهِ شَكُوْرًا وَكُنْ عَلَى بَلاَئِهِ صَبُوْرًا فَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ بِالقَضَاءِ وَالقَدَرْ وَكُلُّ مَقْدُوْرٍ فَمَا عَنْهُ مَفَرْ فَكُنْ لَهُ مُسَلِّمًا كَيْ تَسْلَمَا وَاتْبَعْ سَبِيْلَ النَّاسِكِيْنَ العُلَمَا وَخَلِّصِ القَلْبَ مِنَ الأَغْيَارِ بِالجِدِّ وَالقِيَامِ فِي الأَسْحَارِ وَالفِكْرِ وَالذِّكْرِ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ مُجْتَنِبًا لِسَائِرِ الآثَامِ مُرَاقِبًا لِلَّهِ فِي الأَحْوَالِ لِتَرْتَقِي مَعَالِمَ الكَمَالِ وَقُلْ بِذُلِّ رَبِّ لاَ تَقْطَعْنِي عَنْكَ بِقَاطِعْ وَلاَ تَحْرِمْنِي مِنْ سِرِّكَ الأَبْهَى المُزِيْلِ لِلْعَمَى وَاخْتُمْ بِخَيْرٍ يَا رَحِيْمَ الرُّحَمَا وَالحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ عَلَى الإِنْمَامِ وَأَفْضَلُ الصَّلاَةِ وَالسَّلاَمِ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيِّ الخَاتِمِ وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ الأَكَارِمِ
And faith is required in the Reckoning, the Gathering, the Punishment, the Reward, the Scattering, the Path, the Balance, the Pond, the Fire, the Gardens, the Jinn, the Angels, then the Prophets, the Huris, the Youth, then the Saints. And in everything that came from the Bringer of Glad Tidings (the Prophet) of every ruling that became like the necessary. And what has passed of all the rulings is enclosed in the word of Islam. So increase in its remembrance with etiquette; by this remembrance you will ascend to the highest ranks. And make fear prevail over hope, and journey to your Lord without separation. And renew repentance for sins, and do not despair of the mercy of the Oft-Forgiving. And be grateful for His blessings, and be patient in His trial. For every matter is by decree and predestination, and from every predestined thing there is no escape. So submit to Him so that you may be safe, and follow the path of the ascetic scholars. And purify the heart from distractions with seriousness and standing in the early mornings, and constant thought and remembrance, avoiding all sins, being watchful of Allah in all states, so that you may ascend to the peaks of perfection. And say in humility: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter, and do not deprive me of Your most splendid secret that removes blindness. And conclude with good, O Most Merciful of the merciful. And praise be to Allah for completion, and the best of prayers and peace be upon the Prophet, the Hashimi, the Seal, and his family and noble companions.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This is an enumeration of the articles of faith (īmān) and a concluding exhortation. The poet lists what must be believed: the Reckoning (ḥisāb), Gathering (ḥashr), Punishment (ʿiqāb), Reward (thawāb), Scattering (nashr), Path (ṣirāṭ), Balance (mīzān), Pond (ḥawḍ), Fire (nīrān), Gardens (jinān), Jinn, Angels, Prophets, Huris, Youth (wildān), and Saints (awliyā). Then he says that all these rulings are enclosed (yanṭawī) in the word of Islam (kalimat al-islām), i.e., the shahada encompasses all. Then he gives practical advice: increase remembrance (dhikr) with etiquette, make fear (khawf) prevail over hope (rajāʾ), renew repentance (tawba), be grateful (shakūr) and patient (ṣabūr), acknowledge that all is by predestination (qaḍāʾ wa qadar), submit (musallim), follow ascetic scholars, purify the heart, engage in dhikr, and avoid sins. The poem ends with a supplication and blessings on the Prophet.

Key Terms
الحساب
الحشر
الصراط
الميزان
الحوض
الجنة
النار
الجن
الملائكة
الأنبياء
الحور
الولدان
الأولياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think only a few of these are required to believe in.
Correction: The poem states that faith is required (yalzam) in each of these, so all are obligatory articles of faith.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned in the list of required beliefs in the poem?
A) The Reckoning
B) The Balance
C) The Pen
D) The Pond

Key Takeaway
A Muslim must have faith in a specific set of afterlife events and beings as part of the samiyyat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The poet says 'faith is required' in the Reckoning, Path, Balance, etc. Which of these realities do you think about least, and what is one practical step you can take this week to make it more present in your heart?
?
Consider the line 'وبالحور والولدان والأولياء' – belief in the Huris, Youth, and Saints is obligatory. Do you treat these as just nice stories, or as actual beings waiting for you? How would your daily choices change if you truly believed you will meet them?
?
If you were to be gathered and judged today, which three deeds from your life do you think would weigh heaviest on the Balance? Start a list of deeds you can add to the good side starting tomorrow.

Unseen Matters
beginner
3 min
All Encompassed in the Word of Islam
The poem declares that all rulings from the Prophet are enclosed in the word of Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all these rulings are encompassed in the word of Islam (shahada).

Core Idea
The shahada contains all the rulings of faith.

After listing the beliefs, the poet states that everything that came from the Prophet regarding rulings is enclosed in the word of Islam. This highlights the comprehensiveness of the testimony of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the line: 'wa yanṭawī fī kalimat al-islām mā qad maḍā min sāʾir al-aḥkām'. Notice the word yanṭawī (enclosed).
2
Understand the implication
Reflect on how the shahada is not just a phrase but contains all Islamic teachings.
The entire religion is summarized in the testimony of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَلْزَمُ الإِيْمَانُ بِالحِسَابِ وَالحَشْرِ وَالعِقَابِ وَالثَّوَابِ وَالنَّشْرِ وَالصِّرَاطِ وَالمِيزَانِ وَالحَوْضِ وَالنِّيرَانِ وَالجِنَانِ وَالجِنِّ وَالأَمْلاَكِ ثُمَّ الأَنْبِيَا وَالحُوْرِ وَالوِلْدَانِ ثُمَّ الأَوْلِيَا وَبِكُلِّ مَا جَاءَ عَنِ البَشِيْرِ مِنْ كُلِّ حُكْمِ صَارَ كَالضَّرُوْرِي وَيَنْطَوِي فِي كِلْمَةِ الإِسْلَامِ مَا قَدْ مَضَى مِنْ سَائِرِ الأَحْكَامِ فَأَكْثِرَنْ مِنْ ذِكْرِهَا بِالأَدَبِ تَرْقَى بِهَذَا الذِّكْرِ أَعْلَى الرُّتَبِ وَغَلِّبِ الخَوْفَ عَلَى الرَّجَاءِ وَسِرْ لِمَوْلاَكَ بِلاَ تَنَاءِ وَجَدِّدِ التَّوْبَةَ لِلأَوْزَارِ لاَ تَيْأَسَنْ مِنْ رَحْمَةِ الغَفَّارِ وَكُنْ عَلَى آلائِهِ شَكُوْرًا وَكُنْ عَلَى بَلاَئِهِ صَبُوْرًا فَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ بِالقَضَاءِ وَالقَدَرْ وَكُلُّ مَقْدُوْرٍ فَمَا عَنْهُ مَفَرْ فَكُنْ لَهُ مُسَلِّمًا كَيْ تَسْلَمَا وَاتْبَعْ سَبِيْلَ النَّاسِكِيْنَ العُلَمَا وَخَلِّصِ القَلْبَ مِنَ الأَغْيَارِ بِالجِدِّ وَالقِيَامِ فِي الأَسْحَارِ وَالفِكْرِ وَالذِّكْرِ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ مُجْتَنِبًا لِسَائِرِ الآثَامِ مُرَاقِبًا لِلَّهِ فِي الأَحْوَالِ لِتَرْتَقِي مَعَالِمَ الكَمَالِ وَقُلْ بِذُلِّ رَبِّ لاَ تَقْطَعْنِي عَنْكَ بِقَاطِعْ وَلاَ تَحْرِمْنِي مِنْ سِرِّكَ الأَبْهَى المُزِيْلِ لِلْعَمَى وَاخْتُمْ بِخَيْرٍ يَا رَحِيْمَ الرُّحَمَا وَالحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ عَلَى الإِنْمَامِ وَأَفْضَلُ الصَّلاَةِ وَالسَّلاَمِ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيِّ الخَاتِمِ وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ الأَكَارِمِ
And faith is required in the Reckoning, the Gathering, the Punishment, the Reward, the Scattering, the Path, the Balance, the Pond, the Fire, the Gardens, the Jinn, the Angels, then the Prophets, the Huris, the Youth, then the Saints. And in everything that came from the Bringer of Glad Tidings (the Prophet) of every ruling that became like the necessary. And what has passed of all the rulings is enclosed in the word of Islam. So increase in its remembrance with etiquette; by this remembrance you will ascend to the highest ranks. And make fear prevail over hope, and journey to your Lord without separation. And renew repentance for sins, and do not despair of the mercy of the Oft-Forgiving. And be grateful for His blessings, and be patient in His trial. For every matter is by decree and predestination, and from every predestined thing there is no escape. So submit to Him so that you may be safe, and follow the path of the ascetic scholars. And purify the heart from distractions with seriousness and standing in the early mornings, and constant thought and remembrance, avoiding all sins, being watchful of Allah in all states, so that you may ascend to the peaks of perfection. And say in humility: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter, and do not deprive me of Your most splendid secret that removes blindness. And conclude with good, O Most Merciful of the merciful. Commentary
This is an enumeration of the articles of faith (īmān) and a concluding exhortation. The poet lists what must be believed: the Reckoning (ḥisāb), Gathering (ḥashr), Punishment (ʿiqāb), Reward (thawāb), Scattering (nashr), Path (ṣirāṭ), Balance (mīzān), Pond (ḥawḍ), Fire (nīrān), Gardens (jinān), Jinn, Angels, Prophets, Huris, Youth (wildān), and Saints (awliyā). Key Terms
كلمة الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the shahada is just a formula without deeper meaning.
Correction: The poem shows that it encompasses all rulings.

Checkpoint
According to the poem, where are all the rulings enclosed?
A) In the Quran
B) In the word of Islam
C) In the Sunnah
D) In the intellect

Key Takeaway
The shahada encompasses all Islamic rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every Islamic ruling is contained in your declaration of faith? If so, how does that change your approach to learning and practicing Islam?
?
When you say the shahada daily, do you feel the weight of all the rulings it contains? What is missing from your life that should be there?
?
The poet says the shahada encloses all rulings. Are there any rulings you have neglected because you think they are separate from your faith? Write down one such ruling and commit to acting on it.

Unseen Matters
beginner
6 min
Spiritual Conduct: Fear, Hope, Repentance, and Submission
The poem gives practical spiritual advice on dhikr, fear, hope, repentance, and submission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the balanced spiritual conduct recommended by the poem: fear, hope, repentance, gratitude, patience, and submission to divine decree.

Core Idea
Balance fear and hope, repent, be grateful and patient, submit to Allah's decree.

Moving from beliefs to practice, the poet advises on inner states and actions that lead to spiritual elevation. These include making fear prevail over hope, renewing repentance, being grateful and patient, and submitting to predestination.

Guided Path
1
Read the advice
Read the lines from 'fa-akthir min dhikriha' through 'wa-ttabiʿ sabīl al-nāsikīn al-ʿulamā'. Identify the sequence of advice.
2
Identify key themes
Note the concepts: dhikr, khawf, rajāʾ, tawba, shukr, ṣabr, qaḍāʾ wa qadar, taslīm.
Each verse addresses a different virtue.
3
Reflect on balance
Consider why the poet emphasizes fear over hope, and how gratitude and patience complement each other.
This is a practical guide for the spiritual seeker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَلْزَمُ الإِيْمَانُ بِالحِسَابِ وَالحَشْرِ وَالعِقَابِ وَالثَّوَابِ وَالنَّشْرِ وَالصِّرَاطِ وَالمِيزَانِ وَالحَوْضِ وَالنِّيرَانِ وَالجِنَانِ وَالجِنِّ وَالأَمْلاَكِ ثُمَّ الأَنْبِيَا وَالحُوْرِ وَالوِلْدَانِ ثُمَّ الأَوْلِيَا وَبِكُلِّ مَا جَاءَ عَنِ البَشِيْرِ مِنْ كُلِّ حُكْمِ صَارَ كَالضَّرُوْرِي وَيَنْطَوِي فِي كِلْمَةِ الإِسْلَامِ مَا قَدْ مَضَى مِنْ سَائِرِ الأَحْكَامِ فَأَكْثِرَنْ مِنْ ذِكْرِهَا بِالأَدَبِ تَرْقَى بِهَذَا الذِّكْرِ أَعْلَى الرُّتَبِ وَغَلِّبِ الخَوْفَ عَلَى الرَّجَاءِ وَسِرْ لِمَوْلاَكَ بِلاَ تَنَاءِ وَجَدِّدِ التَّوْبَةَ لِلأَوْزَارِ لاَ تَيْأَسَنْ مِنْ رَحْمَةِ الغَفَّارِ وَكُنْ عَلَى آلائِهِ شَكُوْرًا وَكُنْ عَلَى بَلاَئِهِ صَبُوْرًا فَكُلُّ أَمْرٍ بِالقَضَاءِ وَالقَدَرْ وَكُلُّ مَقْدُوْرٍ فَمَا عَنْهُ مَفَرْ فَكُنْ لَهُ مُسَلِّمًا كَيْ تَسْلَمَا وَاتْبَعْ سَبِيْلَ النَّاسِكِيْنَ العُلَمَا وَخَلِّصِ القَلْبَ مِنَ الأَغْيَارِ بِالجِدِّ وَالقِيَامِ فِي الأَسْحَارِ وَالفِكْرِ وَالذِّكْرِ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ مُجْتَنِبًا لِسَائِرِ الآثَامِ مُرَاقِبًا لِلَّهِ فِي الأَحْوَالِ لِتَرْتَقِي مَعَالِمَ الكَمَالِ وَقُلْ بِذُلِّ رَبِّ لاَ تَقْطَعْنِي عَنْكَ بِقَاطِعْ وَلاَ تَحْرِمْنِي مِنْ سِرِّكَ الأَبْهَى المُزِيْلِ لِلْعَمَى وَاخْتُمْ بِخَيْرٍ يَا رَحِيْمَ الرُّحَمَا وَالحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ عَلَى الإِنْمَامِ وَأَفْضَلُ الصَّلاَةِ وَالسَّلاَمِ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ الهَاشِمِيِّ الخَاتِمِ وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ الأَكَارِمِ

Purification and Supplication
The poem gives advice on heart purification and ends with a supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will learn the methods of heart purification and the supplication for divine closeness.

Core Idea
Purify the heart through dhikr, avoid sins, and supplicate for Allah's grace.

The poem concludes with instructions on purifying the heart from distractions through seriousness, early morning prayer, constant remembrance, and avoiding sins, followed by a heartfelt supplication to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the final advice
Read from 'wa khalliṣ al-qalb' to the end of the poem. Notice the list of practices.
2
Identify purification methods
Note the practices: seriousness (jidd), standing in early mornings (qiyām fī al-asḥār), thought (fikr), remembrance (dhikr), avoiding sins, and watchfulness (murāqaba).
These are concrete actions for spiritual development.
3
Reflect on the supplication
Read the dua: 'O Lord, do not cut me off from You...' and understand its meaning.
The secret (sirr) refers to spiritual insight.

And faith is required in the Reckoning, the Gathering, the Punishment, the Reward, the Scattering, the Path, the Balance, the Pond, the Fire, the Gardens, the Jinn, the Angels, then the Prophets, the Huris, the Youth, then the Saints. And in everything that came from the Bringer of Glad Tidings (the Prophet) of every ruling that became like the necessary. And what has passed of all the rulings is enclosed in the word of Islam. So increase in its remembrance with etiquette; by this remembrance you will ascend to the highest ranks. And make fear prevail over hope, and journey to your Lord without separation. And renew repentance for sins, and do not despair of the mercy of the Oft-Forgiving. And be grateful for His blessings, and be patient in His trial. For every matter is by decree and predestination, and from every predestined thing there is no escape. So submit to Him so that you may be safe, and follow the path of the ascetic scholars. And purify the heart from distractions with seriousness and standing in the early mornings, and constant thought and remembrance, avoiding all sins, being watchful of Allah in all states, so that you may ascend to the peaks of perfection. And say in humility: O Lord, do not cut me off from You by any cutter, and do not deprive me of Your most splendid secret that removes blindness. And conclude with good, O Most Merciful of the merciful. And praise be to Allah for completion, and the best of prayers and peace be upon the Prophet, the Hashimi, the Seal, and his family and noble companions.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This is an enumeration of the articles of faith (īmān) and a concluding exhortation. The poet lists what must be believed: the Reckoning (ḥisāb), Gathering (ḥashr), Punishment (ʿiqāb), Reward (thawāb), Scattering (nashr), Path (ṣirāṭ), Balance (mīzān), Pond (ḥawḍ), Fire (nīrān), Gardens (jinān), Jinn, Angels, Prophets, Huris, Youth (wildān), and Saints (awliyā). Then he says that all these rulings are enclosed (yanṭawī) in the word of Islam (kalimat al-islām), i.e., the shahada encompasses all. Then he gives practical advice: increase remembrance (dhikr) with etiquette, make fear (khawf) prevail over hope (rajāʾ), renew repentance (tawba), be grateful (shakūr) and patient (ṣabūr), acknowledge that all is by predestination (qaḍāʾ wa qadar), submit (musallim), follow ascetic scholars, purify the heart, engage in dhikr, and avoid sins. The poem ends with a supplication and blessings on the Prophet.

Who is Included in 'Al' for Zakat?
The commentator reports the Maliki and Shafi'i views on 'Al' in zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing views of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i on the meaning of 'Al' in the context of zakat and why this distinction matters in Islamic law.

Core Idea
In zakat, 'Al' specifically refers to the Prophet's close relatives, but scholars differed on exactly who that includes.

This passage addresses a specific fiqh issue: who is prohibited from receiving zakat because they belong to the Prophet's household (Ahl al-Bayt). Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i both restrict the prohibition to certain clans, but they disagree on the exact scope. Understanding their positions helps clarify a key ruling in Islamic jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure: first a context statement, then two opinions.
2
Identify the two opinions
Look for Imam Malik's view that 'Al' refers only to Banu Hashim, and Imam al-Shafi'i's view that it includes Banu al-Muttalib as well.
The text says 'only' for Malik, 'and al-Muttalib' for Shafi'i.
3
Understand the context
The commentator explains that 'in the context of zakat' means the situation where giving charity to Ahl al-Bayt is prohibited. This frames the ruling.
Zakat is a specific obligatory charity, distinct from voluntary sadaqah.
4
Reflect on the practical difference
Consider how the disagreement affects who can receive zakat. If a person is from Banu al-Muttalib, Malik's ruling would forbid receiving zakat, while Shafi'i would allow it.
This shows how fiqh rulings have real-world implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في مقام الزَّكاة : فقال الإمام مالك عنه : هم بنو هاشم فقط . وقال الإمام الشافعي صلي الله : بنو هاشم والمطلب . قوله: (وأما في مقام الزَّكاة :أي مقام حرمة الصَّدقة على أهل البيت
And as for in the context of zakat: Imam Malik said concerning him: they are Banu Hashim only. And Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, said: Banu Hashim and al-Muttalib. His saying: (And as for in the context of zakat): i.e., the context of the prohibition of charity upon the people of the household.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a comparative fiqh ruling on the meaning of 'Al' in the context of zakat (obligatory charity). The commentator reports two opinions: Imam Malik holds that 'Al' in this context refers exclusively to Banu Hashim (the Prophet's clan), while Imam al-Shafi'i expands it to include Banu al-Muttalib as well. The explanation clarifies that 'مقام الزكاة' refers to the situation where it is forbidden to give zakat to the Prophet's household, so determining who is included is crucial.

Correction: In the context of zakat, 'Al' does not refer to all followers or supporters, but specifically to the Prophet's close blood relatives as defined by the scholars.

The Saved Status of Ahl al-Fatrah
Clarifies the ruling on ahl al-fatrah and their exemption from obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that ahl al-fatrah (people who never received any prophetic message) are not obligated to believe and are saved from punishment in the afterlife.

Core Idea
Those unreached by revelation are not punished; Allah's justice demands a messenger.

This lesson addresses a key theological question: what happens to people who never encountered any prophetic call? The author clarifies that according to the Qur'an, such individuals are not held accountable. This principle has profound implications for understanding divine justice and the scope of human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the author's core point.
2
Identify the condition
Note the phrase 'the one whom the call reached' and its implication.
Those not reached are not obligated.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider the saved status of ahl al-fatrah and the supporting verse.
This confirms divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم أهل الفترة الذي بلغته الدعوة.
إن قلت : إنَّ ردَّة الصَّبي وإسلامه معتبران عند المالكية، فما معنى اشتراط البلوغ؟
أجيب : بأنَّ اعتبار ردّته وإسلامه بالنظر لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية عليه؛ كتغسيله وتكفينه، والصَّلاة عليه وإرثه، ونحو ذلك .
قوله : (الَّذي بلغته الدَّعوة) : أي : وأما من لم تبلغه الدعوة؛ فليس مكلفاً، ويؤخذ منه أنَّ أهل الفترة ناجون ولو غيّروا وبدلوا؛ لقوله تعالى : وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولاً) (١) .
(۲)
وما ورد من تعذيب بعض أهل الفترة؛ كحاتم الطائي (٢) وامرئ القيس (۳)، فإما رواية آحاد ؛ وهي لا تعارض الدليل القطعي، وعلى تسليم ليس رواية آحاد ، فتعذيبهم لحكمة يعلمها الله تعالى .
ومن جملة أهل الفترة أبواه على أنه ورد إحياء أبويه وإيمانهما به ، كما قال الحافظ الدمشقي (٤):
[من الوافر]
حباك الله النبي مزيد فضل على فضل وكان به رؤوفا
فأحيا أمه وكذا أباه لإيمان به فضلا منيفا
فسلم فـالـقـديـم بـذا قدير وإن كان الحديث به ضعيفا
(١) سورة الإسراء: (١٥)
(٢) وهو ما أخرجه الإمام أحمد في مسنده (۲٥۸/٤) عن عدي بن حاتم قال: قلت يا رسول الله؛ إن أبي يصل الرحم ويفعل كذا كذا، قال: «إن أباك أراد أمراً فأدركه» يعني الذكر.
(٣) وهو ما أخرجه الإمام أحمد في مسنده (۲۲۸/٤) عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: امرؤ القيس لواء الشعراء إلى النار.
(٤) مورد الصادي في مولد الهادي (ص ٦٨)، والحافظ الدمشقي هو: العلامة المحدث الحافظ شمس الدين محمد بن عبد الله القيسي الدمشقي الشافعي المعروف بابن ناصر الدين، ولي مشيخة دار الحديث الأشرفية، ودرس وأفتى وتصدى لنشر الحديث الشريف، له من المصنفات: افتتاح القاري لصحيح البخاري، وعقود الدرر في علوم الأثر، ومورد الصادي، وجامع الآثار في مولد المختار، وغيرها من المصنفات، توفي رحمه الله سنة (٨٤٢هـ). ينظر الضوء اللامع (۱۰۲/۸).
Ruling of the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) - the one whom the call reached. If you say: Surely the apostasy of the child and his Islam are considered according to the Malikis, so what is the meaning of stipulating puberty? Answer: Because consideration of his apostasy and Islam is with regard to applying worldly rulings upon him; like washing him, shrouding him, praying over him, inheriting from him, and the like. His statement: (the one whom the call reached): meaning: And as for the one whom the call did not reach, he is not obligated, and from this it is taken that the people of the interval are saved even if they changed and altered, due to His statement, the Most High: 'And We never punish until We send a Messenger' (17:15). And what has been reported of punishment of some of the people of the interval, like Hatim al-Ta'i and Imru' al-Qais, then it is either an isolated report (riwayat ahad), and it does not contradict the definitive proof; and if it is conceded that it is not an isolated report, then their punishment is for a wisdom known to Allah, the Most High. And among the people of the interval are his (the Prophet's) parents, since it has been reported that his parents were revived and believed in him, as al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi said: [From al-Wafir meter] Allah gifted you, O Prophet, with increasing favor over favor, and He was compassionate to you. So He revived his mother and likewise his father for faith in him, a lofty favor. So submit, for the Eternal is able to do that, even if the hadith is weak. (1) Surah al-Isra: 15 (2) It is what Imam Ahmad narrated in his Musnad (4/258) from 'Adi ibn Hatim who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, my father maintains ties of kinship and does such and such. He said: 'Your father intended a matter and attained it' meaning the dhikr. (3) It is what Imam Ahmad narrated in his Musnad (4/228) from Abu Hurayrah who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Imru' al-Qais is the leader of the poets to the Fire. (4) Mawrid al-Sadi fi Mawlid al-Hadi (p. 68). And al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi is: the 'Allamah, the Muhaddith, the Hafiz Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi al-Dimashqi al-Shafi'i, known as Ibn Nasir al-Din. He was in charge of the teaching position of Dar al-Hadith al-Ashrafiyya, and he taught, issued fatwas, and dedicated himself to spreading the noble hadith. He authored: Iftitah al-Qari li Sahih al-Bukhari, 'Uqud al-Durar fi 'Ulum al-Athar, Mawrid al-Sadi, Jami' al-Athar fi Mawlid al-Mukhtar, and other works. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 842 AH. See al-Daw' al-Lami' (8/102).
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and argument about the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah). It begins by stating the phrase 'the one whom the call reached' which is part of the matn. The commentator clarifies that this implies that those who did not receive the call are not obligated (mukallaf). From this, it follows that ahl al-fatrah are saved (najun) even if they changed or altered, because God only punishes after sending a messenger (citing 17:15). The passage then addresses an objection: Malikis consider the apostasy and Islam of a child valid in worldly rulings (like washing, shrouding, praying, inheritance) even though the child is not yet obligated. The answer is that those rulings are merely worldly (dunyawiyya), not moral accountability. Next, the passage addresses narrations that some ahl al-fatrah were punished, such as Hatim al-Ta'i and Imru' al-Qais. It responds that these are isolated narrations (riwayat ahad) which do not contradict the definitive Qur'anic proof; even if accepted, their punishment is for a wisdom known only to Allah. Finally, the passage mentions that the Prophet's parents are among ahl al-fatrah, and it is reported that they were revived and believed. It quotes a poem by al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi in this regard. The poem argues that Allah revived the Prophet's mother and father for faith, even if the hadith about it is weak, because the Eternal is able. The footnote then provides the biography of al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi and references.

Key Terms
أهل الفترة
التكليف
القطع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahl al-fatrah are automatically punished because they did not follow any religion.
Correction: The passage clarifies they are saved by default because they were not obligated, based on the Qur'anic principle that punishment only occurs after a messenger is sent.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether a person is obligated to follow a religion?
A) Location
B) Whether the call reached them
C) Their innate disposition
D) Their age

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-fatrah are not punished because Allah does not punish without sending a messenger; their salvation is a direct consequence of divine justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have received the message of Islam clearly. Are you living with the same sense of urgency and gratitude as someone who knows they are not ahl al-fatrah? What specific step will you take today to act on the knowledge you have been given?
?
The lesson shows that Allah's justice prevents punishment without a messenger. How does this deepen your trust in Allah's fairness when you see people who have not been guided? Will you commit to not judging them, but instead making du'a for their guidance?
?
If you were among ahl al-fatrah, you would be saved by default. But you are not. Does the weight of your responsibility move you to change anything about your worship or character? Write down one change you will make this week because you have no excuse.

Child Apostasy and Worldly Rulings
Addresses the objection about child apostasy and explains the Maliki view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Malikis consider a child's apostasy and Islam valid for worldly rulings despite the child not being morally obligated.

Core Idea
Worldly rulings (like inheritance) differ from moral accountability; a child's actions can have legal consequences.

This lesson examines an objection raised against the previous principle: if those not reached by the call are not obligated, then what about children who apostatize? The Malikis treat a child's apostasy as valid for worldly matters. The author explains the distinction between worldly legal effects and moral responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the hypothetical objection about child apostasy.
2
Analyze the answer
Note the distinction between worldly rulings and moral obligation.
Worldly rulings include washing, shrouding, etc.
3
Apply the distinction
Reflect on how this maintains the principle that only those reached by call are obligated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم أهل الفترة الذي بلغته الدعوة.
إن قلت : إنَّ ردَّة الصَّبي وإسلامه معتبران عند المالكية، فما معنى اشتراط البلوغ؟
أجيب : بأنَّ اعتبار ردّته وإسلامه بالنظر لإجراء الأحكام الدنيوية عليه؛ كتغسيله وتكفينه، والصَّلاة عليه وإرثه، ونحو ذلك .
قوله : (الَّذي بلغته الدَّعوة) : أي : وأما من لم تبلغه الدعوة؛ فليس مكلفاً، ويؤخذ منه أنَّ أهل الفترة ناجون ولو غيّروا وبدلوا؛ لقوله تعالى : وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولاً) (١) .
(۲)
وما ورد من تعذيب بعض أهل الفترة؛ كحاتم الطائي (٢) وامرئ القيس (۳)، فإما رواية آحاد ؛ وهي لا تعارض الدليل القطعي، وعلى تسليم ليس رواية آحاد ، فتعذيبهم لحكمة يعلمها الله تعالى .
ومن جملة أهل الفترة أبواه على أنه ورد إحياء أبويه وإيمانهما به ، كما قال الحافظ الدمشقي (٤):
[من الوافر]
حباك الله النبي مزيد فضل على فضل وكان به رؤوفا
فأحيا أمه وكذا أباه لإيمان به فضلا منيفا
فسلم فـالـقـديـم بـذا قدير وإن كان الحديث به ضعيفا
(١) سورة الإسراء: (١٥)
(٢) وهو ما أخرجه الإمام أحمد في مسنده (۲٥۸/٤) عن عدي بن حاتم قال: قلت يا رسول الله؛ إن أبي يصل الرحم ويفعل كذا كذا، قال: «إن أباك أراد أمراً فأدركه» يعني الذكر.
(٣) وهو ما أخرجه الإمام أحمد في مسنده (۲۲۸/٤) عن أبي هريرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: امرؤ القيس لواء الشعراء إلى النار.
(٤) مورد الصادي في مولد الهادي (ص ٦٨)، والحافظ الدمشقي هو: العلامة المحدث الحافظ شمس الدين محمد بن عبد الله القيسي الدمشقي الشافعي المعروف بابن ناصر الدين، ولي مشيخة دار الحديث الأشرفية، ودرس وأفتى وتصدى لنشر الحديث الشريف، له من المصنفات: افتتاح القاري لصحيح البخاري، وعقود الدرر في علوم الأثر، ومورد الصادي، وجامع الآثار في مولد المختار، وغيرها من المصنفات، توفي رحمه الله سنة (٨٤٢هـ). ينظر الضوء اللامع (۱۰۲/۸).
Ruling of the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) - the one whom the call reached. If you say: Surely the apostasy of the child and his Islam are considered according to the Malikis, so what is the meaning of stipulating puberty? Answer: Because consideration of his apostasy and Islam is with regard to applying worldly rulings upon him; like washing him, shrouding him, praying over him, inheriting from him, and the like. His statement: (the one whom the call reached): meaning: And as for the one whom the call did not reach, he is not obligated, and from this it is taken that the people of the interval are saved even if they changed and altered, due to His statement, the Most High: 'And We never punish until We send a Messenger' (17:15). And what has been reported of punishment of some of the people of the interval, like Hatim al-Ta'i and Imru' al-Qais, then it is either an isolated report (riwayat ahad), and it does not contradict the definitive proof; and if it is conceded that it is not an isolated report, then their punishment is for a wisdom known to Allah, the Most High. And among the people of the interval are his (the Prophet's) parents, since it has been reported that his parents were revived and believed in him, as al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi said: [From al-Wafir meter] Allah gifted you, O Prophet, with increasing favor over favor, and He was compassionate to you. So He revived his mother and likewise his father for faith in him, a lofty favor. So submit, for the Eternal is able to do that, even if the hadith is weak. (1) Surah al-Isra: 15 (2) It is what Imam Ahmad narrated in his Musnad (4/258) from 'Adi ibn Hatim who said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, my father maintains ties of kinship and does such and such. He said: 'Your father intended a matter and attained it' meaning the dhikr. (3) It is what Imam Ahmad narrated in his Musnad (4/228) from Abu Hurayrah who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: Imru' al-Qais is the leader of the poets to the Fire. (4) Mawrid al-Sadi fi Mawlid al-Hadi (p. 68). And al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi is: the 'Allamah, the Muhaddith, the Hafiz Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Qaysi al-Dimashqi al-Shafi'i, known as Ibn Nasir al-Din. He was in charge of the teaching position of Dar al-Hadith al-Ashrafiyya, and he taught, issued fatwas, and dedicated himself to spreading the noble hadith. He authored: Iftitah al-Qari li Sahih al-Bukhari, 'Uqud al-Durar fi 'Ulum al-Athar, Mawrid al-Sadi, Jami' al-Athar fi Mawlid al-Mukhtar, and other works. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 842 AH. See al-Daw' al-Lami' (8/102).
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and argument about the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah). It begins by stating the phrase 'the one whom the call reached' which is part of the matn. The commentator clarifies that this implies that those who did not receive the call are not obligated (mukallaf). From this, it follows that ahl al-fatrah are saved (najun) even if they changed or altered, because God only punishes after sending a messenger (citing 17:15). The passage then addresses an objection: Malikis consider the apostasy and Islam of a child valid in worldly rulings (like washing, shrouding, praying, inheritance) even though the child is not yet obligated. The answer is that those rulings are merely worldly (dunyawiyya), not moral accountability. Next, the passage addresses narrations that some ahl al-fatrah were punished, such as Hatim al-Ta'i and Imru' al-Qais. It responds that these are isolated narrations (riwayat ahad) which do not contradict the definitive Qur'anic proof; even if accepted, their punishment is for a wisdom known only to Allah. Finally, the passage mentions that the Prophet's parents are among ahl al-fatrah, and it is reported that they were revived and believed. It quotes a poem by al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi in this regard. The poem argues that Allah revived the Prophet's mother and father for faith, even if the hadith about it is weak, because the Eternal is able. The footnote then provides the biography of al-Hafiz al-Dimashqi and references.

Key Terms
ردة
إسلام
البلوغ
أحكام دنيوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a child's apostasy is valid, it means the child is morally accountable.
Correction: The validity is only for worldly legal effects, not for moral obligation or punishment in the afterlife.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do Malikis consider a child's apostasy valid?
A) Because the child is fully responsible
B) For applying worldly rulings only
C) Because puberty is not required
D) Because of the child's free will

Key Takeaway
Child apostasy is valid for worldly legal rulings like inheritance and funeral rites, but does not entail moral accountability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat people's mistakes differently based on their age or understanding? Think of a recent instance where you judged someone harshly without considering their level of accountability. How does this lesson challenge you to separate worldly consequences from spiritual judgment?
?
The child's apostasy has worldly effects but no afterlife blame. Are there areas in your own life where you confuse external religious performance with inner faith? Commit to one concrete change in how you evaluate yourself or others.
?
If you were responsible for a child or new Muslim who made a serious error, how would you apply the principle of 'worldly rulings only'? Write down a specific action you would take that reflects this distinction.

Addressing Reports and the Prophet's Parents
Addresses narrations of punishment and the status of the Prophet's parents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how isolated narrations about punishment of ahl al-fatrah are reconciled with the definitive Qur'anic principle, and that the Prophet's parents are considered among the saved ahl al-fatrah.

Core Idea
Weak or isolated reports cannot override the clear Qur'an; the Prophet's parents are saved.

This lesson tackles two related issues. First, how to respond to narrations that some ahl al-fatrah (like Hatim al-Ta'i and Imru' al-Qais) were punished? Second, what about the Prophet's own parents? The author uses the principle that isolated reports (riwayat ahad) do not contradict definitive proofs (qat'i), and then mentions a report that the Prophet's parents were revived and believed, though the hadith is weak.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read both parts concerning reports and the Prophet's parents.
2
Understand the response to reports
Note the two approaches: they are ahad reports or punishment for a hidden wisdom.
3
Consider the Prophet's parents
Read the poem and note the weak hadith but the principle that Allah is able.
4
Synthesize
See how both points reinforce the saved status of ahl al-fatrah.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's parents were polytheists and will be punished.

Checkpoint
How does the passage reconcile reports of punishment of some ahl al-fatrah with the Qur'anic verse?
A) By denying the reports entirely
B) By saying they are isolated reports that do not contradict the definitive proof
C) By claiming those people were not actually from ahl al-fatrah
D) By saying the reports are fabricated

Key Takeaway
Isolated reports cannot override definitive Qur'anic proofs, and the Prophet's parents are saved as ahl al-fatrah according to a report, even if weak.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear reports about someone's fate that contradict Allah's mercy, do you weigh them against the clear Qur'an? Are there weak narrations you have accepted too readily that made you doubt Allah's mercy? Will you commit to prioritizing definitive proofs over weak ones?
?
The Prophet's parents were saved despite living in an interval. Do you assume about people's salvation based on hearsay? Are there people you have written off due to weak reports? How will you change your judgment?
?
This lesson shows that even weak hadith can be used for hope. Are there aspects of your faith where you rely only on fear-based narrations? Will you seek out the definitive proofs of hope and mercy?

Unseen Matters
beginner

Sensory Experience in Paradise
Al-Khawwas explains the difference in constitution and sensory perception in Paradise, citing Ibn al-Farid's poem.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the sensory experiences in Paradise are real but fundamentally different from worldly experiences, as articulated by Ali al-Khawwas and Ibn al-Farid.

Core Idea
In Paradise, every sense perceives in a way beyond all worldly imagination.

This passage draws on the testimony of two great spiritual masters to illustrate a profound truth about the afterlife. Ali al-Khawwas explains that the very nature of the inhabitants of Paradise is different from ours, and that this difference extends to every mode of perception. Ibn al-Farid's poetry gives us a glimpse of this all-encompassing sensory reality.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Khawwas's statement
Read the passage from 'Ali al-Khawwas carefully. Notice how he states that the constitution (nash'a) of the people of Paradise differs from worldly beings in both form and meaning. He cites the hadith to support this.
The hadith emphasizes that Paradise contains what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and no heart has conceived.
2
Understand the application to senses
Al-Khawwas then applies this difference to each sense: seeing, eating, smelling, speaking, and perceiving. Reflect on what it means for each sense to operate 'in that way'—i.e., in a manner beyond worldly experience.
3
Explore Ibn al-Farid's poem
Read the verses from Ibn al-Farid's Ta'iyya. Notice how he describes perception by every atom, every sense, and every part of the lover's being. This poetic depiction illustrates the integrated and intensified sensory experience of Paradise.
The beloved in the poem can be understood as representing the divine or paradisial reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ سَيِّدِي عَلِيٌّ الْخَوَّاصُ: نَشْأَةُ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ مُخَالِفَةٌ لِنَشْأَةِ أَهْلِ الدُّنْيَا الَّتِي نَحْنُ عَلَيْهِ صُورَةً وَمَعْنًى، كَمَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ حَدِيثُ: «إِنَّ فِي الْجَنَّةِ مَا لَا عَيْنٌ رَأَتْ وَلَا أُذُنٌ سَمِعَتْ، وَلَا خَطَرَ عَلَى قَلْبِ بَشَرٍ». فَيُبْصِرُ الْإِنْسَانُ كَذَلِكَ، وَيَأْكُلُ كَذَلِكَ، وَيَشَمُّ كَذَلِكَ، وَيَنْطِقُ كَذَلِكَ، وَيُدْرِكُ كَذَلِكَ. وَهَذَا الْقَدْرُ الْقَلِيلُ مِنْ أَحْوَالِ الْجَنَّةِ يَبْعُدُهُ عَقْلُ مَنْ يَسْمَعُ ذَلِكَ، فَكَيْفَ بِغَيْرِ الْقَلِيلِ مِمَّا هُوَ أَعْظَمُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ؟ قَالَ: وَلَمْ أَرَ أَحَدًا تَكَلَّمَ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْتُهُ غَيْرَ سَيِّدِي عُمَرَ ابْنِ الْفَارِضِ فِي تَائِيَّتِهِ. أَيْ حَيْثُ قَالَ: [مِنَ الطَّوِيلِ] يُشَاهِدُ مِنِّي حُسْنَهَا كُلُّ ذَرَّةٍ بِهَا كُلُّ طَرْفٍ جَالٍ فِي كُلِّ طَرْفَةِ وَيُثْنِي عَلَيْهَا فِي كُلِّ لَطِيفَةٍ بِكُلِّ لِسَانٍ جَالٍ فِي كُلِّ لَفْظَةِ وَأَنْشَقُ رَيَّاهَا بِكُلِّ رَقِيقَةٍ بِهَا كُلُّ أَنْفٍ نَاشِقٍ كُلَّ هَبَّةِ وَيَسْمَعُ مِنِّي لَفْظَهَا كُلُّ بَضْعَةٍ بِهَا كُلُّ سَمْعٍ سَامِعٍ مُتَنَصِّتِ وَيَلْثُمُ مِنِّي كُلَّ جُزْءٍ لِثَامَهَا بِكُلِّ فَمٍ فِي لَثْمِهِ كُلَّ قُبْلَةِ
And Sayyidi ‘Ali al-Khawwas said: The constitution of the people of Paradise is different from the constitution of the people of this world, which we are upon, in form and meaning, as indicated by the hadith: 'In Paradise there is what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to a human heart.' So a person sees in that way, and eats in that way, and smells in that way, and speaks in that way, and perceives in that way. And this small amount of the states of Paradise is far from the intellect of one who hears it; so how about other than the small amount, which is greater than that? He said: I have not seen anyone speak about what I have mentioned except my master ‘Umar ibn al-Farid in his Ta'iyya. That is, where he said: [from the poetical metre tawil] Every atom of me witnesses her beauty, with every eye that glances in every blink. And every subtlety praises her, with every tongue that roves in every utterance. And I sniff her fragrance with every delicate thing, with every nose sniffing every breeze. And every part of me hears her speech, with every ear listening attentively. And every part of me kisses her veil, with every mouth kissing in every kiss.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of sensory perception in Paradise as radically different from worldly experience. ‘Ali al-Khawwas states that the very constitution (nash'a) of the people of Paradise differs in both form (sura) and meaning (ma'na) from worldly beings, citing the well-known hadith that Paradise contains what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and no heart has conceived. Consequently, every sense—sight, taste, smell, hearing, touch—operates in a manner beyond worldly comprehension. The author remarks that even this small glimpse of Paradise is beyond the intellect of hearers, implying that the full reality is even more unimaginable. Then he notes that only ‘Umar ibn al-Farid in his famous Ta'iyya poem has articulated this concept. The poem describes a beloved (often interpreted as divine or paradisal) whose beauty, fragrance, voice, and kiss are perceived by every part of the lover's being, with every atom, every sense, participating in the perception. This illustrates the integration and intensification of sensory experience in the afterlife, where perception is not limited to specific organs but is all-encompassing. The passage thus defends the orthodox Sunni position that the pleasures of Paradise are real and sensory, albeit utterly transcendent and incommensurable with worldly experience.

Key Terms
نشأة
أهل الجنة
تائية ابن الفارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Descriptions of Paradise are merely metaphorical, or its senses are identical to worldly senses.
Correction: The passage affirms that the sensory experiences in Paradise are real but fundamentally different in form and meaning, as indicated by the hadith and the poem.

Checkpoint
According to ‘Ali al-Khawwas, how does the constitution (nash'a) of the people of Paradise relate to that of worldly people?
A) It is the same in form but different in meaning
B) It differs in both form and meaning
C) It is the same but intensified
D) It is purely spiritual without physical senses

Key Takeaway
The sensory pleasures of Paradise are real, but utterly beyond worldly experience; every part of the blessed being will perceive with intensified and integrated senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every part of your being will perceive Paradise in a way that your current senses cannot conceive, which of your worldly attachments are you clinging to that will be obsolete there? What would it mean to let go now?
?
The poem describes every atom perceiving the beloved's beauty. If your entire being is to be engaged in that perception, what part of you is currently not oriented towards Allah? How will you align all your senses now?
?
Al-Khawwas says even this small glimpse is beyond the intellect. Are you satisfied with intellectual understanding alone, or do you yearn for a direct taste? What would change if you truly believed that Paradise is beyond all imagination?

The Perfection of Sensory Perception in Paradise
The commentator extols the extraordinary hearing and sight of the people of paradise, citing a hadith and poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the senses of the people of Paradise are perfected beyond worldly limitations, as illustrated by hadith and poetry.

Core Idea
Paradise grants sensory perfection beyond worldly imagination.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary explores the extraordinary sensory abilities of Paradise's inhabitants. It begins with a striking example of hearing at ten farsakhs, then explains the fundamental difference between earthly and paradisal existence, supported by a famous hadith and a poetic depiction. The material shows that in Paradise, every sense operates at an unimaginable level of perfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the example
Read the Arabic and translation, paying attention to the example of hearing the ant from ten farsakhs. This sets the stage for the extraordinary nature of Paradise.
This is a concrete illustration of sensory perfection.
2
Understand the principle of different constitution
Ali al-Khawwas explains that the constitution (nash'a) of the people of Paradise is entirely different from ours, both in form and meaning. This is the key principle.
The hadith 'what no eye has seen' supports this.
3
Identify the five sensory activities
The passage lists: sees, eats, smells, speaks, perceives. Notice that these cover all major senses and beyond.
Eating implies taste, and perception is holistic.
4
Reflect on the poetic illustration
Ibn al-Farid's poem uses lover imagery to show how every part of the being perceives every aspect of the beloved, symbolizing Paradise.
This emphasizes the integration of all senses.
5
Ask: why does this matter?
This lesson deepens our longing for Paradise and affirms that its pleasures are beyond comprehension, motivating faith and good deeds.
It also corrects the misconception that Paradise is just like this world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسمع دبيب النملة السوداء في الليلة الظلماء من مسيرة عشرة فراسخ . وقال سيدي علي الخواص : نشأة أهل الجنَّة مخالفة لنشأة أهل الدُّنيا التي نحن عليه صورة ومعنى كما أشار إليه حديث: «إنَّ في الجنَّة ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت، ولا خطر على قلب بشر»(۱)، فيبصر الإنسان كذلك، ويأكل كذلك، ويشم كذلك، وينطق كذلك، ويدرك كذلك، وهذا القدر القليل من أحوال الجنَّة يبعده عقل من يسمع ذلك، فكيف بغير القليل مما هو أعظم من ذلك؟ أعظم من في الجنَّة بسائر جسده، ويسمع قال : ولم أر أحداً تكلّم على ما ذكرته غير سيدي عمر ابن الفارض في تائيته) انتهى ملخصاً من الشحيمي على الشَّيخ عبد السَّلام) (۲) . أي : حيث قال (۳) : من الطويل] يشاهد مني حسنها كل ذرَّةٍ بها كلُّ طرف جال في كل طرفةِ ويثني عليها في كل لطيفة بكل لسان جال في كل لفظةِ وأنشق رياها بكل رقيقة بها كـل أنـف نـاشـق كـل هـبـة ويسمع منّي لفظها كل بضعة بها كل سمع سامع مـتـنـصـتِ ويلثم مني كل جزء لثامها بكل فم في لثمه كل قبلة (1) أخرجه البخاري (٣٢٤٤) ، ومسلم (۲/۲۸۲٤ ، والإمام أحمد في مسنده» (٢) ٤٦١) عن أبي هريرة الله (۲) حاشية السحيمي (ق ٢/ ٢١٦). (۳) ديوان ابن الفارض (ص۸۲).
He hears the crawling of the black ant on a dark night from a distance of ten farsakhs. And Sayyidi Ali al-Khawwas said: The constitution of the people of Paradise is different from the constitution of the people of this world which we have, in form and meaning, as indicated by the hadith: 'In Paradise there is what no eye has seen, nor ear heard, nor has it occurred to the human heart.' Thus a person sees similarly, eats similarly, smells similarly, speaks similarly, and perceives similarly. This small amount of the states of Paradise astounds the intellect of whoever hears it, so how about what is beyond this small amount which is greater than that? Greater than that in Paradise with his entire body, and he hears. He said: 'I have not seen anyone discuss what I mentioned except my master Umar ibn al-Farid in his Ta'iyyah.' End, summarized from al-Shihimi's commentary on Shaykh Abd al-Salam. That is, where he said [from the long meter]: Each atom of me witnesses her beauty, with every eye gazing in every blink. And praises her in every subtlety, with every tongue speaking in every word. And I inhale her fragrance with every delicate breeze, with every nose inhaling every gust. And my every part hears her words, with every ear listening attentively. And my every part kisses her veil, with every mouth in its kissing, every kiss. (1) Narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and Ahmad from Abu Hurayra. (2) Hashiyat al-Suhaymi. (3) Diwan Ibn al-Farid.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage describes the extraordinary sensory capabilities of the people of Paradise. It begins with the statement that a person in Paradise can hear the crawling of a black ant on a dark night from ten farsakhs away, illustrating perfect hearing. It then quotes Ali al-Khawwas, who explains that the constitution of Paradise's inhabitants differs entirely from that of this world, both in form and meaning, as supported by the hadith about unseen delights. Consequently, all senses—sight, taste, smell, speech, and perception—are elevated. The commentator marvels that this small glimpse of Paradise confounds the intellect, so what of greater wonders? He notes that only Umar ibn al-Farid has eloquently addressed this in his poem, which he then quotes. The poem uses a lover's imagery to depict how every part of the beloved (symbolizing Paradise) is perceived by every sense of the lover (the blessed person), emphasizing the complete and perfect integration of sensory experience. This serves to illustrate the transcendence of Paradise over worldly limitations.

Refuting the Denial of Bodily Resurrection
Al-Sawi refutes the philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection and how al-Sawi refutes their arguments by comparing them to a mirage.

Core Idea
The philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection is built on mirage-like sophistries.

Al-Sawi begins by exposing the philosophers' rejection of bodily resurrection. He compares their arguments to a mirage that misleads the thirsty. This lesson explains their claim and the severe warning against being deceived by their false knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Notice the flow: from their claim to the mirage analogy to the outcry 'kalla'. Then read the translation.
The passage uses a vivid simile to highlight the deceitfulness of their arguments.
2
Identify the philosophers' claim
The philosophers deny bodily resurrection. Understand what that means: they believe the world's primary elements are eternal, but individual forms do not return after perishing.
This is explained in the commentary part of the source.
3
Analyze al-Sawi's refutation
Al-Sawi refutes by calling their arguments 'imaginary doubtful sophistries' and comparing them to a mirage. He then says that people were misled into thinking this is knowledge, and even prefer these philosophers over Shari'a scholars. The repetition of 'kalla sawfa ya'lamoon' is a severe threat.
This refutation is not philosophical but rhetorical and based on revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وممَّا بنَوْه على مذهبهم عدم المعاد الجسماني، وقد زخرفوا بشُبَه ظَنِّيَّة خيالية كسراب بقيعة يحسبه الظمآن ماء حتى إذا جاءه لم يجده شيئاً، فضَلُّوا وأضلوا حتى ظنَّ كثير من النَّاس أنَّ هذه الزَّخارف علم، بل فَضَّلوا المتمسكين بها على علماء الشَّريعة، كلا سوف يعلمون، ثمَّ كلا سوف يعلمون . واعلم أنَّ من اشتغل بعلم الفلاسفة قل أن تنجو عقيدته من ظلمة، أقلُّها كثرة التشكيك والوسوسة التي تجره إلى الابتداع أو إلى الكفر والعياذ بالله تعالى فالحذر من الاشتغال بخرافاتهم، على أنَّ المطلوب من العبد إنَّما هو عبادة الله اعتقاداً وعملاً؛ لينجو من النار في الآخرة. قوله : (عدم المعاد الجسماني) أي: فهم يقولون : إنَّ أصول العالم القديمة لا تنعدم وفروعه تنعدم ولا تعود. قوله : (بل) فضَّلوا إضراب عما قبله قصد به الترقي في الرَّدِّ عليهم. قوله : (كلًّا سوف يعلمون كلا ردع وزجر، وفيه تعريض لهم بوعيد التكاثر.
And among what they built upon their doctrine is the denial of bodily resurrection. They have decorated with imaginary, doubtful sophistries like a mirage in a depression which the thirsty man thinks is water until when he comes to it, he finds it nothing. So they went astray and led others astray until many people thought that these decorations are knowledge. Rather, they preferred those who cling to them over the scholars of the Shari'a. No! They will come to know, then no! They will come to know. And know that whoever occupies himself with the science of the philosophers, rarely will his creed be saved from darkness, the least of which is much doubt and whispering that drag him into innovation or into disbelief - God forbid. So beware of occupying yourselves with their myths. Indeed, what is required from the servant is only the worship of God in belief and deed, to be saved from the Fire in the Hereafter. His saying: (denial of bodily resurrection) i.e., they say that the ancient principles of the world do not perish, and their branches perish and do not return. His saying: (Rather they preferred) is a turning away from what preceded, intending progression in refuting them. His saying: (No! They will come to know) is a deterrent and warning, and in it is a threat to them with the threat of al-takathur.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage refutes the philosophers' rejection of bodily resurrection (al-ma'ad al-jismani). Al-Sawi likens their arguments to a mirage that appears as water but is nothing. He states that they have misled many people into thinking their sophistry is knowledge, and even prefer them over scholars of Shari'a. The phrase 'kalla sawfa ya'lamoon' is a severe warning. Then al-Sawi issues a personal warning: anyone who engages in philosophy rarely keeps his creed safe; it leads to doubt, innovation (ibtida'), or even disbelief (kufr). He emphasizes that the purpose of the servant is to worship God through belief and action to escape Hellfire. The passage then provides brief commentary on specific terms: explaining that denial of resurrection means they believe the world's primary elements are eternal while individual forms perish without return. The commentary on 'bal' explains it as a transition for stronger refutation, and on 'kalla' as a deterrent and threat referencing the Quranic surah al-Takathur.

Key Terms
المعاد الجسماني
الفلاسفة
الزخارف
السراب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the philosophers' rejection of bodily resurrection is based on rational proofs that cannot be refuted.
Correction: Al-Sawi shows that their arguments are merely imaginary and deceptive, like a mirage, and are not valid.

Checkpoint
What simile does al-Sawi use to describe the philosophers' arguments?
A) A burning fire
B) A mirage in a depression
C) A sturdy fortress
D) A flowing river

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection is based on deceptive, mirage-like sophistries, and is refuted by a severe Quranic warning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been deceived by an argument that seemed brilliant and logical but later realized it contradicted the clear truths of the Quran and Sunnah? How does this passage call you to reconsider the sources you trust for guidance?
?
The philosophers' 'knowledge' was preferred over the scholars of Shari'a. Is there an area in your life where you seek validation from worldly intellectuals or modern experts more than from religious scholars? What would it take for you to realign your priorities?
?
The mirage promises water but gives nothing. Are there any beliefs or attitudes you hold that promise fulfillment but leave you empty before Allah? Will you examine them today and surrender them to the truth of revelation?

The Dangers of Studying Philosophy
Al-Sawi warns against studying philosophy and emphasizes worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severe warning against studying philosophy and how it endangers one's creed, leading to innovation or disbelief.

Core Idea
Philosophy's doubt and whispering drag the soul into innovation and disbelief.

After refuting the deniers of bodily resurrection, al-Sawi issues a personal warning. He states that engaging with the philosophers' 'science' rarely leaves one's creed untouched; it often leads to doubt and ultimately to innovation or kufr. This lesson explains why philosophy is so dangerous and what the true purpose of the servant is.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning passage
Read the Arabic passage that begins with 'Wa'lam anna man ishtaghala bi'ilm al-falasifah...'. Understand the severity of the tone.
Al-Sawi uses the word 'kalla' to emphasize danger.
2
Trace the progression
Identify the chain: studying philosophy → darkness in creed → doubt and whispering → innovation (ibtida') or disbelief (kufr). Note the phrase 'aqalluha kathrat al-tashkik wa al-waswasah'.
This shows that even if one does not fall into kufr, at least they will experience doubt.
3
Understand the purpose of worship
Al-Sawi contrasts philosophy with the true purpose: worship of Allah in belief and deed to be saved from Hell. This reorients the learner to the ultimate goal.
The warning is not just theoretical but practical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What Makes Divine Speech 'Khabar'? The Role of Actual Addressees
Definition of khabar and dispute over actual addressees.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine speech as khabar (informative statement) and the theological dispute over whether it requires actual addressees to be considered as such.

Core Idea
Divine speech is called khabar regardless of actual addressees, but the status of rulings depends on this.

This passage introduces the concept of divine speech (kalam) when it is used to affirm or negate something about something, known as khabar. A key theological question arises: does divine address require the actual existence of addressees at the moment of speech? This issue has implications for whether God's commands and prohibitions are eternal or temporal. Let's explore the definition and the different positions.

Guided Path
1
Define khabar
Read the definition: speech is called khabar when it affirms or negates something of something.
Notice the term 'khabar' is broader than 'khitab'.
2
Identify the dispute
Look for the question: is the presence of actual addressees required for it to be called khabar or khitab? The passage says there is disagreement (khilaf).
3
Connect to rulings
Understand that this dispute affects whether the ahkam (rulings) are considered temporal or eternal, based on considering future beings as existing in God's knowledge.
This introduces the idea of 'tanjiz' and 'suluh' that will be detailed later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن حيث تعلقه بثبوت أمر لأمر، أو نفيه عنه، يسمى خبراً . وهل يشترط في تسميته بذلك كالخطاب وجود مخاطبين بالفعل أو لا؟ خلاف، وينبني عليه الخلاف في الأحكام، هل هي حادثة أو قديمة باعتبار تنزيل من سيوجد منزلة الموجود اكتفاء بوجود المأمور في علم الآمر . وله تعلقات ثلاثة : - تنجيزي قديم باعتبار دلالته على الواجبات والمستحيلات والجائزات التي سيوجد منها وما لا يوجد. - وصلوحي قديم باعتبار دلالته على الأمر والنهي قبل وجود المخاطبين . - وتنجيزي حادث عند وجودهم. قوله : (وهل يشترط ... إلخ ) : المعتمد أنَّه لا يشترط، وعليه فالأحكام قديمة . قوله : (وتنجيزي حادث عند وجودهم : هذا مبني على أنَّه لا يشترط في الخطاب وجود المخاطبين بالفعل.
And from the perspective of its relation to affirming something for something, or negating it from it, it is called khabar (statement/information). And is it required for its being so called, like khitab (address), that there be actual addressees or not? There is disagreement, and upon it depends the disagreement about the rulings (al-ahkam): whether they are temporal (haditha) or eternal (qadima), based on considering the one who will exist as existing, satisfied with the existence of the commanded thing in the knowledge of the Commander. And it has three relations: - Actual eternal (tanjizi qadim) by virtue of its indication of the necessary (wajibat), impossible (mustahilat), and possible (ja'izat) which will come to exist and those which do not. - Potential eternal (suluhi qadim) by virtue of its indication of command and prohibition before the existence of addressees. - And actual temporal (tanjizi hadith) at the time of their existence. His saying: (And is it required... etc.): The relied-upon view is that it is not required, and accordingly the rulings are eternal. His saying: (And actual temporal at the time of their existence): This is based on the view that addressees actually being present is not required for address.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the relations of divine speech (kalam). It first explains that speech, when considered in terms of affirming or negating something of something, is called khabar (informative statement). The author then raises a theological dispute: whether the term 'khitab' (divine address) requires the actual existence of addressees at the time of speech? This dispute affects the ruling on whether divine commands and prohibitions (al-ahkam) are temporal or eternal. The author notes that some consider those who will exist as if they already exist, relying on God's eternal knowledge. The passage then enumerates three relations (ta'alluqat) of divine speech: (1) an eternal actual relation, referring to its indication of necessary, impossible, and possible things regardless of actual existence; (2) an eternal potential relation, referring to its indication of commands and prohibitions before addressees exist; and (3) a temporal actual relation, occurring when addressees actually exist. After this, the commentary provides the author's preferred view: the relied-upon position is that actual addressees are not required, so the rulings themselves are eternal. The commentator further explains that the third relation (temporal actual) is based on the premise that actual addressees are not required for divine address, which aligns with the preferred opinion. This passage carefully distinguishes the eternal and temporal aspects of divine speech to avoid attributing temporality to God's essence while affirming His interaction with creation.

Key Terms
خبر
خطاب
الأحكام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine speech requires actual addressees to be considered speech.
Correction: The passage indicates that it is not required; the rulings can be eternal regardless of actual addressees.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the dispute about whether rulings are temporal or eternal depends on what?
A) The existence of actual addressees
B) The definition of khabar
C) The three relations of speech
D) The knowledge of the Commander

Key Takeaway
Divine speech as khabar is defined without necessarily requiring actual addressees, affecting the theological status of rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a command in the Quran, do you realize that the rulings are considered eternal in Allah's knowledge, even if no one was present when they were revealed? How does that make you feel about your responsibility to obey them today?
?
If divine speech as 'khabar' does not require immediate listeners, does that change how you view Allah's eternal attributes? What would it mean for your relationship with Him if His speech were dependent on creation?
?
The passage suggests that future addressees are treated as if they exist in Allah's knowledge. Does that change how you read verses that were not directly addressed to you? Will you now read them as if they are speaking to you personally?

The Three Relations of Divine Speech: Eternal and Temporal
Enumeration of three relations of divine speech with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of relations of divine speech (tanjizi qadim, suluhi qadim, tanjizi hadith) and how they reconcile God's eternity with His interaction with creation.

Core Idea
Divine speech has three relations: eternal actual, eternal potential, and temporal actual.

After defining khabar, the passage presents a classification of the relations (ta'alluqat) of divine speech. These relations show how God's eternal speech can relate to created beings both before and after their existence. The commentary clarifies the preferred position regarding the need for actual addressees. Let's examine each relation.

Guided Path
1
List the three relations
Read the enumerated list of three ta'alluqat: tanjizi qadim, suluhi qadim, and tanjizi hadith.
Notice the pattern: two are eternal, one is temporal.
2
Understand 'actual eternal'
This relation concerns God's speech about necessary, impossible, and possible things, regardless of actual existence.
It is called 'tanjizi qadim' because it is actual but eternal.
3
Understand 'potential eternal'
This relates to commands and prohibitions before addressees exist; it is potential but eternal.
4
Understand 'actual temporal'
This occurs when addressees actually exist. Note the commentary: this relation is based on the view that actual addressees are not required for address.
This temporal relation does not imply God's speech itself is temporal.

Source Text

Affirming the Believers' Vision of God in Paradise
Sanusi affirms the beatific vision and explains its nature, location, and recipients.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine of the beatific vision, including its nature as a direct unveiling by sight, its location in Paradise, its universality for all believers, and its transcendence of physical conditions.

Core Idea
The believers will see God in Paradise without modality, limit, or physical conditions.

This passage from al-Kharida affirms the vision of God as a core belief of the Samiyyat. It clarifies that the vision is a literal unveiling by sight, yet entirely different from physical sight: no place, direction, or distance. Understanding this doctrine requires balancing affirmation with divine transcendence. This lesson unpacks the essential points Sanusi makes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic matn once, then the literal translation. Let the author's own words set the foundation.
Notice the parenthetical 'my brother in Islam'—a rhetorical flourish.
2
Identify the key affirmations
The passage affirms the vision's nature (complete unveiling), location (Garden of Eternity), manner (without limit, place, direction, etc.), and recipients (all Paradise dwellers). List them.
Also note the statement about superiority in quantity.
3
Reflect on how this differs from physical sight
Sanusi stresses that the vision occurs without spatial conditions. Contrast this with ordinary sight. Ask yourself: why is it important to deny modality (bilā kayf) here?
This connects to the broader principle of tanzīh (divine transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

واجزم) أي : اقطع واعتقد وجوباً (أخي) في الإسلام، إذ الأب الذي خرجنا بسببه من ظلمة الكفر إلى نور الإيمان واحد، وهو النبي برؤية الإله سبحانه وتعالى بمعنى الانكشاف التّام بالبصر ؛
أي : بوقوعها (في جنّة (الخُلد :أي: الإقامة على سبيل الدوام حال كون الرُّؤية حاصلة بلا) تناهي للمرئي تعالى؛ أي: من غير إحاطة في حدود المرئي ونهاياته ؛ لاستحالة الحدود والنّهايات عليه تعالى . فكما أنَّهم يعلمونه بلا حد ونهاية وبلا كيف يرونه كذلك، فيرى لا مكان ولا في جهة، ولا باتصال شعاع ولا على مسافة بينه تعالى وبين الرَّائي؛ لأنَّ الرُّؤية عندنا بخَلْق الله تعالى في أي محل شاء، وليس بلازم ألا يكون إلا عند اجتماع الشَّرائط كما سيأتي توضيحه. وتقع لكلِّ من دخل الجنَّة؛ من إنس وجن من هذه الأمة وغيرها، حتّى النِّساء والصبيان . وتتفاضل الرُّؤية كماً

وقوله : (كمّاً) : أي : عدداً .
Affirming the believers' vision of their Lord on the Day of Resurrection. And affirm (i.e., cut and believe obligatorily, my brother in Islam, for the father through whom we came out from the darkness of disbelief to the light of faith is one, and he is the Prophet) the vision of the Divine, Exalted and High, in the sense of complete unveiling by sight. i.e., its occurrence in the Garden of Eternity, i.e., residence perpetually, while the vision is occurring without ending for the Seen, Exalted; i.e., without encompassing the limits and ends of the seen, due to the impossibility of limits and ends upon Him, Exalted. So just as they know Him without limit and without end and without how, they see Him likewise; He is seen without place and without direction, without connection of a ray, and without distance between Him, Exalted, and the seer, because the vision with us is by the creation of God, Exalted, in any place He wills, and it is not necessary that it be only when conditions are met, as will be clarified. And it occurs for everyone who enters Paradise, from humans and jinn, from this nation and others, even women and children. And the vision is superior in quantity. His saying: (i.e., its occurrence) i.e., its attainment. His saying: (i.e., residence perpetually) is an interpretation of 'al-khuld,' and it contains an indication that what is meant is the abode of happiness absolutely, not specifically the one named by this name. His saying: (for everyone who enters Paradise) i.e., from animals whose nature is obligation; thus the non-rational animals are excluded, so they do not see even if they enter Paradise. His saying: (even women and children) i.e., from this nation and others; this is the relied-upon view, and it is said: they do not see Him, and it is said: they see Him on the festivals. His saying: (and the vision is superior) i.e., increases. And His saying: (in quantity) i.e., in number.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation and explanation of the believers' vision of God (ru'yat Allah) on the Day of Judgment. It begins with a command to affirm this vision as an obligatory belief, noting that the Prophet is the spiritual father who brought humanity out of disbelief. The vision is defined as 'complete unveiling by sight' (al-inkishāf al-tāmm bi al-baṣr). The commentary clarifies that this vision occurs in the Garden of Eternity perpetually, and it is without limitation or encompassment of God because He transcends all limits. Just as believers know God without modality (bilā kayf) in this world, they will see Him similarly: without place, direction, physical ray, or distance. The vision is not subject to physical conditions but occurs by God's direct creation in any location He wills. It occurs for all inhabitants of Paradise—humans and jinn, men and women, adults and children—from this nation and previous ones. The commentary notes that non-rational animals do not see God. The vision also admits of superiority in quantity (kamm), meaning varying degrees or frequency. The author also mentions alternative views regarding women and children but confirms the relied-upon position that they do see God.
