Fate of Disbelievers and Sinners
Al-Sawi states the fate of disbelievers and sinful believers, introducing intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different fates of disbelievers and sinful believers in the afterlife, including the role of intercession.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are punished forever; sinful believers may be forgiven or saved through intercession.

This lesson focuses on the first part of al-Sawi's discussion on reward and punishment. He establishes the ultimate destination of disbelievers and the possibility of mercy for believers who commit sins. The passage also introduces the concept of intercession as a means of salvation for sinful believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand the basic meaning.
Pay attention to the contrast between disbelievers and sinners.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage mentions disbelievers, sinners who are forgiven, and sinners who enter the Fire but eventually leave. Notice how each is treated.
3
Reflect on the role of intercession
Ask yourself why intercession is necessary for some sinners. The commentary will clarify that intercession is a mercy from Allah.
This connects to the broader aqeeda of shafa'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك، ثمَّ مآل الكفَّار إلى النَّار ويُخلَّدون فيها، وأما أهل المعاصي : فقد يُغفر لهم فلا يدخلون النَّار، وبعضُهم يدخلها ولكن لا يخلد فيها، بل لا بدَّ من خروجها بشفاعة نبينا أو غيره على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى .
وأمَّا بعد البعث : فمحله الرُّوح والجسد قطعاً، وكذا قبله في البرزخ على المشهور بأن يعيد الله الرُّوح إليه، أو إلى جزء منه إن قلنا إِنَّ المعذَّب بعض الجسد، ولا يمنع من ذلك كون الميت قد تفرّقت أجزاؤه أو أكلته السِّباع أو الحيتان فإنّ القادر لا يعجزه شيء، وقيل: ، إنه يتعلّق بالأرواح فقط . (والثواب) أي : الجزاء على الأعمال بالجَنَّة في الآخرة، وغيرها
من أنواع النّعيم، وكذا في البرزخ وبعده
قوله : (وكذا قبله في البرزخ) : أي : ويكون للكفّار، والمنافقين، هذه الأمة أو غيرها، ويدوم على الكفار والمنافقين، وبعض
والعصاة من العصاة، وينقطع عمن خفَّت ذنوبهم .
قوله : (وغيرها من أنواع النَّعيم) : أي : كرؤية وجه الله الكريم. قوله : (وكذا في البرزخ) : هو في اللُّغة: الحاجز بين الشيئين، وعرفاً : الحاجز بين الدُّنيا والآخرة، وله زمان ومآل ومكان؛ فزمانه من الموت إلى
القيامة، ومآله الأرواح، ومكانه من القبر إلى الجنَّة لأرواح السُّعداء، يوم أو إلى النَّار لأرواح الأشقياء.
وقوله: (وبعده) : أي : وبعد البرزخ وهو يوم القيامة، فينعم بظل
العرش مثلاً .
That being said, then the abode of the disbelievers is the Fire and they will be immortalized therein. As for the people of sins, they may be forgiven and not enter the Fire, and some of them enter it but are not immortalized therein; rather they must leave it through the intercession of our Prophet or others, as will come إن شاء الله تعالى. As for after the resurrection, its locus is the soul and the body definitively, and likewise before it in the barzakh according to the well-known view, by God returning the soul to it or to a part of it if we say that the punished is some part of the body. And nothing prevents this even if the deceased's parts have scattered or beasts or fish have eaten him, for the All-Powerful is not incapacitated by anything. And it is said that it pertains only to the souls. (And reward) meaning the recompense for deeds by Paradise in the Hereafter, and other types of bliss, and likewise in the barzakh and after it. His saying: (and likewise before it in the barzakh) meaning: and it occurs for the disbelievers, the hypocrites of this nation or others, and it continues for the disbelievers and hypocrites and some of the disobedient, and ceases for those whose sins are light. His saying: (and other types of bliss) meaning: such as seeing the face of Allah the Generous. His saying: (and likewise in the barzakh) — in language it is the barrier between two things, and in technical terms it is the barrier between this world and the Hereafter. It has a time, a final destination, and a place: its time is from death to the Resurrection, its final destination is the souls, and its place is from the grave to Paradise for the souls of the blessed, or to the Fire for the souls of the wretched. His saying: (and after it) meaning: after the barzakh, which is the Day of Resurrection, and they are blessed with the shade of the Throne, for example.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the fate of disbelievers and believers in the barzakh (intermediate state) and after resurrection. It opens by stating that disbelievers will be immortalized in the Fire, while sinful believers may either be forgiven and not enter the Fire, or enter but eventually leave through intercession. Then it discusses the locus of punishment and reward after resurrection: definitively both soul and body, and before resurrection (in the barzakh) most scholars hold that the soul is returned to the body (or a part of it) for punishment, and God's power is not limited by the body's disintegration. An alternative view is that punishment pertains only to souls. Next, it defines reward as recompense by Paradise and other bliss, also in barzakh and after. The commentary clarifies that punishment in barzakh applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and some disobedient, but ceases for those with light sins. It then defines 'barzakh' linguistically and technically, describing its time (death to resurrection), final destination (souls), and place (grave to Paradise or Fire). Finally, it notes that after the barzakh (on Judgment Day) believers are blessed with the shade of the Throne.

Key Terms
عقاب
نار
شفاعة
معاصي
كفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sinners will be punished eternally in Hell.
Correction: The text clarifies that sinful believers may be forgiven or eventually leave through intercession; only disbelievers are immortalized.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the final outcome for a believer who dies with sins but does not receive forgiveness?
A) They will be immortalized in the Fire.
B) They will enter the Fire but eventually leave through intercession.
C) They will be punished only in the barzakh.
D) They will be resurrected as disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Disbelievers face eternal punishment, while sinful believers may be saved through intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight, knowing your own record of sins, do you have any certainty that you are among those who will be forgiven and never enter the Fire? What in your life right now gives you that assurance?
?
The passage distinguishes between disbelievers and sinful believers. Could it be that you are living in a way that blurs that line—committing sins while assuming you are a believer, yet lacking the fear that distinguishes true faith?
?
Intercession is a mercy, but it is not a license to sin carelessly. What specific sin are you currently tolerating in your life that you are relying on intercession to excuse? What will you do about it before the end of this day?

Locus of Punishment and Reward in Barzakh and After Resurrection
Al-Sawi explains the locus of punishment and reward in barzakh and after resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that punishment and reward after death involve both soul and body according to the majority view, and that God's power is not limited by physical disintegration.

Core Idea
Punishment and reward affect both soul and body, even in barzakh, by God's power.

This lesson discusses the nature of punishment and reward: is it purely spiritual or physical? Al-Sawi presents the well-known view that both soul and body are involved, emphasizing God's ability to reunite them even if the body has decayed. He also mentions an alternative opinion that only the soul is affected.

Guided Path
1
Understand the locus after resurrection
The passage states that after resurrection, punishment/reward is definitively for soul and body together. This is a key aqeeda point.
2
Learn the barzakh ruling
Before resurrection (in barzakh), the majority view is the same: God returns the soul to the body. Explore the reasoning.
Note the condition 'if we say the punished is part of the body'.
3
Consider God's power
The passage affirms that even if the body is scattered or eaten, God can restore it. Reflect on this aspect of divine omnipotence.
Also note the minority view that punishment is only for souls.

Understanding Barzakh and the Reward of Believers
Al-Sawi defines barzakh and describes reward and punishment details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of barzakh, its temporal and spatial dimensions, and the reward believers receive including the vision of Allah.

Core Idea
Barzakh is the intermediate state between death and resurrection with specific dimensions.

This lesson covers the latter part of al-Sawi's discussion, defining the term 'barzakh' and detailing the reward of believers. It explains that reward includes Paradise and other bliss, such as seeing Allah's face. The passage also clarifies that punishment in barzakh applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and some disobedient, but ceases for those with light sins.

Guided Path

3

Final Abode of Disbelievers and Sinners
Defines the eternal and non-eternal punishments of disbelievers and sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrinal distinction between the eternal punishment of disbelievers and the temporary punishment of sinful Muslims, who may be forgiven or eventually saved by intercession.

Core Idea
The Fire is eternal for disbelievers but not for sinful Muslims.

This short passage from a classical creedal text lays out the final destinations of two groups: disbelievers and sinful Muslims. It clarifies a key point of Islamic eschatology: while the punishment of disbelievers is eternal, sinful Muslims have hope of forgiveness or eventual release through intercession. Let's examine the text to see the precise distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note the clear division between 'الكفَّار' and 'أهل المعاصي'.
2
Identify the two categories and their outcomes
The passage presents two main categories: disbelievers (kuffār) and people of sins (ahl al-ma‘āṣī). For disbelievers, the outcome is eternal fire. For sinful Muslims, there are two possibilities: forgiveness without entering the fire, or entering but eventually leaving by intercession.
Notice the word 'يُخلَّدون' for disbelievers vs 'لا يخلد' for sinful Muslims.
3
Understand the role of intercession
The passage states that sinful Muslims who enter the Fire will eventually exit 'بشفاعة نبينا أو غيره' (by the intercession of our Prophet or others). This is a key doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna.
The author promises further details later ('على ما سيأتي').
4
Reflect on the misconception
Some mistakenly think all sinful Muslims will remain in Hell forever. This passage corrects that by showing that forgiveness and intercession apply to them.
The common misunderstanding is addressed in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك، ثمَّ مآل الكفَّار إلى النَّار ويُخلَّدون فيها، وأما أهل المعاصي : فقد يُغفر لهم فلا يدخلون النَّار، وبعضُهم يدخلها ولكن لا يخلد فيها، بل لا بدَّ من خروجه منها بشفاعة نبينا أو غيره على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى .
That is, then the final abode of the disbelievers is the Fire and they are made to abide therein forever. As for the people of sins: some are forgiven so they do not enter the Fire, and some of them enter it but do not abide forever; rather, they must come out of it by the intercession of our Prophet or others, as will come, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement about the final destinations of different categories of people. It begins with disbelievers (kuffār): their final abode (māl) is the Fire (an-nār) and they are made to abide (yukhalladūn) there eternally. Then it addresses the people of sins (ahl al-ma‘āṣī), i.e., Muslims who commit major sins without repentance. Among them, some are forgiven by Allah's mercy and never enter the Fire. Others do enter the Fire but are not eternal therein (lā yukhallad fīhā); they must eventually exit by means of intercession (shafā‘a) from our Prophet Muhammad or other intercessors. The author notes that details will follow later, if Allah wills.

Key Terms
مآل
الكفَّار
النَّار
الخلد
أهل المعاصي
المغفرة
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sinful Muslims will remain in Hell forever.
Correction: The passage teaches that some sinful Muslims are forgiven entirely and some enter the Fire but eventually leave by intercession, so they do not abide forever.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the outcome of disbelievers in the Fire?
A) They are punished temporarily
B) They are made to abide forever
C) They are forgiven
D) They are saved by intercession

Key Takeaway
The Fire is eternal for disbelievers, but sinful Muslims may be forgiven or eventually freed by intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you secretly rely on the possibility of intercession to escape Hell, or does this lesson’s emphasis on forgiveness before entering the Fire push you to seek sincere repentance today?
?
The passage states some sinful Muslims are forgiven and never see the Fire. What does that reveal about the depth of Allah’s mercy? Are you living as though you deserve that mercy, or are you taking it for granted by continuing in disobedience?
?
If you truly believed that disbelievers face eternal Fire, would your concern for their salvation be stronger? How does this reality challenge the way you interact with non-Muslims in your daily life?

Locus of Reward and Punishment After Death
Sanusi explains the locus of punishment and reward in two eschatological stages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subject (maḥall) of punishment and reward after resurrection and in the intermediate state (barzakh), including the well‑known view and a minority opinion.

Core Idea
Punishment and reward involve both soul and body, even after death.

This passage from the Kharīda clarifies a key question in Islamic eschatology: what part of the human being experiences reward and punishment after death? Sanusi presents two time periods — after the Resurrection (ba‘th) and before it, in the Barzakh — and gives the well‑known view that the soul is returned to the body (or part of it). He also answers an obvious objection about the body decaying or being eaten by animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two time periods
The passage discusses punishment/reward at two distinct times: after the Resurrection and before it (in Barzakh). Notice that the ruling for each is different in certainty.
2
Understand the definitive ruling after Resurrection
The text says that after the Resurrection, the locus (maḥall) is the soul and the body 'definitively' (qaṭ‘an). This is the settled position.
3
Grasp the well‑known view in Barzakh
Before the Resurrection, in Barzakh, the well‑known view (al‑mashhūr) is that Allah returns the soul to the body, or to a part of the body if punishment is on a part. This is a nuanced position.
The text notes a weaker alternative: only souls.
4
Reflect on the divine power argument
The passage answers a problem: even if the body has scattered or been eaten, Allah is all‑powerful (Qādir) and can restore it. This shows that the doctrine relies on God's omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا بعد البعث : فمحله الرُّوح والجسد قطعاً، وكذا قبله في البرزخ على المشهور بأن يعيد الله الرُّوح إليه، أو إلى جزء منه إن قلنا إِنَّ المعذَّب بعض الجسد، ولا يمنع من ذلك كون الميت قد تفرّقت أجزاؤه أو أكلته السِّباع أو الحيتان فإنّ القادر لا يعجزه شيء، وقيل: ، إنه يتعلّق بالأرواح فقط .
As for after the Resurrection: its locus is the soul and the body definitively. And likewise before it, in the Barzakh, according to the well-known view, by Allah returning the soul to it, or to a part of it if we say that the punished one is a part of the body. And that is not prevented by the fact that the deceased's parts have scattered or that beasts or fish have eaten him, for the All-Powerful is not incapacitated by anything. And it is said: it pertains only to souls.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the subject (maḥall) of punishment and reward. It states that after the Resurrection (ba‘th), the locus is definitively both the soul (rūḥ) and the body (jasad). Before the Resurrection, in the intermediate state (al-barzakh), the well-known opinion (al-mashhūr) is that Allah returns the soul to the body, or to a part of the body, if one accepts the view that the punishment is on a part of the body. The text then addresses a potential objection: even if the body has disintegrated, scattered, or been consumed by predators, Allah's power is not hindered—He is al-Qādir (the All-Powerful). A second, weaker opinion is mentioned: that punishment/reward pertains only to souls.

الرُّوح

القادر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The text affirms the well‑known view that both soul and body are involved, even in Barzakh, because Allah returns the soul to the body.

Checkpoint

The Comprehensive Definition of Reward
Lexical and theological definition of thawab with expansion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that reward (thawab) encompasses both Paradise and other blessings, including the vision of Allah, and applies in Barzakh and the afterlife.

Core Idea
Reward is not just Paradise; it includes every blessing, culminating in seeing Allah.

Before we explore the deeper implications of divine reward, we must first understand what the term 'thawab' truly means. The author provides a precise lexical and theological definition, clarifying that reward is not limited to Paradise but includes all types of bliss, both in the intermediate state and the Hereafter. Most importantly, he points to the greatest reward: the vision of Allah's face.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once. Notice how the author defines 'thawab' as a recompense (jaza') and then expands it with details.
Pay attention to the parenthetical explanation of 'other types of bliss'.
2
Identify the components of reward
The definition lists several components: Paradise, other types of bliss, the Barzakh, and the afterlife. Also note the specific example of seeing Allah's face.
This shows that reward is comprehensive.
3
Contrast with potential misunderstandings
Some might think reward is only Paradise. The text explicitly includes 'other types of bliss' and gives a concrete example. Compare this with the common misunderstanding.
This guards against a narrow view of reward.
4
Reflect on the significance of the vision of Allah
The vision of Allah's face is mentioned as an example of 'other bliss'. Consider why the author highlights this: it is the ultimate reward.
This connects to broader theological discussions about the beatific vision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والثواب) أي : الجزاء على الأعمال بالجَنَّة في الآخرة، وغيرها من أنواع النّعيم، وكذا في البرزخ وبعده وقوله : (وغيرها من أنواع النَّعيم) : أي : كرؤية وجه الله الكريم.
(And reward) i.e., the recompense for deeds with Paradise in the Hereafter, and other types of bliss, and likewise in the Barzakh and after it. And his saying: (and other types of bliss) i.e., like the vision of the face of Allah, the Generous.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and theological definition of the term 'al-thawāb' (reward). It explains that thawāb is the recompense (jizā') for good deeds, which includes Paradise (al-janna) in the Hereafter (al-ākhira) as well as other types of bliss (anwā‘ an-na‘īm). This reward is also given in the Barzakh (intermediate state) and after it (i.e., after the Resurrection). The commentary on the phrase 'and other types of bliss' specifies that one such type is the vision of the face of Allah (ru’yat wajh Allāh al-Karīm), which is the greatest blessing.

Punishment in Barzakh for Different Categories
Clarifies which groups experience punishment in the Barzakh and its duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that punishment in the Barzakh applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and some sinners, but ceases for those whose sins are light.

Core Idea
Barzakh punishment is certain for disbelievers and hypocrites, but only some sinners face it.

This lesson examines a brief but crucial passage from the commentary that clarifies the scope of punishment in the Barzakh. It distinguishes between permanent punishment for disbelievers and hypocrites, and temporary or no punishment for light-sinning believers. Understanding this helps avoid overgeneralizing about the intermediate state.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it is a commentary explaining the phrase 'and likewise before it in the Barzakh'.
2
Identify the categories mentioned
The passage lists two main groups: disbelievers and hypocrites (whose punishment continues), and sinners (some of whom are punished, but not those with light sins).
3
Reflect on the distinction
Consider why the punishment ceases for those with light sins. This shows that Barzakh punishment is not automatic for all wrongdoers.
This connects to broader concepts of divine mercy and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكذا قبله في البرزخ) : أي : ويكون للكفّار، والمنافقين، هذه الأمة أو غيرها، ويدوم على الكفار والمنافقين، وبعض والعصاة من العصاة، وينقطع عمن خفَّت ذنوبهم .
His saying: (and likewise before it in the Barzakh) i.e., it is for the disbelievers, the hypocrites— of this nation or others— and it continues for the disbelievers and the hypocrites, and some of the sinners from among the sinners, and it ceases for those whose sins are light.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the phrase 'and likewise before it in the Barzakh' found in the preceding text. It clarifies that punishment in the Barzakh is for the disbelievers (al-kuffār) and the hypocrites (al-munāfiqīn), whether from this Muslim nation or other nations. This punishment persists (yadūm) for the disbelievers and hypocrites. Additionally, some of the sinners ('uṣāt) also receive punishment in the Barzakh, but it ceases (yanqaṭi‘) for those whose sins are light (khaffat dhunūbuhum).

Correction: The text specifies that only some sinners face punishment in Barzakh, and it ceases for those whose sins are light.

Understanding Barzakh: Definition and Aspects
Defines barzakh linguistically, technically, and explains its time, outcome, and place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical definitions of Barzakh, as well as its time, outcome, and place dimensions.

Core Idea
Barzakh is the barrier between this world and the next, with a defined time, outcome, and place.

This lesson introduces the concept of Barzakh, a key term in Islamic eschatology. Al-Sawi begins by giving both the linguistic and technical meanings, then expands on three essential aspects: its time frame, what happens to the souls, and its location. This foundational understanding is crucial for grasping what happens between death and the Resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the literal English translation. Notice the structure: definition first, then three aspects.
The passage is short but packed with key terms.
2
Understand the two definitions
Identify the linguistic meaning ('barrier between two things') and the technical meaning ('barrier between this world and the Hereafter'). Note that the technical meaning is specific to eschatology.
3
Examine the three aspects
The passage lists time, outcome, and place. For each, note what is specified: time from death to Resurrection, outcome is the souls, place from grave to Paradise or Fire.
The place varies depending on whether the soul is blessed or wretched.
4
Connect to the broader context
Consider how this definition fits into the topic of samiyyat (matters of the unseen). The Barzakh is the first stage after death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكذا في البرزخ) : هو في اللُّغة: الحاجز بين الشيئين، وعرفاً : الدُّنيا والآخرة، وله زمان ومآل ومكان؛ فزمانه من الموت إلى القيامة، ومآله الأرواح، ومكانه من القبر إلى الجنَّة لأرواح السُّعداء، يوم أو إلى النَّار لأرواح الأشقياء. وقوله: (وبعده) : أي : وبعد البرزخ وهو يوم القيامة، فينعم بظل العرش مثلاً .
His saying: (and likewise in the Barzakh): It is linguistically: the barrier between two things. And technically: the barrier between this world and the Hereafter. And it has a time, an outcome, and a place. Its time is from death to the Resurrection. Its outcome is the souls. Its place is from the grave to Paradise for the souls of the blessed, then or to the Fire for the souls of the wretched. And his saying: (and after it) i.e., after the Barzakh, which is the Day of Resurrection, so one is blessed with, for example, the shade of the Throne.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the term 'al-barzakh'. It gives the linguistic meaning: a barrier (al-ḥājiz) between two things. Then the technical meaning (ʿurfan): the barrier between this world (ad-dunyā) and the Hereafter (al-ākhira). The author then explains that barzakh has three aspects: a time (zamān), an outcome (ma’āl), and a place (makān). The time of barzakh is from death until the Resurrection (al-qiyāma). Its outcome is the souls (al-arwāḥ)—that is, the souls go to their respective places. The place of barzakh is from the grave to Paradise for the souls of the blessed (as-su‘adā’), and to the Fire for the souls of the wretched (al-ashqiyā’). The commentary then explains the phrase 'and after it' (ba‘dahu) meaning after the Barzakh is the Day of Resurrection, and then the blessed enjoy things like the shade of the Throne (ẓill al-‘arsh).

Key Terms

الحاجز
الدنيا
الآخرة
القيامة
الأرواح
السُّعداء
الأشقياء
ظل العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think Barzakh is only the grave itself.
Correction: The text clarifies that Barzakh is the entire interval from death to Resurrection, not just the grave. The grave is part of its place, but Barzakh encompasses a broader temporal and spatial dimension.

Checkpoint

A) The interval between death and judgment
B) The barrier between two things
C) The place of souls
D) The Day of Resurrection

Key Takeaway
Barzakh is the barrier between this world and the Hereafter, with a specific time (death to Resurrection), outcome (souls), and place (grave to Paradise or Fire).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Al-Nashr: The Nature of Bodily Resurrection
Definition of al-Nashr and two opinions on gathering body parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what al-Nashr means and the two scholarly opinions on how Allah gathers the body parts for resurrection, including the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The resurrection is a physical recreation except for the coccyx bone, as per the relied-upon opinion.

In this lesson, we learn the definition of al-Nashr (resurrection) and explore a key theological debate: are the dead revived by gathering scattered parts, or by complete recreation? The author presents both views and concludes which is the relied-upon position. Understanding this distinction clarifies the nature of bodily resurrection in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage first defines al-Nashr, then presents two opinions.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage presents two opinions on gathering the original parts: after dispersion or after complete non-existence. Find each one and note the exception of the coccyx bone.
The second opinion is supported by Quran 7:29.
3
Understand the relied-upon opinion
The author states which opinion is al-mu‘tamad (relied-upon). Understand why this opinion is preferred and its implication for bodily resurrection.
This connects to the learning objective.
4
Note the exception
The passage mentions that this disagreement applies only to those whose bodies are consumed by the earth. Reflect on who might be excluded.
Prophets and martyrs are often mentioned as exceptions in other texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والنشر) وهو البعث والمراد به إحياء الله الموتى من قبورهم بعد جمع أجزائهم الأصليّة ؛ بأن يجمعها الله بعد تفرقها، وقيل: بعد عدمها بالكلية ما عدا عجب الذنب فإنَّه لا يُعدم. قوله: (وقيل بعد عدمها بالكلِّيَّة أي : فيصير الجسم معدوماً بالكلِّيَّة، كما كان قبل وجوده قال تعالى: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تَعُودُونَ (١) ، وهذا :القول: هو المعتمد، وهذا الخلاف في غير من لا تأكل الأرض أجسامهم
(And al-nashr) i.e., the resurrection (al-ba‘th), meaning Allah's reviving the dead from their graves after gathering their original parts; by Allah gathering them after their dispersion, and it is said: after their non-existence entirely, except the coccyx bone, for it is not annihilated. His saying: (and it is said: after their non-existence entirely), i.e., the body becomes entirely non-existent, just as it was before its existence. Allah said: 'As He began you, you shall return' (Quran 7:29). And this opinion is the relied-upon one. And this disagreement applies to other than those whose bodies the earth does not consume.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage defines 'al-nashr', which is equivalent to 'al-ba‘th' (resurrection). It means Allah's act of reviving the dead from their graves. There are two opinions regarding the gathering of the original parts (ajzā’ihim al-aṣliyya). The first opinion: Allah gathers the scattered parts after they have dispersed. The second opinion: the body becomes completely non-existent (except for the coccyx bone, 'ajb adh-dhanab, which remains), and Allah creates it anew. The second opinion is supported by the Qur'anic verse 'As He began you, you shall return' (7:29). The author states that this second opinion is the relied-upon (al-mu‘tamad) one. However, this disagreement applies only to those whose bodies are not consumed by the earth; there are exceptions for certain types of people whose bodies are preserved.

Key Terms
النشر
البعث
الإحياء
الأجزاء الأصليّة
عجب الذنب
المعتمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the resurrection is purely spiritual or that the body is completely annihilated without any continuity.
Correction: The relied-upon opinion affirms physical recreation with the coccyx bone remaining as a continuous element, thus preserving bodily identity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon opinion (al-mu‘tamad) about the body at resurrection?
A) The original parts are gathered after dispersion
B) The body is created anew from non-existence except the coccyx bone
C) The body remains unchanged
D) Only the soul is resurrected

Key Takeaway
The resurrection of the body involves a recreation from non-existence, with the coccyx bone as the only original part that persists, as per the relied-upon view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe your body will be resurrected, but do you live as if every part of it will be brought to account? How does that change how you use your eyes, tongue, and hands today? Resolve to guard one of them this week.

Bodies Preserved from Decay: Prophets, Scholars, Martyrs, and Others
Enumerates ten categories of preserved bodies via two poems.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten categories of people whose bodies are preserved from decay according to classical Sunni tradition, as enumerated in two poems.

Core Idea
The earth does not consume the bodies of certain righteous souls.

This lesson presents two poetic enumerations listing categories of people whose bodies are protected from decay. The first, by al-Tana'i, mentions five groups; the second, by al-Ajhūrī, adds five more. These lists highlight the spiritual honor bestowed upon certain believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic poems
Read the two poems carefully. Notice the meter (basīṭ) and the rhyme. Try to identify the categories listed in each.
The poems are cited as proof of the doctrine.
2
List the categories from the first poem
Identify the five categories al-Tana'i mentions: Prophet, scholar, martyr killed in battle, Quran reciter, and one who reckons his call to prayer.
3
List the categories from the second poem
Identify the five additional categories al-Ajhūrī adds: lover for Allah, one who dies by plague, one who dies on a frontier, and one who engages in much remembrance (the latter being the greatest devotion).
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these particular groups are singled out. The common misunderstanding is that all bodies decay; these exceptions indicate special spiritual status.
The passage does not explain the reasons, only states the fact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونظمهم التنائي فقال(۲): [ من البسيط] لا تأكل الأرض جسماً للنَّبيِّ ولا لعالم وشـهـيـد قـتـل مـعـتـرك ولا لقارئ قرآن ومـحـتـسـب أذانه لإلهِ مُجري الفلك وزاد العلامة الأجهوري خمسة فقال(۳) : [ من البسيط] غدا محبّاً لأجل الواحد الملك ومن يموت بطعن أو رباط أو كثير ذكـر وهـذا أعـظـم الـنـسـك
And he (al-Tana'i) composed poetry, saying (in basīṭ meter): 'The earth does not consume the body of a Prophet, nor of a scholar, nor of a martyr killed in battle, nor of a reciter of the Qur'an, nor of one who reckons his call to prayer for the God who runs the celestial sphere.' And the scholar al-Ajhūrī added five, saying (in basīṭ meter): '[And] he who becomes a lover for the sake of the One, the King, and he who dies by plague or on a frontier or much remembrance— and this is the greatest act of devotion.'
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a poetical enumeration of types of people whose bodies are not consumed by the earth (lā ta'kul al-arḍ ajsāmahum), preserving them from decay. It begins by quoting a poem by al-Tana'i (or al-Tanā'ī) listing five categories: a Prophet (nabī), a scholar ('ālim), a martyr (shahīd) killed in battle (qutl mu‘tarak), a reciter of the Quran (qāri’ Quran), and one who reckons his call to prayer (muḥtasib adhānahu) for God. Then it adds that the scholar al-Ajhūrī added five more categories in another poem: one who becomes a lover for Allah (ghada muḥibban), one who dies by plague (ṭa‘n), one who dies on a frontier (ribāṭ), and one who engages in much remembrance (kathīr dhikr)—and this last is said to be the greatest act of devotion (a‘ẓam an-nusuk).

Key Terms
لا تأكل الأرض
النبي
العالم
الشهيد
قارئ القرآن
المحتسب
الطاعون
الرباط
الذكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All bodies decay in the earth without exception.
Correction: This text lists ten categories of people whose bodies are not consumed, indicating exceptions based on spiritual status.

Checkpoint

A) Dying by plague
B) Dying on a frontier
C) Much remembrance
D) Being a lover for Allah

Key Takeaway
The earth does not consume the bodies of ten specific categories of believers, as preserved in two poems.

Defining al-Nashr and the Debate on Body Annihilation
Al-Sawi defines al-nashr and presents two opinions on body annihilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-nashr and the two opinions on the state of bodies at death before resurrection, including the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Resurrection involves recreating bodies from the coccyx bone after annihilation.

Al-Sawi begins by defining the key term 'al-nashr' and immediately introduces a theological debate: what happens to the body at death? Two views are presented, and the second is affirmed as the relied-upon position. This lesson focuses on that definition and the evidence from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Start by reading the Arabic passage that defines al-nashr. Note the key words: النشر, البعث, إحياء, أجزائهم الأصليّة.
The definition equates al-nashr with al-ba'th (raising).
2
Identify the two opinions
Look for the phrases 'بعد تفرقها' and 'بعد عدمها بالكلية'. These present the two views on the state of the body.
The second opinion includes the exception of the coccyx bone (عجب الذنب).
3
Understand the evidence for the relied-upon view
Notice the Quranic citation (7:29) and the statement 'وهذا القول هو المعتمد'. This establishes the preferred position.
The coccyx bone is said to never be annihilated, serving as the seed for recreation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالنشر والصّراط (والنشر) وهو البعث والمراد به إحياء الله الموتى من قبورهم بعد جمع أجزائهم الأصليّة ؛ بأن يجمعها الله بعد تفرقها، وقيل: بعد عدمها بالكلية ما عدا عجب الذنب فإنَّه لا يُعدم. قوله: (وقيل بعد عدمها بالكلِّيَّة أي : فيصير الجسم معدوماً بالكلِّيَّة، كما كان قبل وجوده قال تعالى: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تَعُودُونَ (١) ، وهذا :القول: هو المعتمد، وهذا الخلاف في غير من لا تأكل الأرض أجسامهم، ونظمهم التنائي فقال(۲): [ من البسيط] لا تأكل الأرض جسماً للنَّبيِّ ولا لعالم وشـهـيـد قـتـل مـعـتـرك ولا لقارئ قرآن ومـحـتـسـب أذانه لإلهِ مُجري الفلك وزاد العلامة الأجهوري خمسة فقال(۳) : من [ من البسيط] غدا محبّاً لأجل الواحد الملك ومن يموت بطعن أو رباط أو كثير ذكـر وهـذا أعـظـم الـنـسـك وقيل : هو الإخراج من القبور بعد الإحياء بردّ الرُّوح فيه
Faith in al-Nashr (the Resurrection). al-Nashr is the Raising, and what is meant by it is God's reviving of the dead from their graves after gathering their original parts: by Him gathering them after their dispersal, and it is said: after their complete non-existence except for the coccyx bone, for it does not cease. His saying: (and it is said: after their complete non-existence meaning: the body becomes completely non-existent, as it was before its existence. He said, Exalted: 'As He began you, you shall return' (7:29). And this saying is the relied-upon one. And this disagreement is for other than those whose bodies the earth does not eat. And al-Tana'i organized them in verse, saying (from basit): 'The earth does not eat the body of a prophet, nor of a scholar, nor of a martyr killed in battle, nor of a Quran reciter, nor of a muhtasib whose call to prayer is for the God who runs the celestial sphere.' And the scholar al-Ujhuri added five, saying (from basit): 'And add whoever becomes a saintly friend likewise, who becomes a lover for the sake of the One King, and who dies by stabbing or ribat or much remembrance, and this is the greatest act of devotion.' And it is said: it is the taking out from the graves after reviving by returning the spirit into it.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage defines the doctrine of al-nashr (resurrection) and discusses two opinions on the state of bodies. It begins by defining al-nashr as 'al-ba'th' (the raising), meaning God's reviving of the dead after gathering their original parts. Two opinions are then given: first, that God gathers the parts after they have dispersed; second, that the body becomes completely non-existent except for the coccyx bone (عجب الذنب). The second opinion is supported by Quran 7:29 and is called 'al-mu'tamad' (the relied-upon). The commentator then notes that this disagreement only applies to those whose bodies are eaten by the earth; for those whose bodies are not eaten, there is no debate. To illustrate the exception, he presents a poetic list by al-Tana'i naming prophets, scholars, martyrs, Quran reciters, and a muhtasib. al-Ujhuri added five more categories: the saintly friend (siddiq), the lover of God, one who dies by stabbing, one who dies in ribat (frontier guard), and one engaged in abundant remembrance. Finally, a second definition of al-nashr is given: it is the extraction (ikhraj) from the graves after reviving by returning the spirit. This complements the first definition and completes the doctrinal overview.

Key Terms
النشر
البعث
عجب الذنب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the body remains intact but dispersed, or that the coccyx is the only part that remains while the rest is annihilated.
Correction: The relied-upon view is that the body becomes completely non-existent except for the coccyx bone, which is preserved as the basis for recreation.

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon view regarding the state of the body at death before resurrection?
A) The body remains intact but is gathered from dispersal.
B) The body becomes completely non-existent except for the coccyx bone.
C) The body is preserved in the grave unchanged.
D) The body is transformed into a spiritual substance.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection involves the complete annihilation of the body except the coccyx bone, which remains as the seed for recreation, as supported by Quran 7:29.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that your entire body will be annihilated except for a single bone, then recreated by God. How does this change your attitude toward your physical appearance and desires today? What one concrete action will you take this week to prioritize your spiritual reality over your physical urges?
?
The relied-upon opinion teaches that your body will become completely non-existent, as it was before you were born. Does this make you more or less attached to your body and its pleasures? What can you do today to use your body in a way that you would be proud to have it recreated by God?
?
If the resurrection is as certain as this lesson affirms, what is one habit or sin you have been justifying because you thought your body would just be reassembled from scattered parts? How will you respond now that you know it will be created anew from nothing?

Exceptions and the Second Definition of Resurrection
Al-Sawi lists exceptions whose bodies are not eaten by earth and gives a second definition of resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that certain individuals are exempt from body annihilation and that al-nashr also means extraction from graves after reviving.

Core Idea
Prophets, scholars, martyrs, and others are exempt from body decay; resurrection is also extraction from graves.

After settling the general rule of body annihilation, Al-Sawi notes an important exception: some individuals' bodies are not consumed by the earth. He then provides poetic lists of these exceptions and concludes with a second definition of resurrection as extraction from the graves. This lesson covers that exception and the complementary definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the exception clause
Look for the phrase 'وهذا الخلاف في غير من لا تأكل الأرض أجبادهم'. This tells you that the earlier debate does not apply to certain people.
The earth does not eat the bodies of these special individuals.
2
Study the poetic lists
Read the two poems by al-Tana'i and al-Ujhuri. Identify the categories mentioned: prophets, scholars, martyrs, Quran reciters, muhtasib, etc.
These poems serve as mnemonic devices to remember the exceptions.
3
Understand the second definition
The passage ends with 'وقيل: هو الإخراج من القبور بعد الإحياء بردّ الرُّوح فيه'. This defines al-nashr also as extraction from graves after returning the spirit.
This complements the earlier definition by specifying the physical process.

Source Text

Faith in al-Nashr (the Resurrection). al-Nashr is the Raising, and what is meant by it is God's reviving of the dead from their graves after gathering their original parts: by Him gathering them after their dispersal, and it is said: after their complete non-existence except for the coccyx bone, for it does not cease. His saying: (and it is said: after their complete non-existence meaning: the body becomes completely non-existent, as it was before its existence. And al-Tana'i organized them in verse, saying (from basit): 'The earth does not eat the body of a prophet, nor of a scholar, nor of a martyr killed in battle, nor of a Quran reciter, nor of a muhtasib whose call to prayer is for the God who runs the celestial sphere.' Commentary
This passage defines the doctrine of al-nashr (resurrection) and discusses two opinions on the state of bodies. It begins by defining al-nashr as 'al-ba'th' (the raising), meaning God's reviving of the dead after gathering their original parts. Two opinions are then given: first, that God gathers the parts after they have dispersed; second, that the body becomes completely non-existent except for the coccyx bone (عجب الذنب). Finally, a second definition of al-nashr is given: it is the extraction (ikhraj) from the graves after reviving by returning the spirit. This complements the first definition and completes the doctrinal overview.

النشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the exception list is limited to the first five categories or that it is not an exception at all.
Correction: The exception includes at least ten categories as per the poems, and the debate only applies to those whose bodies are eaten by the earth.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT included in al-Tana'i's list of those whose bodies are not eaten by the earth?
A) Prophet
B) Scholar
C) Martyr
D) Saintly friend (siddiq)

Key Takeaway
Certain people (prophets, scholars, martyrs, etc.) are exempt from body annihilation, and resurrection also means the extraction of the spirit-returned body from the grave.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which category from this passage do you most desire to be in? What one concrete step can you take today to move toward that identity, knowing that the earth may not consume your body if you do?
?
If resurrection means you will be extracted from your grave with a returned spirit, are you living now as though that moment is real and imminent? What habit or attachment would you need to abandon tonight to truly prepare for that extraction?
?
The muhtasib is praised for calling to prayer for God. Do you ever call people to Allah, even quietly? If not, what fear holds you back from being among those whose bodies are preserved?

Definition and Discussion of al-Sirat (the Bridge)
Al-Sawi defines al-sirat, discusses its nature, and describes the passers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-sirat, its characteristics, the scholarly disagreement about its nature, and how it varies for different people.

Core Idea
Al-sirat is a real bridge whose crossing varies by one's deeds.

Al-Sawi presents the Islamic understanding of al-sirat, the bridge over Hell. He begins with its linguistic and technical definitions, then discusses its physical description and the debate about its width. The passage also clarifies that the crossing speed depends on one's deeds, not on being a believer alone.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of al-sirat
Read the linguistic and technical definitions. Note that linguistically it means a clear path, and technically it is a bridge over Hell between the standing-place and Paradise.
This establishes the basic concept.
2
Examine the description and objection
Consider the description 'finer than a hair, sharper than a sword' and al-Qarafi's objection based on his master al-Izz. Determine why the preferred view is that it varies.
The objection is important for understanding the scholarly debate.
3
Learn the preferred view
The most apparent view (al-azhar) is that the bridge varies in narrowness and width according to deeds. This is the correct position.
This resolves the earlier disagreement.
4
Consider opinions on disbelievers
There are different opinions on whether disbelievers cross the bridge. Some say they are led directly to Hell, others say some cross and some do not.
This shows that not all pass the bridge in the same manner.
5
Review the types of passers
The text lists eight types of passers, from the fastest (blink of an eye) to the slowest (crawling). The speed is based on their righteous deeds and avoidance of sins.
The variation in speed illustrates the principle that deeds affect the crossing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والصراط) وهو لغة : الطريق الواضح. وشرعاً : جسر ممدود على متن جهنّم بين الموقف والجنَّة؛ لأنَّ جهنَّم بينهما، تَرِدُه المؤمنون والكفَّار للمرور عليه إلى الجنَّة، أدق من الشعر وأحد من السيف. وأنكر القرافي تبعاً لشيخه العزّ كونه أدقّ من الشعرة وأحد من السَّيف، بل هو متّسع لما ورد ما يدل على ذلك . والأظهر : أنَّه مختلف في الضّيق والاتساع باختلاف الأعمال. وقيل : إنَّ الكفار لا يمرون عليه، بل يؤمر بهم إلى النَّار من أوَّل الأمر ، وقيل : بعضُهم يمرُّ وبعضُهم لا يمر . والمارون عليه مختلفون : — فمنهم سالم بعمله ناجِ من الوقوع في نار جهنم، وهم على أقسام فمنهم من يجوزه كلمحة البصر، ومنهم من يجوزه كالبرق الخاطف ومنهم كالرّيح العاصف، ومنهم: كالطير، ومنهم: كالجواد السابق، ومنهم من يسعى سعياً، ومنهم من يمشي، : ومنهم من يمرُّ عليه حَبواً على قدر تفاوتهم في الأعمال الصالحة : والإعراض عن المعاصي، فكلُّ من كان أسرع إعراضاً عنها إذا مرَّت قوله : (على متن جهنَّم) أي ظهرها . قوله : (والأظهر : أنَّه مختلف): أي: وهو الصواب. قوله : (وهم على أقسام أي ثمانية.
(and al-Sirat) which is linguistically: the clear path. And technically: a bridge extended over the back of Hell between the standing-place and Paradise; because Hell is between them. The believers and disbelievers will come to it to pass over it to Paradise, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. And al-Qarafi denied, following his master al-Izz, its being finer than a hair and sharper than a sword; rather it is wide, due to what has been reported that indicates that. And the most apparent is that it varies in narrowness and width according to deeds. And it is said: the disbelievers do not pass over it, but rather they are commanded to the Fire from the beginning; and it is said: some of them pass and some do not. And those who pass over it differ: some are safe by their deeds, saved from falling into the fire of Hell, and they are of types: among them is one who crosses it like the blink of an eye, among them one who crosses it like a lightning flash, among them like a violent wind, among them like a bird, among them like a swift horse, among them one who runs, among them one who walks, and among them one who crosses it crawling, according to their difference in righteous deeds and turning away from sins. So whoever was quicker in turning away from them when they pass... His saying: ('on the back of Hell') i.e., its surface. His saying: ('and the most apparent is that it varies'): i.e., and it is correct. His saying: ('and they are of types') i.e., eight.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage defines al-sirat (the bridge) and discusses its characteristics and the details of crossing. It begins with the linguistic meaning: a clear path. The technical definition is a bridge stretched over the back (surface) of Hell, located between the standing-place (al-mawqif) and Paradise, since Hell lies between them. All people—believers and disbelievers—will come to it to pass over to Paradise. It is described as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. Then a disagreement is noted: al-Qarafi, following his master al-Izz, denied this description, claiming rather that it is wide based on evidence. The preferred view (al-azhar) is that its width varies according to deeds, being narrow for some and wide for others. There is also a difference of opinion on whether disbelievers cross it: some say they are led directly to Hell, others say some cross and some do not. The passage then describes the various types of passers, all of whom are safe by their deeds. They are categorized by their speed: like a blink of an eye, like lightning, like wind, like a bird, like a horse, running, walking, or crawling. This variation is based on their righteous deeds and avoidance of sins—the quicker they turned away from sins, the faster they cross. The commentary explains that 'on the back of Hell' means its surface, 'the most apparent is that it varies' means it is correct, and 'they are of types' means eight types.

Key Terms
الصراط
الموقف
الجسر
الأعمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The bridge is uniform for everyone in width and crossing speed.
Correction: The preferred view is that the bridge varies in narrowness and width according to deeds, and the passing speed depends on one's righteous deeds and avoidance of sins.

Checkpoint
What is the preferred view (al-azhar) regarding the nature of al-sirat?
A) It is uniformly fine like a hair.
B) It is uniformly wide.
C) It varies in narrowness and width according to deeds.
D) It does not exist; it is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Al-sirat is a real bridge that varies in narrowness and width according to one's deeds, determining the speed of crossing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If al-sirat becomes narrower and crossing slower for those who cling to sins, what sin in your life right now would make your crossing most difficult? What will you do today to begin abandoning it?
?
The source says the speed of crossing depends on how quickly you turn away from sins when they come to you. Think of a recent temptation you faced. How quickly did you turn away? What can you change to be among those who cross like lightning?
?
You will stand before al-sirat with only your deeds. Are you building a bridge of righteousness or a burden that will slow you down? What one act of obedience can you commit to this week to increase your speed?

Definition and Nature of al-Sirat
Al-Sawi establishes the definition and disputed nature of al-Sirat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and legal definition of al-Sirat and the scholarly discussion about its physical properties.

Core Idea
Al-Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, varying in width according to deeds.

The concept of al-Sirat is one of the major eschatological realities in Sunni Islam. It is not merely a symbol but a physical bridge that every soul must cross. This lesson establishes its definition and the key debate about its dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Sirat
Read both the linguistic and legal definitions. Notice the shift from language to sacred law.
The legal definition adds the eschatological context.
2
Understand its location and description
Consider the bridge's placement between the standing place and Paradise, and the description 'finer than hair, sharper than a sword'.
3
Examine the disagreement about its size
Note al-Qarafi's objection based on lack of evidence, and the response that the more apparent view is that it varies according to deeds.
This disagreement shows the importance of textual evidence in kalam.
4
Reflect on the meaning of variation
Ask yourself: why would the bridge's narrowness depend on deeds? How does this relate to divine justice?
This connects to the broader theme of accountability.

والصراط) وهو لغة : الطريق الواضح. وشرعاً : جسر ممدود على متن جهنّم بين الموقف والجنَّة؛ لأنَّ جهنَّم بينهما ، تَرِدُه المؤمنون والكفَّار للمرور عليه إلى الجنَّة، أدق من الشعر وأحد من السيف. وأنكر القرافي تبعاً لشيخه العزّ كونه أدقّ من الشعرة وأحد من السَّيف، بل هو متّسع لما ورد ما يدل على ذلك . والأظهر : أنَّه مختلف في الضّيق والاتساع باختلاف الأعمال. وقيل : إنَّ الكفار لا يمرون عليه، بل يؤمر بهم إلى النَّار من أوَّل الأمر ، وقيل : بعضُهم يمرُّ وبعضُهم لا يمر . والمارون عليه مختلفون : ـ فمنهم سالم بعمله ناجِ من الوقوع في نار جهنم، وهم على أقسام فمنهم من يجوزه كلمحة البصر، ومنهم من يجوزه كالبرق الخاطف ومنهم كالرّيح العاصف، ومنهم: كالطير، ومنهم: كالجواد السابق، ومنهم من يسعى سعياً، ومنهم من يمشي، : ومنهم من يمرُّ عليه حَبواً على قدر تفاوتهم في الأعمال الصالحة : والإعراض عن المعاصي، فكلُّ من كان أسرع إعراضاً عنها إذا مرَّت على خاطره كان أسرع مروراً، ومنهم من تخدشه كلاليبه فيسقط ولكن يتعلّق بها فيعتدل ويمرّ ويجاوزه بعد أعوام. - ومنهم غير السالم، بل يسقط في نار جهنم، وهم متفاوتون أيضاً بقدر الجرائم، ثمّ منهم من يخلد في النار كالكفَّار، ومنهم: من يخرج منها بعد مدة على حسب ما شاء الله تعالى، وهم المؤمنين بشفاعة النبي أو غيره من الأخيار، وهو من صلى الله عليه وسلم التي أخبر بها الصَّادق، وكلُّ ما كان كذلك فيجب الإيمان به، قال تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَاطَ ) وفي الحديث : ويُضرب الصِّراط بين ظهراني جهنَّم فأكون أنا وأمّتي أَوَّلَ من يجوزه»، وغير ذلك، قال ابن الفاكهاني: (وهو موجود
(And al-Sirat) linguistically: the clear path. And legally: a bridge extended over the surface of Hell between the standing place and Paradise; because Hell is between them. The believers and disbelievers pass over it to cross to Paradise. It is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. Al-Qarafi, following his teacher al-‘Izz, denied that it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword; rather it is wide, because nothing has come that indicates that. And the more apparent view: that it varies in narrowness and width according to deeds. And it is said that the disbelievers do not cross it, but are ordered to the Fire from the beginning; and it is said that some of them cross and some do not. And those who cross it are diverse: Among them are those safe by their deeds, saved from falling into the Fire of Hell, and they are of different categories: some cross it in the blink of an eye, some like a flash of lightning, some like a violent wind, some like a bird, some like a swift horse, some walk, some crawl, according to the difference in their righteous deeds and their turning away from sins. Whoever is quicker in turning away from sins when they occur to his mind is quicker in crossing. Among them are those who are scratched by its hooks and fall, but then cling to them and straighten out and cross after years. And among them are those not safe, but fall into the Fire of Hell, and they also differ according to crimes. Then among them are those who remain forever in the Fire, like the disbelievers; and among them are those who come out of it after a period according to what Allah wills, and they are the believers, by the intercession of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) or other righteous ones. This is among what the truthful one informed of, and everything like that must be believed in. Allah said: {So they hastened to the Path} [Ya-Sin 36:66]. And in the hadith: “And the Bridge will be laid across the middle of Hell, and I and my nation will be the first to cross it.” And other reports. Ibn al-Fakahani said: “It is real.”
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage defines al-Sirat and explains its characteristics and the varying fates of those who cross it. It begins with the linguistic and legal definitions: linguistically, al-Sirat means a clear path; legally, it is a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, between the place of standing and Paradise, because Hell is situated between them. Both believers and disbelievers pass over it in order to reach Paradise. The passage then mentions the traditional description: it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. However, it notes that al-Qarafi, following his teacher al-‘Izz, denied this description, arguing that the bridge is wide, since no evidence indicates otherwise. The author then states the more apparent view: that al-Sirat varies in narrowness and width according to one's deeds. Next, it presents differences of opinion about whether disbelievers cross it: some say they do not cross and are taken directly to the Fire; others say some do cross and some do not. The passage then classifies those who cross into two major types: those who are safe and do not fall, and those who are not safe and fall. The safe ones are further divided into several categories based on the speed of crossing, ranging from the blink of an eye to crawling, corresponding to the speed with which they turn away from sins when thoughts of evil occur. Some of them are scratched by the hooks (khalalib) of the bridge, fall, but then catch hold and eventually cross after years. The unsafe ones fall into Hell, and they too are differentiated according to their crimes. Among them are those who remain forever (the disbelievers) and those who exit after a period (the believers) through intercession of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or other righteous figures. Finally, the passage emphasizes that these details are from authentic reports, and it is obligatory to believe in them. It cites Quranic verse 36:66 and a hadith about the bridge being laid and the Prophet being the first to cross, and quotes Ibn al-Fakahani affirming its reality.

Key Terms
الصراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Sirat is a metaphor for a spiritual state, not a physical bridge.
Correction: This passage affirms it as a real bridge (جسر ممدود) with specific physical characteristics, based on scriptural reports.

Checkpoint
What is the more apparent view regarding the size of al-Sirat?
A) It is as thin as a hair and sharp as a sword for everyone.
B) It is wide and comfortable for all.
C) It varies in narrowness and width according to one's deeds.
D) Only believers see it narrow.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, whose narrowness or width depends on the deeds of the person crossing it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Sirat is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword for some, but wide for others according to their deeds. Considering your own deeds, how wide do you think your path will be? What one deed can you start changing today to ensure a wider crossing?
?
The source says both believers and disbelievers cross al-Sirat, but not all cross safely. Are you confident that your faith will carry you across? What signs of true faith do you see in yourself that guarantee your safe passage?
?
Al-Qarafi denied the traditional description because he saw no evidence. Have you ever rejected a revealed truth because it seemed extreme or uncomfortable? What does this passage teach you about submitting to revelation even when it challenges your reason?

The Crossing of al-Sirat: States of Believers and Disbelievers
Al-Sawi details the diverse experiences of those crossing al-Sirat and the role of deeds and intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different opinions about whether disbelievers cross al-Sirat and the various categories of people who cross it, including their speeds and ultimate fates.

Core Idea
People cross al-Sirat at different speeds based on their piety; disbelievers fall into Hell, while believers may be saved by intercession.

The crossing of al-Sirat is a moment of intense accountability. This passage details the varied experiences of individuals as they traverse the bridge, from the swift passage of the righteous to the fall of the sinful, and clarifies the role of intercession.

Guided Path
1
Review opinions on disbelievers crossing
Note that there are different views: some say disbelievers do not cross at all, others say some do and some don't.
This shows scholarly disagreement on a matter of belief.
2
Identify the two main categories of crossers
The passage divides crossers into safe (saved from falling) and unsafe (those who fall into Hell).
3
Examine the varying speeds among the safe
List the speeds: blink of an eye, lightning, wind, bird, horse, walking, crawling. Each corresponds to how quickly one turns away from sins.
Also note those scratched by hooks who fall but eventually cross.
4
Understand the fate of the unsafe
The unsafe fall into Hell; disbelievers remain forever, while believers exit through intercession after a period.
Intercession is a key doctrine here.

Faith in al-Sirat (the Bridge) and the Sunni Position
Defines al-Sirat, describes crossing states, and affirms Sunni literalist position against Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine of al-Sirat (the Bridge) as a literal reality over Hell, the varying states of people crossing it, and the affirmation of its existence while delegating its true nature to Allah, contrary to the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Al-Sirat is a real bridge over Hell; Ahl al-Sunna affirm it literally, delegating its true nature to Allah.

This lesson introduces al-Sirat, the bridge over Hell that every soul must cross on the Day of Judgment. The passage describes the different ways people cross—swiftly, with difficulty, or falling into the Fire—and emphasizes the Sunni position of affirming its literal reality while delegating the true nature to Allah. It also addresses the Mu'tazila's denial of a physical bridge. By the end, you will grasp how Ahl al-Sunna maintain faith in the unseen realities of the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the content.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail yet.
2
Identify the description of crossing the Bridge
Notice how the passage describes different categories of people: those who pass swiftly, those scratched by hooks, and those who fall. Also note the mention of intercession.
3
Understand the Sunni position
Focus on the concluding part where Ahl al-Sunna affirm the literal reality of the Bridge while delegating knowledge of its essence to Allah. Contrast with the Mu'tazila.
This is the key doctrinal takeaway.
4
Review the commentary on specific phrases
Look at the explanations of 'klalib' (hooks) and 'bayn dhahrani jahannam' (between the two sides of Hell) to see how scholars interpret the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالنشر والصراط على خاطره كان أسرع مروراً، ومنهم من تخدشه كلاليبه فيسقط ولكن يتعلّق بها فيعتدل ويمرّ ويجاوزه بعد أعوام. عصاة - ومنهم غير السالم، بل يسقط في نار جهنم، وهم متفاوتون أيضاً بقدر الجرائم، ثمّ منهم من يخلد في النار كالكفَّار، ومنهم: من يخرج منها بعد مدة على حسب ما شاء الله تعالى، وهم المؤمنين بشفاعة النبي أو غيره من الأخيار، وهو من صلى الله عليه وسلم التي أخبر بها الصَّادق، وكلُّ ما كان كذلك فيجب الإيمان به، قال تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَاطَ﴾. وفي الحديث: ويُضرب الصِّراط بين ظهراني جهنَّم فأكون أنا وأمّتي أَوَّلَ من يجوزه، وغير ذلك، قال ابن الفاكهاني: (وهو موجود قوله: (من تخدشه كلاليبه أي وهي في حافتيه معلقة مأمورة بأخذ من أمرت به؛ كشوك السَّعدان كما ورد ذلك. قوله: (كالكفَّار) الكاف استقصائيَّة والأوضح أن يقول وهم الكفَّار. قوله: (بين ظهراني جهنَّم): تثنية ظهر، والمراد به الجانب؛ أي: بين جانبيها، أو النون والياء زائدتان للمبالغة، والمعنى: بين أجزاء ظهر جهنَّم. والأخبار عنه صحيحة) انتهى. فذهب أهل السُّنَّة إلى إبقائها على ظاهرها مع تفويض علم حقيقته إلى الله تعالى خلافاً للمعتزلة وقال بعضهم: إنّه سيوجد عند الحاجة إليه.
Faith in the Resurrection and the Bridge. Some pass over it swiftly, some are scratched by its hooks and fall but cling to them and then balance and cross after years. Sinners - and among them are not safe, but fall into the fire of Hell, and they vary according to sins; then among them are those who remain in the Fire forever like the disbelievers, and among them are those who come out of it after a period according to the will of Allah Almighty, and they are the believers through the intercession of the Prophet or other righteous persons, and he is the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) about whom the truthful one informed, and everything that is like that must be believed in. Allah Almighty said: 'Then they rushed to the bridge.' And in the hadith: 'The bridge will be set across the middle of Hell, and I and my nation will be the first to cross it,' and other [hadiths]. Ibn al-Fakahani said: 'It exists — his saying: "its hooks scratch him" meaning they are hung on its sides, commanded to seize whom they are commanded to, like the thorns of Sa'dan as reported.' His saying: 'like the disbelievers' — the kaf is inclusive, and clearer would be to say 'and they are the disbelievers. His saying: 'between the two sides of Hell' — dual of 'zahr', meaning side, i.e., between its two sides, or the nun and ya are extra for emphasis, meaning: between the parts of the back of Hell. And the reports about it are authentic.' End. So Ahl al-Sunna maintained its literal meaning while delegating knowledge of its true reality to Allah Almighty, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And some of them said: It will come into existence when needed.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage defines al-Sirat as the bridge over Hell, describes the varying states of people crossing it (some swift, some scratched by hooks and then balance, some fall into fire), and categorizes sinners: some remain forever (disbelievers), some exit after a period (believers through intercession). It cites Quranic verse (36:66) and a hadith stating the Prophet and his nation will cross first. Then it explains the commentary on specific phrases: the hooks are like thorns commanded to seize the intended; 'kuffar' is an inclusive kaf; 'between the two sides of Hell' is interpreted as its sides or parts. Ibn al-Fakahani affirms the reality of the bridge and the authenticity of reports. The passage concludes with the Sunni position: affirming the literal reality while delegating the true nature to Allah, contrary to the Mu'tazila who deny its existence or postpone it.

الكلاليب
الشفاعة
أهل السنة
المعتزلة
تفويض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila deny the literal existence of al-Sirat, claiming it is metaphorical or will only exist at the time of need.
Correction: The passage affirms that Ahl al-Sunna hold al-Sirat as a literal reality over Hell, with authentic reports about it, while delegating its true nature to Allah.

Checkpoint
What is the position of Ahl al-Sunna regarding the bridge (al-Sirat)?
A) They affirm its literal reality but delegate knowledge of its true nature to Allah.
B) They interpret it metaphorically.
C) They deny its existence.
D) They say it will exist only at the time of need.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna affirm the literal reality of al-Sirat, a bridge over Hell, while delegating its true nature to Allah, and reject the Mu'tazila's denial of its existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine crossing al-Sirat, what is the state of your heart today? Are you among those who will pass swiftly, or does the thought of the hooks terrify you? What does your daily obedience to Allah reveal about your readiness?
?
If you were to fall into the Fire because of your sins, would you trust in the intercession of the Prophet? Have you truly sought his intercession by following his sunna and avoiding what he warned against?
?
Ahl al-Sunna delegate the true nature of al-Sirat to Allah. Do you accept this unseen reality without your intellect fully grasping it, or do you find yourself questioning the literal truth of the reports? What does that say about the strength of your iman in the unseen?

Faith in al-Mizan and Its Scriptural Proofs
Affirms the reality of al-Mizan, its scriptural proofs, and refutes Mu'tazila denials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of al-Mizan (the Balance) as a literal scale that weighs deeds, its scriptural proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and the Mu'tazila objections.

Core Idea
The Balance is real – the Quran and Sunnah affirm it, and its hadiths are mutawatir.

This lesson introduces the Islamic belief in al-Mizan, the Balance that will weigh deeds on the Day of Judgment. The author affirms its reality before the Bridge and provides scriptural evidence. He also addresses the Mu'tazila who deny or reinterpret it, showing the mainstream Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the affirmation, then the refutation of Mu'tazila, then the scriptural evidence.
2
Understand the definition of al-Mizan
The passage defines al-Mizan as a device that weighs deeds, placed before the Bridge. Consider why this is a literal belief in Sunni Islam.
3
Appreciate the strength of proof
The author says the hadiths on al-Mizan have reached tawatur (mass transmission), making the belief certain. Locate the reference to tawatur in the text.
4
Analyze the Mu'tazila position
The passage divides the Mu'tazila into two groups: absolute deniers and those who postpone existence. Ask why they would reinterpret clear texts.
5
Review the Quranic evidence
Read the cited verse from Surah al-Anbiya' (21:47). See how the author uses it as direct proof for the literal scales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالميزان (والميزان) وهو قبل الصّراط توزن به أعمال العباد ودلّ عليه الكتاب في آيات متعدّدة والسُّنَّة حتى بلغت أحاديثه مبلغَ التَّواتر. قوله: (خلافاً للمعتزلة): أي: فإنَّهم يقولون بعدم وجوده ويؤولون ما ورد. وقوله: وقال بعضهم: أي: بعض المعتزلة، فهم افترقوا فرقتين؛ فرقة تنكره رأساً، وفرقة تنكر وجوده الآن ويقولون: يوجد عند الحاجة إليه. قوله: (في آياتٍ متعدّدة) منها قوله تعالى: (وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ لِيَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ) فَمَن ثَقُلَتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَتِّيكَ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَيكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنفُسَهُم بِمَا كَانُوا بِآيَاتِنَا يَظْلِمُونَ ... إلى غير ذلك من الآيات.
Faith in the Balance. (The Balance) is before the Bridge; by it the deeds of servants are weighed. The Book and the Sunnah indicate it, to the extent that its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur. His saying: 'Contrary to the Mu'tazila' — meaning: they say it does not exist and interpret what has been reported. And his saying: 'And some of them said' — meaning: some of the Mu'tazila, for they split into two groups: a group denies it completely, and a group denies its existence now and says: it will exist when needed. His saying: 'In multiple verses' — including His Almighty saying: 'And We shall set up the scales of justice for the Day of Resurrection, then whoever's scales are heavy, those are the successful, and whoever's scales are light, those are the ones who have lost their souls because they used to wrong Our signs' ... and other such verses.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage defines al-Mizan as the balance that comes before al-Sirat (the bridge), used to weigh the deeds of servants. It asserts that both the Quran and Sunnah provide evidence for it, with hadiths reaching the level of tawatur (mass transmission). It then addresses the Mu'tazila opposition: they deny its existence and interpret the relevant texts allegorically. The text mentions that some Mu'tazila are further divided—one group denies it entirely, another denies its current existence but says it will appear when needed. Finally, it cites Quranic evidence, specifically verse 47 of Surah al-Anbiya' and verses 8-9 of Surah al-A'raf, as proof for the reality of the scales.

Misconception: Some people think al-Mizan is metaphorical or symbolic.
Correction: The passage affirms it as a literal scale that weighs deeds, supported by mutawatir hadith and Quranic verses.

Checkpoint
What is the position of the Mu'tazila regarding the Balance (al-Mizan) according to this passage?
A) They affirm its literal reality.
B) They are divided: some deny it entirely, others deny its current existence.
C) They unanimously postpone its existence.
D) They interpret it as symbolic of deeds.

Key Takeaway
The Balance (al-Mizan) is a literal scale that weighs deeds on the Day of Judgment, proven by mutawatir hadith and Quranic verses, contrary to Mu'tazila denials.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Mu'tazila denied the Balance because it didn't fit their rational framework. Are there any truths from revelation that you are tempted to reinterpret or explain away to suit your own comfort or logic? What are they, and what would it cost you to submit fully?
?
The Balance is before the Bridge. Have you ever considered the order of events on Judgment Day? If you knew your deeds are weighed first, would you change what you prioritize in your daily life? What specific action can you take today to ensure your scale is heavy?
