The Obligation of Belief in the Balance
Al-Sawi defines al-Mizan and establishes its scriptural basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-Mizan, its scriptural evidence, and why believing in it literally is obligatory even without knowing its exact nature.

Core Idea
Belief in the Balance is obligatory because both Qur'an and Sunnah affirm it literally.

Al-Sawi begins by stating the fundamental belief in the Balance (al-Mizan) as a real scale placed before the Path (al-Sirat). He immediately grounds this belief in scriptural evidence, noting that the Qur'an mentions it in multiple verses and the Sunnah provides hadiths reaching the level of mass transmission (tawatur). This lesson will show you how the author establishes the obligation of literal belief while acknowledging our limited knowledge of its substance.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and evidence
Start by reading the Arabic passage from 'الإيمان بالميزان' to 'وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره'. Notice how Al-Sawi defines the Balance, then immediately provides proof from the Qur'an and Sunnah.
The phrase 'بلغت أحاديثه مبلغَ التَّواتر' indicates the high level of certainty from prophetic reports.
2
Identify the obligation of literal belief
The author states 'الحَمْلُ على الحقيقة ممكن فيجب الإيمان به' – since carrying the texts literally is possible, faith is required. Understand that this is a key principle: when a literal interpretation is possible, it must be followed.
This principle is used to reject metaphorical interpretations.
3
Recognize the limitation of knowledge
Al-Sawi adds 'وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره' – we do not know the reality of its substance. This shows that belief does not require full comprehension.
The description of the two pans (luminous and dark) is a later addition; here the focus is on the obligation itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالميزان (والميزان) وهو قبل الصّراط توزن به أعمال العباد ودلّ عليه الكتاب في آيات متعدّدة والسُّنَّة حتى بلغت أحاديثه مبلغَ التَّواتر، ورد. قوله : (خلافاً للمعتزلة) : أي : فإنَّهم يقولون: بعدم وجوده ويؤولون [؟] . وقوله : وقال بعضهم :أي: بعض المعتزلة، فهم افترقوا فرقتين؛ فرقة تنكره رأساً، وفرقة تنكر وجوده الآن ويقولون : يوجد عند الحاجة إليه . والحَمْلُ على الحقيقة ممكن فيجب الإيمان به وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره ، والتَّأويلُ بتمام العَدْل كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة عناد ومكابرة. والصَّحيحُ أنّه ميزان واحد لجميع الأمم، ولجميع الأعمال، والجَمْعُ في قوله تعالى : (وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ ) للتعظيم . وإِنَّ خِفَّة الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدُّنيا، وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم. قوله : ( وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره) : أي : فغاية ما نعرف منه كفَّتان نورانيَّة للحسنات، وظلمانية للسَّيِّئات. قوله : ( عناد ومكابرة) أي : لأنَّه إذا أمكن الحمل على الحقيقة؛ فلا يعدل عنها، والعدول عنها بارتكاب المجاز تكلُّف ومكابرة. قوله : (التَّعظيم) أي: فهو نظير : (رَبِّ ارْجِعُونِ) . قوله : (على صورته في الدُّنيا) :أي فالخفيفة تطيش وتعلو، والثّقيلة تسقط لأسفل. قوله : ( وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم): أي: فيوزن غير الكفر من السَّيِّئات؛ ليجازوا عليها بالعقاب زيادة على عذاب الكفر، وحسناتهم التي لا تتوقف على نيَّةٍ كالعتق والوقف، وصلة الرحم، يخفف عنهم بذلك من عذاب غير الكفر ؛ فتوزن أعمالهم لأجل ذلك لا للنَّجاة من عذاب الكفر.
Faith in the Balance: The Balance is before the Path (al-Sirat); deeds of servants are weighed by it, and the Book has indicated it in multiple verses and the Sunnah to the extent that its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur, and it is reported. His saying: (Contrary to the Mu'tazila): meaning: they say it does not exist and they interpret [?]. And his saying: And some of them said: meaning some of the Mu'tazila, for they split into two groups: a group denies it outright, and a group denies its existence now but says it will exist at the time of need. Carrying it upon literal meaning is possible, so faith in it is obligatory even if we do not know the reality of its substance, and interpreting it as complete justice as the Mu'tazila held is obstinacy and arrogance. And the correct view is that it is one scale for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in His saying: 'And We shall set up the scales of justice' is for glorification. And the lightness and heaviness of what is weighed is according to its form in this world, and the deeds of the disbelievers are weighed. His saying: (Even if we do not know the reality of its substance): meaning the utmost we know of it is two pans: one luminous for good deeds, and one dark for evil deeds. His saying: (obstinacy and arrogance): meaning because when carrying upon literal meaning is possible, one should not deviate from it, and deviating from it by resorting to metaphor is affectation and arrogance. His saying: (glorification): meaning it is similar to 'Lord, send me back'. His saying: (according to its form in this world): meaning the light one floats and rises, and the heavy one falls downward. His saying: (And the deeds of the disbelievers are weighed): meaning, so what is other than disbelief of evil deeds is weighed so that they may be requited with punishment in addition to the punishment of disbelief, and their good deeds that do not depend on intention, such as freeing slaves, endowments, and maintaining family ties, by that they are relieved of the punishment of non-disbelief; so their deeds are weighed for that reason, not for salvation from the punishment of disbelief.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition of the Islamic belief in al-Mizan (the Balance) on Judgment Day, combining definition, proof, refutation of opposing views, and detailed explanation. The author begins by stating the subject: 'Faith in the Balance.' He then defines it as a scale placed before the Sirat (the bridge) by which the deeds of servants are weighed. The proof is given from both the Qur'an (multiple verses) and the Sunnah, whose hadiths have reached tawatur (mass transmission). He notes that it is 'reported' (ward), meaning it is established. Next, he addresses the position of the Mu'tazila, who deny the Balance or reinterpret it. He quotes a comment: 'Contrary to the Mu'tazila' and explains that they say it does not exist (some deny it outright) or that it does not exist now but will exist at the time of need. This division shows their inconsistent stance. The author then asserts the Sunni position: carrying the texts upon their literal meaning (al-hamlu 'ala al-haqiqah) is possible, so it is obligatory to believe in the Balance as a real entity, even if we do not know the exact nature (haqiqah) of its substance. He condemns the Mu'tazila interpretation as 'complete justice' (tamām al-'adl) as 'obstinacy and arrogance' (inād wa mukābarah), because when a literal meaning is possible, resorting to metaphorical interpretation (ta'wīl) is unnecessary and forced. He then clarifies that the correct view is that it is one scale for all nations and all deeds; the plural form in the Qur'anic verse 'We shall set up the scales' is for glorification, not to indicate multiple scales. Further details are given: the lightness and heaviness of the deeds correspond to their form in this world (i.e., the actual nature of the deeds). The deeds of disbelievers are also weighed, but for a different purpose: their evil deeds (other than disbelief) are weighed to increase their punishment, while their good deeds that do not require intention (like freeing slaves, endowments, maintaining family ties) are weighed to reduce punishment for non-disbelief (but not for salvation from the punishment of disbelief itself). The author also provides a physical description: the scale has two pans, one luminous for good deeds and one dark for evil deeds, and light things float up while heavy ones fall. This confirms the literal nature of the Balance.

Key Terms
الميزان
الصراط
الحقيقة
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance is only metaphorical (majaz) or does not exist now.
Correction: The texts are to be taken literally because that is possible; belief is obligatory even if we do not know its exact nature.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the obligatory belief in al-Mizan?
A) Reason alone proves its existence.
B) The Qur'an and Sunnah indicate it, and literal interpretation is possible.
C) All scholars agree on it.
D) It is mentioned in a single verse of the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Balance is obligatory because the Qur'an and Sunnah affirm it literally, and we do not need to know its exact nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you accept the Balance as a literal reality even though you cannot imagine its substance, or do you find yourself inclined to explain it away? What evidence from this passage can you point to that forces your submission to this truth?
?
Al-Sawi says faith in the Balance is obligatory even without knowing its nature. Is your faith in the unseen matters of the afterlife equally firm, or do you demand explanations that satisfy your intellect before you submit? Where are you currently struggling to accept a revealed truth that seems beyond your comprehension?
?
The Mu'tazila's error was not just denial but obstinacy—they insisted on their interpretation despite clear texts. Do you ever reject a clear command or belief because it clashes with your sense of justice or reason? What would it cost you to simply say, 'I hear and I obey' even when you don't fully understand?

Refuting Mu'tazila Interpretations of the Balance
Al-Sawi refutes the Mu'tazila positions on the Balance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila positions on the Balance, the principle of preferring literal meaning (haqiqah) over metaphorical interpretation (majaz), and why their view is considered obstinacy.

Core Idea
Interpretation departing from literal meaning is arrogant when literal is possible.

Al-Sawi addresses the Mu'tazila who reject the literal Balance, either denying it entirely or postponing its existence. He firmly states that when a literal interpretation is possible, resorting to metaphor or reinterpretation is unjustified. This lesson examines the specific Mu'tazila claims and the author's refutation based on the principle of 'haml ala al-haqiqah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Mu'tazila groups
Read the portion starting from 'خلافاً للمعتزلة' to 'يوجد عند الحاجة إليه'. Notice the two positions: outright denial and postponement of existence.
The word 'فرقتين' shows they split into two factions.
2
Understand the principle of literal meaning
Al-Sawi says 'والحَمْلُ على الحقيقة ممكن' – when it is possible to take the text literally, that must be done. This is a key usul al-fiqh principle.
This principle is used to reject ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation).
3
Analyze the charge of obstinacy
The author calls the Mu'tazila interpretation 'عناد ومكابرة' (obstinacy and arrogance). Reflect on why deviating from literal meaning when possible is considered blameworthy.
The commentary explains: 'لأنَّه إذا أمكن الحمل على الحقيقة؛ فلا يعدل عنها'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Details of the Balance and Weighing of Deeds
Al-Sawi provides details about the Balance's nature and the weighing process.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Balance is one for all nations, its description with two pans, how deeds are weighed, and why the deeds of disbelievers are also weighed.

Core Idea
The single Balance has luminous and dark pans; deeds of believers and disbelievers are weighed differently.

After establishing the reality of the Balance, Al-Sawi provides further details: there is only one scale for all nations (the plural in the Qur'an is for glorification), it has two pans (luminous for good deeds, dark for evil), and even the deeds of disbelievers are weighed for specific purposes. This lesson unpacks these specifics, showing the comprehensive nature of divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Affirm the oneness of the Balance
Read from 'والصَّحيحُ أنّه ميزان واحد' to 'للتعظيم'. Notice that the plural 'موازين' is interpreted as glorification, not multiple scales.
This opposes the view that there are many scales for different deeds.
2
Understand the physical description
Read 'وإنَّ خِفَّة الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدُّنيا' and the commentary on two pans: one luminous for good, one dark for evil. Light deeds float up, heavy deeds fall.
This literal description underscores the physical reality of the scale.
3
Examine the weighing of disbelievers' deeds
Read the final part from 'وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم'. Identify that their deeds are weighed to increase punishment for sins and to lighten punishment for good deeds (like freeing slaves), but not for salvation from disbelief.
This shows divine justice: even disbelievers benefit from good deeds in this world's terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالميزان (والميزان) وهو قبل الصّراط توزن به أعمال العباد ودلّ عليه الكتاب في آيات متعدّدة والسُّنَّة حتى بلغت أحاديثه مبلغَ التَّواتر، ورد. قوله : (خلافاً للمعتزلة) : أي : فإنَّهم يقولون: بعدم وجوده ويؤولون [؟] . وقوله : وقال بعضهم :أي: بعض المعتزلة، فهم افترقوا فرقتين؛ فرقة تنكره رأساً، وفرقة تنكر وجوده الآن ويقولون : يوجد عند الحاجة إليه . والحَمْلُ على الحقيقة ممكن فيجب الإيمان به وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره ، والتَّأويلُ بتمام العَدْل كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة عناد ومكابرة. والصَّحيحُ أنّه ميزان واحد لجميع الأمم، ولجميع الأعمال، والجَمْعُ في قوله تعالى : (وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ ) للتعظيم . وإِنَّ خِفَّة الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدُّنيا، وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم. قوله : ( وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره) : أي : فغاية ما نعرف منه كفَّتان نورانيَّة للحسنات، وظلمانية للسَّيِّئات. قوله : ( عناد ومكابرة) أي : لأنَّه إذا أمكن الحمل على الحقيقة؛ فلا يعدل عنها، والعدول عنها بارتكاب المجاز تكلُّف ومكابرة. قوله : (التَّعظيم) أي: فهو نظير : (رَبِّ ارْجِعُونِ) . قوله : (على صورته في الدُّنيا) :أي فالخفيفة تطيش وتعلو، والثّقيلة تسقط لأسفل. قوله : ( وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم): أي: فيوزن غير الكفر من السَّيِّئات؛ ليجازوا عليها بالعقاب زيادة على عذاب الكفر، وحسناتهم التي لا تتوقف على نيَّةٍ كالعتق والوقف، وصلة الرحم، يخفف عنهم بذلك من عذاب غير الكفر ؛ فتوزن أعمالهم لأجل ذلك لا للنَّجاة من عذاب الكفر.
Faith in the Balance: The Balance is before the Path (al-Sirat); deeds of servants are weighed by it, and the Book has indicated it in multiple verses and the Sunnah to the extent that its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur, and it is reported. His saying: (Contrary to the Mu'tazila): meaning: they say it does not exist and they interpret [?]. And his saying: And some of them said: meaning some of the Mu'tazila, for they split into two groups: a group denies it outright, and a group denies its existence now but says it will exist at the time of need. Carrying it upon literal meaning is possible, so faith in it is obligatory even if we do not know the reality of its substance, and interpreting it as complete justice as the Mu'tazila held is obstinacy and arrogance. And the correct view is that it is one scale for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in His saying: 'And We shall set up the scales of justice' is for glorification. And the lightness and heaviness of what is weighed is according to its form in this world, and the deeds of the disbelievers are weighed. His saying: (Even if we do not know the reality of its substance): meaning the utmost we know of it is two pans: one luminous for good deeds, and one dark for evil deeds. His saying: (obstinacy and arrogance): meaning because when carrying upon literal meaning is possible, one should not deviate from it, and deviating from it by resorting to metaphor is affectation and arrogance. His saying: (glorification): meaning it is similar to 'Lord, send me back'. His saying: (according to its form in this world): meaning the light one floats and rises, and the heavy one falls downward. His saying: (And the deeds of the disbelievers are weighed): meaning, so what is other than disbelief of evil deeds is weighed so that they may be requited with punishment in addition to the punishment of disbelief, and their good deeds that do not depend on intention, such as freeing slaves, endowments, and maintaining family ties, by that they are relieved of the punishment of non-disbelief; so their deeds are weighed for that reason, not for salvation from the punishment of disbelief.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition of the Islamic belief in al-Mizan (the Balance) on Judgment Day, combining definition, proof, refutation of opposing views, and detailed explanation. The author begins by stating the subject: 'Faith in the Balance.' He then defines it as a scale placed before the Sirat (the bridge) by which the deeds of servants are weighed. The proof is given from both the Qur'an (multiple verses) and the Sunnah, whose hadiths have reached tawatur (mass transmission). He notes that it is 'reported' (ward), meaning it is established. Next, he addresses the position of the Mu'tazila, who deny the Balance or reinterpret it. He quotes a comment: 'Contrary to the Mu'tazila' and explains that they say it does not exist (some deny it outright) or that it does not exist now but will exist at the time of need. This division shows their inconsistent stance. The author then asserts the Sunni position: carrying the texts upon their literal meaning (al-hamlu 'ala al-haqiqah) is possible, so it is obligatory to believe in the Balance as a real entity, even if we do not know the exact nature (haqiqah) of its substance. He condemns the Mu'tazila interpretation as 'complete justice' (tamām al-'adl) as 'obstinacy and arrogance' (inād wa mukābarah), because when a literal meaning is possible, resorting to metaphorical interpretation (ta'wīl) is unnecessary and forced. He then clarifies that the correct view is that it is one scale for all nations and all deeds; the plural form in the Qur'anic verse 'We shall set up the scales' is for glorification, not to indicate multiple scales. Further details are given: the lightness and heaviness of the deeds correspond to their form in this world (i.e., the actual nature of the deeds). The deeds of disbelievers are also weighed, but for a different purpose: their evil deeds (other than disbelief) are weighed to increase their punishment, while their good deeds that do not require intention (like freeing slaves, endowments, maintaining family ties) are weighed to reduce punishment for non-disbelief (but not for salvation from the punishment of disbelief itself). The author also provides a physical description: the scale has two pans, one luminous for good deeds and one dark for evil deeds, and light things float up while heavy ones fall. This confirms the literal nature of the Balance.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: They are weighed for purposes of punishment adjustment, but not for salvation from disbelief.

Key Takeaway
The one Balance has two pans and even disbelievers' deeds are weighed to adjust punishment, but faith is necessary for salvation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you knew that every sin you commit darkens a pan that will be placed on the Balance, would you still treat that sin as 'too small to matter'? What are you going to do about it starting now?
?
The deeds of disbelievers can lighten their punishment but not save them from disbelief. Are you relying on your good deeds alone, or have you truly placed your faith in Allah as the only means of salvation?

Belief in the Scale and Refutation of Ta'wil
Al-Sawi states the obligation of belief in the scale and rejects metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Sawi insists on literal interpretation of the scale and rejects the Mu'tazila's metaphorical interpretation, and what the correct belief entails.

Core Idea
The scale is real; literal interpretation is obligatory even without knowing its essence.

Al-Sawi tackles a key eschatological belief: the scale. He faces a challenge: the Mu'tazila interpret it metaphorically. He argues that since literal meaning is possible, it must be accepted. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the details of the correct belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow: obligation, refutation, clarification, and details.
The passage is concise; each sentence carries doctrinal weight.
2
Identify Al-Sawi's main claim and argument
Find the sentence where Al-Sawi states that literal interpretation is possible, so belief is obligatory. Note how he rejects ta'wil.
He calls the Mu'tazila's approach 'stubbornness and obstinacy'.
3
Examine the clarifications
Notice the three clarifications: the scale is one, plural is for glorification, and lightness/heaviness corresponds to this world. Understand why these matter.
These details refute common misunderstandings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالميزان والحَمْلُ على الحقيقة ممكن فيجب الإيمان به وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره ، والتَّأويلُ بتمام العَدْل كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة عناد ومكابرة. والصَّحيحُ أنّه ميزان واحد لجميع الأمم، ولجميع الأعمال، والجَمْعُ في قوله تعالى : (وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَزِينَ الْقِسْطَ ) (١) للتعظيم . وإِنَّ خِفَّة الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدُّنيا، وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم
Belief in the scale [is obligatory], and literal interpretation is possible, so belief in it is obligatory even if we do not know the reality of its substance. Ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation) as done by the Mu'tazila is stubbornness and obstinacy. The correct view is that it is one scale for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in His statement: 'And We shall set up the scales of justice' (Quran 21:47) is for glorification. And the lightness of what is weighed and its heaviness are as they were in this world, and the disbelievers' deeds are weighed.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of the required belief in the scale (mizan) and a refutation of those who interpret it metaphorically. Al-Sawi begins by stating that belief in the scale is obligatory. He argues that since a literal interpretation is possible, one must adhere to it, even if the true nature of the scale is unknown to us. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for their ta'wil, calling it 'stubbornness and obstinacy'. Next, he clarifies that the correct belief is that the scale is one for all nations and all deeds, and that the plural form 'mawazin' in the Quranic verse is for glorification, not indicating multiple scales. Finally, he explains two characteristics: (1) the lightness or heaviness of deeds on the scale corresponds to their state in this world, and (2) the deeds of disbelievers are also weighed, implying that they are not exempt from this reckoning.

Correction: Al-Sawi insists that literal interpretation is possible and therefore obligatory; not knowing the essence does not justify metaphorical interpretation.

?
When you encounter a matter of faith that your intellect cannot fully grasp, do you humbly submit to the literal meaning revealed, or do you find yourself tempted to reinterpret it to fit your understanding, like the Mu'tazila did with the scale?
?
The scale weighs deeds exactly as they were in this world—no exaggeration, no discount. Imagine your own deeds on that scale right now: what would tip it? What can you do this week to add weight to the side of good?

What We Know of the Scale and Rejecting Ta'wil
Al-Sawi clarifies known attributes of the scale and defends literal interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that despite not knowing the scale's substance, we know its two pans are associated with deeds, and that resorting to metaphorical interpretation when literal is possible is obstinacy.

Core Idea
Literal interpretation is preferred; metaphor without necessity is stubbornness.

Al-Sawi continues his commentary on the nature of the scale (mizan) that will weigh deeds. While its exact substance is unknown, he clarifies what is known about it. He then defends the literal understanding against those who resort to metaphorical interpretation, arguing that such ta'wil is a form of obstinacy when a literal meaning is perfectly acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the two separate glosses: one explaining what we know of the scale, the other condemning ta'wil.
2
Understand the first gloss
Identify what Al-Sawi says we do know about the scale: it has two pans, luminous for good deeds and dark for evil. This shows that even if the essence is unknown, effects and attributes are known.
This guards against the misconception that nothing is known.
3
Understand the second gloss
Al-Sawi argues that when literal interpretation is possible, deviating to metaphorical is 'cumbersome and obstinate'. Reflect on the reasoning: necessity dictates sticking to literal.
This refutes the Mu'tazila who interpreted the scale metaphorically.
4
Connect to broader kalam method
Consider how this passage exemplifies the principle of interpreting religious texts literally unless there is a compelling reason to do otherwise.
This is a key principle in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره) : أي : فغاية ما نعرف منه كفَّتان نورانيَّة للحسنات، وظلمانية للسَّيِّئات. قوله : ( عناد ومكابرة) أي : لأنَّه إذا أمكن الحمل على الحقيقة؛ فلا يعدل عنها، والعدول عنها بارتكاب المجاز تكلُّف ومكابرة.

His saying: '(stubbornness and obstinacy)' means: because when literal interpretation is possible, one should not deviate from it, and deviating from it by resorting to metaphor is cumbersome and obstinate.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage contains two glosses explaining phrases from the original text. The first gloss interprets the phrase 'even if we do not know the reality of its substance'. Al-Sawi clarifies that despite our ignorance of the scale's exact essence, we do know that it consists of two pans: one luminous, representing good deeds, and one dark, representing evil deeds. The second gloss explains the accusation of 'stubbornness and obstinacy' against the Mu'tazila. The reasoning is that since a literal interpretation of the scale is possible and unproblematic, there is no need to resort to metaphorical interpretation. Doing so without necessity is a futile effort and an act of obstinacy.

The Scale's Plural for Glorification and Lightness/Heaviness
Al-Sawi's glosses on plural form and physical behavior of the scale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose of the plural form 'al-mawazin' and the physical analogy of deeds on the scale.

Core Idea
The plural form of the scale is for glorification, not multiplicity.

Al-Sawi offers two brief but important clarifications about the scale. First, he explains why the Quran uses the plural 'mawazin' when referring to a single scale; it is a form of glorification, similar to other Quranic examples. Second, he describes how the scale's operation mirrors this-worldly physics: light deeds rise, heavy deeds fall.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the two separate glosses.
The passage references Quran 23:99 as an analogy.
2
Understand the first gloss: plural for glorification
Al-Sawi says the plural 'mawazin' is for ta'zim (glorification), not indicating multiple scales. He compares it to 'rabb irji'oon' where the plural is used for a single person as honorific.
This interpretation avoids the implication of many scales.
3
Understand the second gloss: light rises, heavy falls
Al-Sawi explains that a light deed will flutter upward and a heavy deed will sink downward, just as in this world. This is a physical metaphor for the weighing of deeds.
The phrase 'as it was in this world' connects the afterlife to worldly experience.
4
Connect to the central idea
Both glosses clarify how we should understand the Quranic description of the scale: it is one scale, used in a glorifying plural, and its operation is analogous to physical weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (التَّعظيم) أي: فهو نظير : رَبِّ ارْجِعُونِ ) (۲) قوله : (على صورته في الدُّنيا :أي فالخفيفة تطيش وتعلو، والثّقيلة تسقط لأسفل.
His saying: '(for glorification)' means: it is similar to 'Lord, send me back' (Quran 23:99). His saying: ('as it was in this world') means: so the light [deed] flies and rises, and the heavy [deed] falls downwards.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage contains two brief glosses. The first explains that the plural form 'al-mawazin' (the scales) in the verse is used for glorification (ta'zim), not to indicate multiple scales. Al-Sawi compares it to the Quranic phrase 'Lord, send me back' (rabb irji'oon), which uses the plural form for a single person as a form of glorification. The second gloss explains the phrase 'as it was in this world' regarding the lightness or heaviness of deeds. Al-Sawi clarifies that on the Day of Judgment, a light deed will rise and flutter upward, while a heavy deed will sink downward, mirroring the behavior of light and heavy objects in this world.

Weighing Disbelievers' Deeds and the Abu Lahab Proof
Al-Sawi explains why disbelievers' deeds are weighed and uses Abu Lahab as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why disbelievers' deeds are weighed, what deeds are weighed, and how the story of Abu Lahab serves as a proof that even disbelievers can receive temporary alleviation for worldly good deeds.

Core Idea
Disbelievers' deeds are weighed for justice, not for salvation—even Abu Lahab gets a Monday break.

In this passage, Al-Sawi tackles a theological nuance: if disbelievers are eternally punished, why are their deeds weighed? He explains that the weighing affects the severity of punishment, not the removal of disbelief itself. The famous account of Abu Lahab's alleviation every Monday provides striking proof that even a disbeliever can benefit from a good deed done out of joy for the Prophet's birth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the argument in full. Let Al-Sawi's own words establish the framework before you analyze.
2
Identify the types of deeds weighed
Notice that Al-Sawi specifies which deeds are weighed: sins other than disbelief, and good deeds that do not require intention (like freeing slaves). Understand why these are singled out.
3
Understand the purpose of weighing
The weighing is meant to increase punishment for sins or reduce punishment for non-disbelief matters, but never to save the disbeliever from the eternal punishment of disbelief. This is the core principle.
The phrase 'لا للنَّجاة من عذاب الكفر' is key.
4
Examine the proof and its implications
Study the Abu Lahab story and the poetic conclusion. How does it support the principle? What does it tell us about the value of rejoicing in the Prophet's birth?
The two quotes drive home the lesson for believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإنَّ الكفَّار توزن أعمالهم: أي: فيوزن غير الكفر من السَّيِّئات؛ ليجازوا عليها بالعقاب زيادة على عذاب الكفر، وحسناتهم التي لا تتوقف على نيَّةٍ كالعتق والوقف، وصلة الرحم، من عذاب غير الكفر ; فتوزن أعمالهم لأجل ذلك لا للنَّجاة من عذاب الكفر؛ فإنَّه لا يخفّف عنهم ولا ينقطع، بدليل: أنَّ أبا لهب جُوزي بالتخفيف؛ بسبب عتقه جاريته التي بشرته بولادته له. وقيل : حسناته التي فعلها يجازى عليها في الدُّنيا؛ كسعة الرزق وعافية البدن، ولا يجازي عليها في الآخرة أصلاً، ويكون ثمرة وزن عمله التشديد في عذاب الكفر وعدمه ; لأنَّ الكفَّار يتفاوتون في العذاب، بقدر تفاوتهم في الكفر. أخرجه البخاري (۵۱۰۱) قال الإمام ابن الجزري في كتابه عرف التعريف بالمولد الشريف» (ص۲۲): (قد رئي أبو لهب بعد موته في النوم، فقيل له : ما حالك؟ فقال: في النار، إلا أنه يخفف عني كل ليلة اثنين وأمصُّ من بين إصبعي ماءً بقدر هذا – وأشار لرأس إصبعه - وأن ذلك بإعتاقي لثويبة عندما بشرتني بولادة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وبإرضاعها له. فإذا كان أبو لهب الكافر الذي نزل القرآن بذمه ; جوزي في النار بفرحه ليلة مولد النبي به ، فما حال المسلم الموحد من أمة محمد يسر بمولده، ويبذل ما تصل إليه قدرته في محبته لعمري؛ إنما يكون جزاؤه من الله الكريم أن يدخله بفضله جنات النعيم). وقال الحافظ شمس الدین ابن ناصر الدين الدمشقى في كتابه المسمى «مورد الصادي في مولد الهادي ( ص (٢٦) : قد صح أن أبا لهب يخفف عنه عذاب النار في مثل يوم الاثنين لإعتاقه ثويبة ; سروراً بميلاد النبي ، ثم أنشد: إذا كان هذا كافراً جاء ذمه وتبت يداه في الجحيم مخلدا أتى أنه في يوم الاثنين دائماً يخفف عنه للسرور بأحمدا فما الظن بالعبد الذي كان عمره بأحمد مسروراً ومات موحدا
His saying: '(And the disbelievers' deeds are weighed)' means: what is weighed are the sins other than disbelief, so that they may be punished for them in addition to the punishment of disbelief; and their good deeds that do not depend on intention, like freeing slaves, endowments, and maintaining family ties, [are weighed] to reduce punishment other than the punishment of disbelief. So their deeds are weighed for that reason, not for salvation from the punishment of disbelief; for it is not lightened for them nor does it cease, evidenced by the fact that Abu Lahab was rewarded with alleviation because of his freeing of his slave-girl who gave him the good news of his [the Prophet's] birth. And it is said: his good deeds which he did are rewarded in this world, like ample provision and bodily health, and he is not rewarded for them in the Hereafter at all, and the fruit of weighing his deed is either intensification of the punishment of disbelief or its non-intensification, because disbelievers differ in punishment according to their difference in disbelief. Al-Bukhari reported it (5101). Imam Ibn al-Jazari said in his book 'Arf al-Ta'rif bi al-Mawlid al-Sharif' (p. 22): 'Abu Lahab was seen after his death in a dream, and he was asked: What is your state? He said: In the Fire, except that every Monday night alleviation is granted to me, and I suck water from between my fingers to this extent – and he pointed to the tip of his finger – and that is because I freed Thuwaiyba when she gave me the good news of the birth of Muhammad, peace be upon him, and because she nursed him. So if Abu Lahab, the disbeliever whom the Quran condemned, was rewarded in the Fire because of his joy on the night of the Prophet's birth, then what about the Muslim monotheist from the nation of Muhammad who rejoices at his birth and spends whatever he can out of love for him? By my life, his reward from Allah the Generous will be that He admits him by His grace to the Gardens of Bliss.' And al-Hafiz Shams al-Din ibn Nasir al-Din al-Dimashqi said in his book 'Mawrid al-Sadi fi Mawlid al-Hadi' (p. 26): 'It is authentically reported that Abu Lahab's punishment in the Fire is lightened on Mondays because he freed Thuwaiyba out of joy at the Prophet's birth.' Then he recited: If this is a disbeliever whose blame has come / And 'Perish his hands' abides in Hell eternally / Yet it is reported that on Monday always / His punishment is lightened for joy at Ahmad / Then what of a servant whose whole life / Was joyful at Ahmad and died a monotheist?
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of why disbelievers' deeds are weighed, with a proof from the story of Abu Lahab. Al-Sawi first clarifies that the deeds weighed for disbelievers are not their disbelief itself, but other sins and good deeds that do not require intention (like freeing slaves). These are weighed to either increase punishment for sins or to reduce punishment for non-disbelief-related matters, but never to save them from the eternal punishment of disbelief. The proof is the well-known account that Abu Lahab receives alleviation from the Fire every Monday because he freed his slave-girl Thuwaiyba out of joy at the Prophet's birth. This indicates that even a disbeliever can have his punishment lightened for a worldly good deed, but the punishment for disbelief itself remains. Al-Sawi then mentions another opinion that disbelievers are rewarded for their good deeds in this world only, and the weighing results in variation of punishment according to the degree of their disbelief. The passage concludes with two quotations: one from Ibn al-Jazari and one from Ibn Nasir al-Din al-Dimashqi, both affirming the story and using it as an argument for the virtue of rejoicing in the Prophet's birth, comparing Abu Lahab's temporary alleviation to the eternal reward of a Muslim who loves the Prophet.

Key Terms
الكفار
توزن
السيئات
الحسنات
أبو لهب
تخفيف
ثويبة
المولد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That disbelievers' good deeds can save them from Hellfire or earn them salvation.
Correction: Al-Sawi emphasizes that good deeds are weighed only to add or reduce punishment for non-disbelief matters, never to remove the eternal punishment of disbelief.

Checkpoint
Why are the good deeds of disbelievers weighed according to Al-Sawi?
A) To increase their reward in Paradise
B) To perhaps save them from Hellfire
C) To either increase punishment for sins or reduce non-disbelief punishment
D) They are not weighed at all

Key Takeaway
The weighing of disbelievers' deeds serves to tailor their punishment according to their deeds, but never lifts the eternal punishment for disbelief itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even Abu Lahab receives relief every Monday for one act of kindness, how does this display Allah's overwhelming justice and mercy? How does this motivate you to do good deeds even when your faith feels low, knowing that nothing is wasted? What one small act of good will you commit today for Allah's sake alone?
?
Abu Lahab's joy at the Prophet's birth brought him temporary relief, but his disbelief kept him in eternal punishment. How does this reality confront your own relationship with the Prophet? Are you content with just celebrating his birth once a year, or are you actively learning his sunnah and following him daily? What specific step will you take this week to increase your love for him practically?
?
This lesson shows that disbelievers' deeds are weighed but cannot save them from the Fire. Does this truth stir in you a sense of urgency for your non-Muslim loved ones? Have you been complacent in calling them to Islam? Write down one name of a person you will speak to about Allah and His Messenger within the next month.

The Reality of the Balance and the Weighing of Deeds
Al-Sawi describes the Balance, its parts, and how deeds are weighed, and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the Balance (al-mizan) as a real scale with two pans, how deeds are weighed, and the rational response to the objection that this entails a transformation of realities.

Core Idea
The Balance is real; deeds become luminous or dark forms that are literally weighed.

This lesson explores the nature of the Balance (al-mizan) on the Day of Judgment. Drawing from Quranic verses and rational argument, the author affirms that the Balance is a literal scale with two pans, and that deeds are transformed into forms that are weighed. He also addresses an objection that this would involve changing realities, showing that such a transformation is within God's power.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Quranic foundation
Read the Quranic verses cited to see that the Balance is a matter of belief supported by revelation.
These verses are the primary evidence for the reality of the Balance.
2
Identify who is exempted
Notice that prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account do not require the Balance because it depends on having an account.
This exemption is based on hadith.
3
Visualize the physical description
Picture the Balance as having two pans and a tongue, with the pan of light on the right side of the Throne and the pan of darkness on the left.
This description affirms the Balance is a real object.
4
Grasp the objection and refutation
Consider the objection that transforming deeds into forms would change realities. The author answers that it is an example and even if not, it is possible for God, as only changing rational categories is impossible.
The response defends the literal understanding while addressing philosophical concerns.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالميزان. كالمؤمنين بدليل قوله تعالى : (وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنفُسَهُم ... الآية (١) ، وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُمَّهُ هَاوِيَةٌ (٢) ، وقوله تعالى : فَلَا نُقِيمُ هُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيِّمَةِ وَزْنَا (۳) ، أي : نافعاً . ولا يكون للأنبياء ولا للملائكة ، ولا لمن يدخل الجنَّة بغير حساب؛ لأنَّه فرع عن الحساب ولا حساب على من ذكر وهو على صورة ميزان الدنيا، له كفَّتان ولسان . وتوزن الأعمال بأن تُصوّر الأعمال الصَّالحة في صورة حسنة نورانيَّة، فتوضع في كِفَّةَ النُّور، وهي المُعدَّة للحسنات، وهى عن يمين العرش، مقابلة للجَنَّة، وتُصوّر الأعمال السيِّئَةُ بصورة قبيحة ظلمانية، فتوضع في كِفَّة الظُّلْمة المُعدَّة للسيئات ، وهي عن شمال العرش تجاه النَّار . قوله : (ولا لمن يدخل الجنَّة بغير حساب) : أي : لما ورد : يا محمد ؛ أدخل الجنَّة من أمَّتك من لا حساب عليه من الباب الأيمن (4) . )) . قوله : (بأنَّ تصوّر الأعمال ... إلخ) : أي : ولا يقال : إنَّ فيه قلباً للحقائق؛ لأنه مثال، وعلى تسليم أنَّ فيه قلباً للحقائق، يقال: إنَّ الممتنع قلب أقسام الحكم العقليّ لا تصيير المعنى جرماً ؛ لأنَّ قدرته تعالى صالحة لذلك، فإنَّه من جملة الممكنات .
Belief in the Balance. Like the believers, by the evidence of His statement: 'And whoever's scales are light, those are the ones who have lost their souls'... and His statement: 'And as for one whose scales are light, his refuge is an abyss' and His statement: 'So We will not establish for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' i.e., beneficial. And it will not be for the prophets, nor for the angels, nor for those who enter Paradise without account, because it (the Balance) is a branch of the account, and there is no account for those mentioned. And it is in the form of a worldly scale, having two pans and a tongue. And deeds are weighed by depicting righteous deeds in a beautiful luminous form, placed in the pan of light, which is prepared for good deeds, and it is on the right side of the Throne, facing Paradise; and evil deeds are depicted in an ugly dark form, placed in the pan of darkness prepared for evil deeds, and it is on the left side of the Throne, facing the Fire. His statement: 'nor for those who enter Paradise without account' means: because it has come: 'O Muhammad, let those of your nation who have no account enter Paradise from the right door.' His statement: 'by depicting deeds... etc.' means: And it is not said that there is a transformation of realities in it, because it is an example; and if it is granted that there is transformation of realities, it is said: what is impossible is the transformation of the categories of rational judgment, not making a meaning into a body, because His power is capable of that, for it is among possibles.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage defines the reality of the Balance (al-mizan) and addresses an objection. The author first affirms belief in the Balance as a religious necessity, citing Quranic verses. He then specifies that the Balance is not for prophets, angels, or those who enter Paradise without account because the Balance is contingent upon accounting. He describes its physical form: like a worldly scale with two pans and a tongue. Good deeds are given a luminous form and placed in the right pan (facing Paradise), evil deeds are given a dark form and placed in the left pan (facing Hell). The marginal comment explains that the phrase 'nor for those who enter without account' is supported by a hadith. The second marginal comment refutes an objection: that depicting deeds as forms changes realities. The author responds that it is a metaphor (mithal), and even if it were a transformation, it is possible for God to make a meaning into a body because it is a possible thing, and the impossibility only applies to changing the categories of rational judgment, not to this.

Key Terms

الحساب
كفة النور
كفة الظلمة
قلب الحقائق
الحكم العقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance is merely a metaphor or that transforming deeds into forms is impossible.
Correction: The Balance is a real scale, and God can transform deeds into bodies because it is a possible thing; only changing categories of rational judgment is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who does not require the Balance?
A) All believers
B) Prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account
C) Only the unbelievers
D) All of humanity

Key Takeaway
The Balance is a real scale with two pans for good and evil deeds, and God's power makes the weighing possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to face the Balance today, would your good deeds outweigh your bad? What specific actions are you neglecting that could tip the scale?
?
The source says that those who enter Paradise without account are exempt from the Balance. Does your hope in Allah's mercy lead you to be careless about your deeds, or does it spur you to strive for that exemption?
?
When you consider that every deed—even the smallest—will be given a visible form on the Day of Judgment, what secret sin are you most afraid of seeing materialized in the pan of darkness? What will you do today to turn it into a deed of light?

Weighing Scrolls and the Hadith of the Card
Al-Sawi presents an alternative view on weighing scrolls and the hadith of the card.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternative view that the scrolls containing deeds are weighed in the Balance, and how the hadith of the card demonstrates the immense weight of the testimony of faith.

Core Idea
The hadith of the card shows that 'La ilaha illa Allah' can outweigh a lifetime of sins.

This lesson explores an alternative perspective on the weighing of deeds in the Hereafter. While some scholars hold that deeds themselves take form and are weighed, others maintain that the scrolls recording them are what is weighed. The famous hadith of the card provides compelling support for this view, illustrating the overwhelming mercy of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two opinions about what is weighed and the evidence presented.
The hadith of the card is central to this view.
2
Identify the alternative opinion
Look for the phrase 'وقيل' (and it is said) which introduces the alternative view that scrolls are weighed. Understand the reasoning that good and evil deeds are distinguished in writing.
3
Reflect on the hadith and its lesson
The hadith narrates a servant with many sins but a single card with the shahada. Consider why the card outweighs everything and what that teaches about Allah's mercy.
The hadith emphasizes that nothing outweighs the name of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل : توزن الصُّحُف المكتوبةُ فيها الأعمال، بناءً على أنَّ الحسنات متميّزة عن السَّيِّئات بكتاب ويشهد لهذا حديث البطاقة. وهناك صنج مثاقيل الذر يعلم بها كميّة التفاوت تحقيقاً لتمام العدل فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا. قوله : ( حديث البطاقة) : أي : فقد ورد ما معناه: «أنَّ عبداً كتب عليه تسعة وتسعون سجلاً من المعاصي، كل سجل طوله مد البصر، فتوضع في كفَّة السَّيِّئات، فيقول الله له يا عبدي ؛ هل فعلت حسنة؟ فيقول: لا يا رب، فيقول : بل بقي لك عندنا أمانة، فيأمر بإخراج بطاقة وهي صغيرة قدر الأنملة مكتوب فيها : (لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله)، فتوضع في كفَّة الحسنات، فتطيش سجلات المعاصي، ولا يثقل مع اسم الله شيء، فيقول : امضوا بعبدي إلى الجنَّة بفضلي ومغفرتي» قوله : (يعلم بها كمية التَّفاوت :أي: فتوضع السَّيِّئات في مقابلة الحسنات، فإن رجح أحدهما ؛ وضع صنج بقدر ما رجح، فينعم بقدره أو يعذب بقدره.)
And it is said: The scrolls upon which deeds are written are weighed, based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished from evil deeds by writing, and the hadith of the card testifies to this. And there are weights of atoms by which the amount of difference is known, achieving complete justice. 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.' His statement: (Hadith of the card) meaning: It has been reported with the meaning: 'A servant had ninety-nine scrolls of sins written against him, each scroll stretching as far as the eye can see. They are placed in the pan of evil deeds. Allah says to him: O my servant, have you done any good deed? He says: No, O Lord. He says: Rather, you still have a trust with Us. He orders the extraction of a card, small as a fingertip, on which is written: "There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah." It is placed in the pan of good deeds, and the scrolls of sins fly away, and nothing weighs heavier than the name of Allah. He says: Take my servant to Paradise by My favor and My forgiveness.' His statement: (by which the amount of difference is known) means: The evil deeds are placed opposite the good deeds; if one outweighs the other, a weight is placed equivalent to the excess, and he is rewarded or punished accordingly.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage discusses an alternative view regarding the weighing of deeds. The first opinion presented earlier was that deeds themselves are given forms and weighed. Here, the author reports that some say the scrolls (suhuf) containing the record of deeds are weighed. This is supported by the hadith of the card (hadith al-bitaqah). The author adds that there are weights (sanaj) corresponding to atoms (mithaqil al-dharr) to measure the exact difference in weight, ensuring complete justice, as indicated by the Quranic verse. The marginal comment then relates the famous hadith of the card, which narrates that a servant who had many sins on scrolls had a single card with the shahada, and that card outweighed all the sins because nothing weighs heavier than the name of Allah. The final marginal comment explains the function of the weights: they measure the excess, so that punishment or reward is exactly proportional.

Key Terms
صحف
البطاقة
صنج
مثاقيل الذر
لا إله إلا الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith of the card means deeds are not necessary for salvation.
Correction: The hadith emphasizes Allah's immense grace; it does not negate the importance of deeds but shows that sincere faith can override many sins. The servant's case is exceptional, and the hadith ends with 'by My favor and My forgiveness', highlighting mercy.

Checkpoint
What is the significance of the hadith of the card (بطاقة)?
A) It proves that deeds are weighed as forms
B) It shows that a single testimony of faith can outweigh many sins
C) It indicates that angels write deeds on scrolls
D) It rejects the concept of the Balance

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the card demonstrates that sincere faith in Allah and His Messenger, even in a single declaration, can outweigh an enormous burden of sins by Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your sins were written on scrolls stretching as far as the eye can see, would you have a 'card' of sincere faith that you are confident outweighs them? What does your current relationship with the shahada say about your certainty in Allah's mercy?
?
The hadith ends with 'by My favor and My forgiveness.' Does your hope for salvation rest more on your own deeds or on Allah's grace? How would you answer Allah if He asked you, 'Have you done any good deed?'—honestly, what would you say?
?
If nothing outweighs the name of Allah, why do you still allow certain sins to weigh you down as if they are greater than His mercy? What is one sin you need to repent from today, trusting that His forgiveness can tip the scale?

Belief in the Prophet's Pond
Al-Sawi affirms belief in the Prophet's Pond and notes the hadith are mutawatir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in the Prophet's Pond (al-hawd) is obligatory and how the hadith reaching tawatur establish its certainty.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Pond is a real, mass-transmitted truth of the Hereafter.

This short but powerful passage affirms one of the eschatological realities known as the sam'iyyat — matters heard from revelation. Al-Sawi asserts that the hadith concerning the Prophet's Pond are so numerous and reliably transmitted that they reach tawatur, the highest level of certainty. This makes belief in the Pond a necessary part of Sunni creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's words settle before interpretation.
Notice the brevity: only two key points are made.
2
Identify the two elements
Identify the object of belief (the Prophet's specific Pond) and the evidential status (hadith reaching tawatur).
3
Understand why tawatur matters
Tawatur means mass transmission that yields certain knowledge. In creed, only mutawatir reports are used to establish obligatory beliefs. Ask yourself: Why is this important for belief in the Pond?
The commentary will clarify.
4
Reflect on the implication
If someone denies a mutawatir report, they are rejecting certain knowledge. This passage shows that denying the Pond is not a valid option for a Sunni Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالحوض (والحوض) أي : حوض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وورد فيه أحاديث كثيرة بلغت مبلغ التّواتر،
Belief in the Pond — i.e., the Pond of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. And there are many hadith regarding it, reaching the level of tawatur.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This short passage states the belief in the Pond (al-hawd) of the Prophet Muhammad. It identifies that the Pond refers specifically to the Pond of the Messenger. The author notes that the hadith concerning this Pond are numerous and have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission), indicating that the belief is firmly established and obligatory to affirm.

Key Terms
الحوض
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Pond is only symbolic or metaphorical.
Correction: The passage and hadith affirm a real, physical Pond in the Hereafter.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the hadith regarding the Pond?
A) They are weak
B) They are mutawatir
C) They are fabricated
D) They are singular

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Pond is an established reality of the Hereafter, proven by mass-transmitted hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe you will one day stand at the Prophet's Pond, why do you still prioritize this world over preparing for that encounter?
?
The hadith about the Pond are mutawatir—certain. Where does your certainty about the Hereafter rank among your daily certainties? What would change if you lived with that certainty moment by moment?
?
Do you yearn to drink from the Prophet's Pond, or have you become so comfortable with sin that you fear being turned away? What one step can you take today to increase your longing for that meeting?

Belief in the Hawd: Evidence and Universal Prophetic Aspect
Sanusi defines belief in the Hawd and cites hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence for the Hawd from authentic hadith and the correct theological view that every prophet has a Hawd.

Core Idea
The Hawd is not exclusive to Muhammad; every prophet has one.

This passage from Sanusi's work introduces the belief in the Hawd (Pool) and provides compelling textual evidence from the Two Sahihs and divine revelation to Jesus. It also clarifies a common misconception: that the Hawd is a unique feature of Prophet Muhammad, whereas in reality, every prophet has a Hawd.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the direct style: the author states the belief and then immediately provides evidence.
2
Identify the two pieces of evidence
The passage cites two sources: the hadith in the Two Sahihs and the revelation to Jesus. Write down the key descriptions from each.
The descriptions are complementary, emphasizing the vastness and beauty of the Hawd.
3
Understand the theological nuance
The author then states the correct view that every prophet has a Hawd. Reflect on why this distinction matters and what it says about prophetic blessings.
This corrects the misconception that the Hawd is a unique privilege of our Prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالحوض. وفي الصحيحين: حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، من شرب منه لا يظمأ أبداً. وقد ورد فيما أوحى الله إلى عيسى في صفة نبينا: له حوض أبعد من مكة إلى مطلع الشمس، فيه آنية مثل نجوم السماء، وله كل لون شراب الجنة، وطعم كل ثمار الجنة. والصحيح أنَّ لكلّ نبي حوضاً، فليس من خصوصيات نبينا. قوله: (والصحيح أن لكل نبي حوضاً) أي: ولم يصح أن حوض صالح ضرع ناقته.
Belief in the Hawd (Pool). And in the Two Sahihs: 'My Hawd is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is better than musk, and its cups are more than the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst again.' And it has been reported in what Allah revealed to Jesus describing our Prophet: 'He has a Hawd farther than Mecca to the rising of the sun, in it are vessels like the stars of the sky, and it has every color of the wine of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise.' And the correct view is that every prophet has a Hawd, so it is not a speciality of our Prophet. His saying: (And the correct view is that every prophet has a Hawd) meaning: and it is not confirmed that the Hawd of Salih is the udder of his she-camel.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of belief in the Hawd. It begins by stating the doctrine 'Belief in the Hawd'. Then it provides textual evidence from the Two Sahihs (Bukhari and Muslim) quoting a hadith that describes the Hawd's vast size, the whiteness of its water, its pleasant smell, and the multitude of its cups, and that drinking from it prevents thirst forever. Next, it adds another narration from the revelation to Jesus (peace be upon him) that describes the Prophet's Hawd as even more immense and containing vessels like stars and all flavors of Paradise. The author then affirms the correct view that every prophet has a Hawd, so this is not a unique feature of our Prophet Muhammad. Finally, the commentator explains the phrase 'the correct view' by noting that the claim that Salih's Hawd was the udder of his she-camel is not authentically established. The passage establishes the reality of the Hawd and its universal prophetic aspect.

Key Terms
الحوض
الصحيحين
الأنبياء
الخصوصيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hawd is unique to Prophet Muhammad and no other prophet has one.
Correction: The correct view is that every prophet has a Hawd, as the text explicitly states.

Checkpoint
What does the authentic hadith describe about the Hawd?
A) It is located in Paradise after the Bridge
B) It is a month's journey, its water is whiter than milk, and its cups are more than stars
C) Only our Prophet has a Hawd
D) Drinking from it causes thirst later

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Hawd is a core tenet supported by multiple hadith, and it is a blessing shared by all prophets, not exclusive to Prophet Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine the Hawd—its water whiter than milk and its smell better than musk—does your soul genuinely ache to drink from it? What are you doing today to ensure you will be among those who drink?
?
The Prophet's Hawd is described with such detail that it seems real enough to touch. Yet, do you live as if this promise is more certain than tomorrow's sunrise? What worldly distractions keep you from longing for it?
?
Every prophet has a Hawd, yet our love for Prophet Muhammad should make us yearn for his above all. Do you truly feel that love in your heart, or is it a mere statement? What will you change to make your desire for his Hawd a driving force in your life?

The Hawd's Timing and Essential Belief
Sanusi affirms the Hawd's existence and moderates the timing debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligatory belief regarding the Hawd's timing and why precise knowledge of its sequence is not required.

Core Idea
Belief in the Hawd is obligatory; its exact timing is not essential.

Sanusi begins by affirming that the Hawd is before the Scale, but immediately introduces a scholarly dispute: is it before or after the Path? Rather than settle the debate, he clarifies the core obligation of this discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on timing
Read the Arabic sentence affirming the Hawd is before the Scale, then notice the question raised about the Path.
The matn asserts a position, but the sharh immediately opens a debate.
2
Identify the two opinions
Find the phrase indicating the two opinions on whether the Hawd is before or after the Path.
Sanusi does not prefer one; he notes both are allowed.
3
Understand the obligatory belief
Sanusi says: what is required is to believe the Hawd is established; ignorance of its precedence or delay does not harm.
This is a key principle: speculative matters do not necessitate decisive belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنَّه يكون قبل الميزان. قوله: (وأنَّه يكون قبل الميزان) أي وهل هو قبل الصراط أو بعده قولان؟ وبالجملة: فالواجب علينا اعتقاد أنه ثابت، وجَهْل تقدمه على الخ. وهل هو حوض واحد أو حوضان، والثاني بعد الصراط؟ قولان، وقيل: الذي بعد الصراط هو الكوثر، وهو نهر في الجنة لا حوض، وإنما الحوض قبل الصراط، وهو جسم مخصوص يصب فيه ميزابان ماء الكوثر، ترده أمته عليه الصلاة والسلام، من شرب منه شربة لا يظمأ بعدها أبداً. ويكون الشرب في الجنة إنما هو على سبيل التلذذ لا العطش، ويطرد عنه من بدل وغير، إما بالارتداد وإما أن يحدث في الدين ليس منه؛ كأهل البدع على اختلاف أنواعهم، وكأهل الكبائر المعلنين بها، وكالظلمة الجائرين في أحكامهم؛ لأن المرتد مخلد في النار، وخالف المعتزلة في ذلك، وهم أحق للطرد عنه من غيرهم. قوله: (ترده أمته) أي والأمين عليه علي بن أبي طالب كما ورد. قوله: (لا يظمأ بعدها أبداً) أي ولو دخل النار؛ فلا يعذب فيها بالعطش. قوله: (ويطرد عنه من بدل وغير) أي فالكافر لا يشرب منه، والمبتدع يشرب منه بعد الرد.
And that it is before the Scale. His saying: (And that it is before the Scale) meaning: is it before the Path or after it? Two opinions. And in summary: it is obligatory upon us to believe that it is established, and ignorance of its precedence or delay does not harm. And is it one Hawd or two Hawds, the second after the Path? Two opinions, and it is said that what is after the Path is the Kawthar, and it is a river in Paradise, not a Hawd. Rather the Hawd is before the Path, and it is a particular body into which two channels pour the water of Kawthar; his nation visits it, peace and blessings be upon him; whoever drinks from it a drink will never thirst after it forever. And drinking in Paradise is only for pleasure, not thirst. And those who change and alter are driven away from it, either by apostasy or by introducing into the religion that which is not from it; like the people of innovation of all their types, and the people of major sins who commit them openly, and the unjust oppressors in their judgments. Because the apostate is eternally in the Fire, and the Mu'tazila disagreed in that, and they are more deserving of being driven away from it than others. His saying: (his nation visits it) meaning: and the trusted custodian over it is Ali ibn Abi Talib, as has been reported. His saying: (will never thirst after it ever) meaning: even if he enters the Fire; he will not be punished therein with thirst. His saying: (and those who change and alter are driven away) meaning: the disbeliever does not drink from it, and the innovator drinks from it after being repelled.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the Hawd's timing and the categories of people excluded from it. It begins with the matn statement that the Hawd is before the Scale. The commentator then raises the question: is it before the Path (Sirat) or after? He notes two opinions but says the obligatory belief is simply that it is established; not knowing the precise order does not harm. Then he discusses whether there is one Hawd or two, citing the view that a second one after the Sirat is actually the Kawthar, a river in Paradise, and that the true Hawd is a specific body before the Sirat supplied by two channels from Kawthar. The Prophet's nation visits it, and drinking prevents thirst forever. Drinking in Paradise is for pleasure, not thirst. Then he lists those driven away: apostates, innovators of all kinds, open sinners, and unjust rulers. The apostate is eternally in Fire. He notes that the Mu'tazila disagreed on this issue and are especially worthy of being driven away. Finally, three additional comments are explained: that Ali is entrusted with the Hawd, that even if one enters Fire he will not be punished with thirst after drinking, and that the disbeliever is completely barred while the innovator may drink after being repelled.

Key Terms
الميزان
الصراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One must know exactly when the Hawd occurs.
Correction: Sanusi says ignorance of its timing does not harm; belief in its existence suffices.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the obligatory belief regarding the Hawd?
A) That it is exactly before the Scale
B) That it is after the Path
C) That it is established, regardless of its exact timing
D) That it is both before the Scale and after the Path

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Hawd is required, but its precise sequence relative to the Path is not a matter of essential creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of one Islamic belief (about the Hereafter) where you have focused more on the 'when' or 'how' than on establishing certainty that it is true. How does this lesson's principle—that ignorance of details does not harm—free you to strengthen your faith in that area? What is one thing you will do today to turn that belief into action?
?
Are there any unseen matters you have dismissed because scholars differed over secondary aspects? How can you practice accepting the agreed-upon core while leaving the disputed details aside—starting with the Hawd itself?
?
If you were asked about the Hawd on the Day of Judgment, would you be able to say, 'I believed it was real, even though I didn't know exactly when it would appear'? Or would you have to admit you waited to be fully convinced? What does your answer reveal about the state of your heart toward Allah's promises?

The Hawd and Kawthar: One or Two?
Sanusi discusses the number of Hawds and defines the true Hawd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly opinions on whether there is one Hawd or two, and the distinction between the Hawd and Kawthar.

Core Idea
The Hawd is a specific basin before the Path; the Kawthar is a river in Paradise.

After settling the importance of belief, Sanusi addresses a further dispute: is there one Hawd or two? Some say a second water source after the Path is actually the Kawthar, not a Hawd. The passage clarifies the unique characteristics of the true Hawd.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on one or two Hawds
Read from 'هل هو حوض واحد أو حوضان' to 'ترده أمته'. Identify the two opinions.
2
Distinguish Hawd and Kawthar
Notice the view that the second is Kawthar, a river in Paradise, not a Hawd. The Hawd is a specific body before the Path.
Kawthar is a river, Hawd is a basin supplied by it.
3
Understand the description of the Hawd
The Hawd has two channels from Kawthar, and the Prophet's nation visits it. Drinking prevents thirst forever.
Drinking in Paradise is for pleasure, not thirst.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to the passage, what is the relationship between the Hawd and Kawthar?
A) They are two names for the same thing

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the Hawd is before the Path, it reminds you that mercy precedes judgment. In your own life, where have you been rushing to judgment without first offering mercy? Commit to one act of mercy this week as a preparation for that Day.
?
The Prophet's nation will visit the Hawd and drink. Do you truly count yourself among his nation? What evidence is there in your daily actions that you are following him, not just claiming his name? Write down one specific way you will follow his sunnah more closely starting today.

Those Driven Away from the Hawd
Sanusi lists who is driven away and adds clarifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of people who are driven away from the Hawd and the rationale for their exclusion.

Core Idea
Apostates, innovators, open sinners, and unjust rulers are driven away.

Sanusi now specifies who is barred from drinking at the Hawd. He enumerates those who 'change and alter' the religion, from apostasy to open sin, and even highlights the Mu'tazila as especially deserving of exclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of those driven away
Find the sentence beginning 'ويطرد عنه من بدل وغير' and note the categories mentioned.
2
Understand the two types of alteration
The text says: 'by apostasy or by introducing into the religion that which is not from it.' This covers major innovation.
3
Identify specific groups
The commentator lists: people of innovation (all types), open sinners, and unjust rulers. He adds the Mu'tazila separately.
The Mu'tazila are singled out because they disagreed on this issue.
4
Read the additional comments
The passage ends with notes on Ali's role and that even if one enters Fire, he won't thirst after drinking.

?

?
If you hold any position of authority over others, do you judge justly according to Allah's law, or do you follow your own desires? How will you change today?

Belief in Paradise and Hell Created Now
Sanusi affirms that Paradise and Hell are already created and clarifies the term 'al-Niran'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are already created and that the term 'al-Niran' refers to the Path and the Scale.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now, and the 'Fires' refer to the Path and Scale.

Sanusi affirms a key tenet of Sunni belief: that Paradise and Hell are already created and not future events. He also clarifies that the term 'al-Niran' (the fires) in certain contexts means the Sirat (Path) and Mizan (Scale), not literal flames. This lesson explores this passage and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Notice how the passage affirms the current existence of Paradise and Hell and then explains the term 'al-Niran'.
The passage is short but dense with meaning.
2
Understand the affirmation of current creation
Focus on the phrase 'وانهما مخلوقتان الآن' (both are created now). This is a direct statement that Paradise and Hell exist at the present time, not merely in the future.
This counters a common misconception that they will only be created after the Day of Judgment.
3
Clarify the meaning of 'al-Niran'
The passage explains that 'al-Niran' (fires) is plural of 'nar' and refers to a subtle, burning body that tends upward. It then specifies that in this context it means the Sirat (Path) and Mizan (Scale). Note also that ignorance of their timing does not harm belief.
This shows careful attention to theological terms and their referents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما الإيمان بالجنة والنار، وأنهما مخلوقتان الآن. (والنيران) بكسر النون جمع نار وهي جسم لطيف محرق يميل إلى جهة العلو، والمراد بها الصراط والميزان أو تأخره لا يضر في الاعتقاد.

Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage defines belief in Paradise and Hell, stating that they are already created (makhluqatan al-an). It then explains the word 'al-Niran' (the fires): it is the plural of 'nar' (fire), and it is described as a subtle, burning body that tends upward. The commentator clarifies that by 'al-Niran' is meant the Sirat (Path) and the Mizan (Scale). He then adds that not knowing whether the Sirat and Mizan come before or after other events does not harm one's belief. The passage thus affirms the reality of Paradise and Hell as currently existing creations and clarifies an ambiguous term, while also noting that the precise timing of the Sirat and Mizan is not essential doctrine.
