The Nature of Angels: Definition and Infallibility
Defines angels and asserts their infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of an angel as a subtle, spiritual, luminous body capable of assuming beautiful forms, and their infallibility as proven by the Quran.

Core Idea
Angels are luminous spiritual bodies that never disobey Allah.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary establishes the essential nature of angels. Before discussing specific angels, the author defines what an angel is and affirms their complete obedience to Allah. This foundational understanding is crucial for all subsequent discussion about angels.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the literal English translation. Notice the flow from obligation to definition.
Pay attention to the Quranic citation as evidence.
2
Identify the three characteristics of an angel
The definition contains three adjectives: لطيف (subtle), روحاني (spiritual), نوراني (luminous). Write them down and reflect on what each means.
These describe the angelic body as unlike human bodies.
3
Understand the ability to assume forms
The passage says angels have the power to take on beautiful shapes. Consider why this ability is important for their roles.
This will be clarified further in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) بوجود (الأملاك) وعصمتهم أيضاً، قال تعالى: لَا يَعْصُونَ اللهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ (١) ، جمع [؟] وهو : جسم لطيف روحاني نوراني له القدرة على التشكلات الجميلة. ويجب الإيمان بهم إجمالاً فيمن علم منهم إجمالاً، وتفصيلا فيمن علم منهم تفصيلاً بالشَّخص ؛ كجبريل وإسرافيل وميكائيل وعزرائيل، وهم رؤساء الملائكة عليهم الصلاة والسلام أجمعين، ومُنكَر ونكير. قوله : (على التَّشكُلات الجميلة): المراد بها ما عدا الخسيسة؛ كالكلب والخنزير فيشمل الفظيعة الهائلة؛ كمالك خازن النَّار، ومنكر ونكير، وعزرائيل في إتيانهم الكفَّار، ولا تحكم عليهم الصورة. فإنَّهم أنكروا وجودهما بالمرة.
And (it is obligatory to believe) in the existence of the angels and their infallibility as well. He said: 'They do not disobey Allah in what He commands them and they do what they are commanded' (Qur'an 66:6). The plural [؟] is: a subtle spiritual luminous body, having the ability to assume beautiful forms. And it is obligatory to believe in them in general for those known in general, and in detail for those known in detail by person, like Jibril, Israfil, Mikail, and Azrael, and they are the chiefs of the angels, peace be upon them all, and Munkar and Nakir. His saying: 'upon beautiful forms' means: other than base forms, like the dog and pig, so it includes the terrible and magnificent, like Malik the keeper of Hell, Munkar and Nakir, and Azrael in their coming to the disbelievers, and the form does not dominate them. For they (some people) denied their existence entirely.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage defines angels and mandates belief in them with details. It begins by stating the obligation of belief in the existence of angels and their infallibility, citing the verse that angels never disobey God's commands. It then defines an angel as a subtle (lāṭif) spiritual (rūḥānī) luminous (nūrānī) body capable of assuming beautiful forms. Belief is required in a general way for those angels known generally, and in specific detail for those known personally, such as the four archangels (Jibril, Israfil, Mikail, Azrael) – described as the chiefs of angels – and also Munkar and Nakir, the angels of the grave. The commentator explains that 'beautiful forms' excludes base shapes like dogs and pigs but includes fearsome and magnificent forms, such as Malik (the keeper of Hell), Munkar and Nakir, and Azrael when appearing to disbelievers. He adds that these angels are not controlled by the form (i.e., they are not subject to it). The passage ends by noting that some people denied the existence of Munkar and Nakir altogether.

Belief in Angels: General and Specific Obligation
Explains the obligation to believe in angels generally and specifically, and clarifies the range of their forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in angels in general and in detail, and the clarification that 'beautiful forms' includes fearsome appearances.

Core Idea
We must believe in angels by name when known, and their forms do not limit them.

Having defined angels, the author now explains how we must believe in them. Some angels are known by name, like the four archangels, while others are believed in generally. A subtle point about 'beautiful forms' is clarified to include fearsome appearances, showing that angels are not bound by their outward form.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage for this lesson and its translation. Notice the distinction between general and specific belief.
The passage lists specific names of angels.
2
Identify the two types of belief
The passage mentions 'إجمالاً' (general) and 'تفصيلاً' (detailed). Write down what each means based on the text.
General belief is for angels known only as a group; detailed belief is for those known by name.
3
List the named angels
From the passage, extract the names of the angels mentioned: Jibril, Israfil, Mikail, Azrael, Munkar, Nakir. Note that the first four are called chiefs.
These are the most well-known angels in Islamic tradition.
4
Understand the clarification about forms
The passage explains that 'beautiful forms' excludes base forms (e.g., dog, pig) but includes fearsome ones (e.g., Malik, Munkar, Nakir, Azrael when appearing to disbelievers). Reflect on why this matters.
This shows angels can appear in terrifying forms as needed.

Angels: Keepers, Bearers, Guardians, and Recorders
Enumerates specific angel types and their functions with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific types of angels mentioned in Islamic theology, their assigned functions, and the wisdom behind their roles as explained by Imam al-Sawi.

Core Idea
Angels are assigned specific duties: guarding every human, recording deeds, and bearing the Throne.

This lesson presents the classification of angels by name and type, as outlined in the matn and explained by al-Sawi. You will learn about the keepers of Paradise and Hell, the bearers of the Throne, the guardian angels who protect all humans, and the recording angels who document every action. The commentary provides deeper insights, including the honor God bestows on humanity and the wisdom of recording deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall list of angels and their functions.
2
Identify the four angel categories
The passage enumerates several angel types: named keepers (Ridwan, Malik), bearers of the Throne, guardian angels (hafazah), and recording angels (katabah). Locate each in the text.
Notice that the guardians protect even disbelievers and children – an important point.
3
Study the commentary details
Al-Sawi explains that the bearers of the Throne are four in this world and eight in the Hereafter, and that guardian angels protect humans as an honor, citing Qur'an 17:70.
Also note the tradition from Ka'b al-Ahbar about guardian angels defending against jinn.
4
Reflect on the wisdom
Consider why angels are assigned these roles: guardianship shows divine care, recording encourages accountability, and bearing the Throne signifies majesty. What does this teach about God's attributes?
This connects to the broader lesson on samiyyat (matters of the unseen).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورضوان خازن الجنان ومالك خازن النيران، أو بالنَّوع؛ كحملة العرش، وأعوان السَّيِّد عزرائيل . . والحفظة : وهم ملائكة موكَّلون بحفظ البشر – ولو صغيراً وكافراً – ور من الجنّ مثلاً ، قال تعالى: ﴿لَهُ مُعَقِّبَتُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ، يَحْفَظُونَهُ مِنْ أَمْرِ الله ) (١) . والكتبة : وهم ملائكة يكتبون على المكلف جميع ما صدر منه من قول ولو نفسياً وفعل واعتقاد، قوله : (كحملة العرش وهم في الدُّنيا أربعة، وفي الآخرة ثمانية. قوله : (موكَّلون بحفظ البشر ) : أي : تكرمة لهم، قال تعالى : (وَلَقَدْ كَرَّمْنَا بَنِي ءَادَمَ (٢) قوله : (من) الجنِّ مثلاً : أي : والعاهات والآفات. قوله : (مِنْ أَمْرِ اللَّهِ ) : أي من ضرر خلقه الجن والإنس وغيرهم، وقيل : (من) بمعنى الباء ؛ أي: بأمره عن كل مكروه، فإذا جاء القدر تخلّوا عنه، قال كعب الأحبار : لولا أنَّ الله تعالى وكل بكم حفظة يذبون عنكم في مطعمكم ومشربكم ؛ لتخطَّفتكم الجن ) (٣) . قوله : (يكتبون ... إلخ) أي وحكمة الكتابة : أنَّ العبد إذا علم بها
And Ridwan is the keeper of Paradise and Malik is the keeper of Hell, or by type: like the bearers of the Throne and the helpers of Master Azrael. And the guardians: they are angels entrusted with protecting humans – even a child or a disbeliever – and from the jinn for example, He said: 'For him are successive angels before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of Allah' (Qur'an 13:11). And the recorders: they are angels who write upon the accountable person all that proceeds from him of speech, even inward, and action and belief. His saying: 'like the bearers of the Throne, and they are in this world four, and in the Hereafter eight.' His saying: 'entrusted with protecting humans' means: as an honor for them, He said: 'And indeed We have honored the children of Adam' (Qur'an 17:70). His saying: 'from the jinn for example' means: and from ailments and afflictions. His saying: 'by the command of Allah' means: from the harm of His creation, jinn, humans, and others, and it is said that 'min' is in the sense of 'bi' (by); i.e., by His command from every disliked thing, so when destiny comes they leave him. Ka'b al-Ahbar said: 'Were it not that Allah, exalted, has appointed for you guardians who defend you in your food and drink, the jinn would snatch you away.' His saying: 'they write ... etc.' means: and the wisdom of writing is that the servant, when he knows about it
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage enumerates specific types of angels and their functions. It first mentions two named angels: Ridwan, the keeper of Paradise, and Malik, the keeper of Hell. Then it discusses types: the bearers of the Throne (ḥamalat al-‘arsh) and the helpers of Azrael, followed by the guardian angels (ḥafazah) and the recording angels (katabah). The base text states that guardians are assigned to protect every human, including children and disbelievers, from harm including jinn, citing Qur'an 13:11. The recorders write down every word (even internal thoughts), action, and belief of the accountable person. The commentator (al-Sawi) explains the bearers of the Throne: they are four in this world and eight in the Hereafter. He explains that the protection is an honor for humans, referencing Qur'an 17:70. The phrase 'from the jinn' is interpreted broadly to include all harms. The phrase 'by the command of Allah' is explained as protection from harm caused by jinn, humans, etc., but when predestined calamity comes, the angels withdraw. A tradition from Ka'b al-Ahbar emphasizes the guardians' role in protecting from jinn. Finally, the wisdom behind the recording angels is that when a person knows they are being recorded, they become more careful, though the text is cut off.

Correction: The passage explicitly states they protect every human, including disbelievers and children, as an honor from God.

The Guardian Angels (al-Ḥafaẓah)
Al-Sawi defines guardian angels and their protective role with scriptural support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of guardian angels as protectors of humans, including children and disbelievers, and the wisdom behind their guardianship.

Core Idea
Guardian angels protect every human as an honor from Allah until the decree arrives.

Al-Sawi begins by describing the guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓah), who are assigned to protect all humans, regardless of age or faith, and even from the jinn. He supports this with Qur'anic verses and explains that this protection is an act of honor. This lesson explores the nature and scope of their guardianship as derived from scripture and tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage for guardian angels once, then review the translation. Note the key terms.
2
Understand the scope of protection
Notice that guardian angels protect even children and disbelievers, and from jinn and calamities.
The protection is from harm until divine decree.
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
Reflect on the verses cited (13:11 and 17:70) and the quote from Ka'b al-Ahbar.
4
Consider the wisdom
Why does Allah appoint guardian angels? The passage indicates it is an honor for mankind.
The protection ends when the decree comes.

والحفظة : وهم ملائكة موكَّلون بحفظ البشر – ولو صغيراً وكافراً – ومن الجنّ مثلاً، قال تعالى: ﴿لَهُ مُعَقِّبَتُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ، يَحْفَظُونَهُ مِنْ أَمْرِ الله﴾ . والكتبة : وهم ملائكة يكتبون على المكلف جميع ما صدر منه من قول ولو نفسياً وفعل واعتقاد، قوله : (كحملة العرش وهم في الدُّنيا أربعة، وفي الآخرة ثمانية). قوله : (موكَّلون بحفظ البشر ) : أي : تكرمة لهم، قال تعالى : ﴿وَلَقَدْ كَرَّمْنَا بَنِي ءَادَمَ﴾ قوله : (من) الجنِّ مثلاً : أي : والعاهات والآفات. قوله : (مِنْ أَمْرِ اللَّهِ ) : أي من ضرر خلقه الجن والإنس وغيرهم، وقيل : (من) بمعنى الباء ؛ أي: بأمره عن كل مكروه، فإذا جاء القدر تخلّوا عنه، قال كعب الأحبار : لولا أنَّ الله تعالى وكل بكم حفظة يذبون عنكم في مطعمكم ومشربكم ؛ لتخطَّفتكم الجن . قوله : (يكتبون ... إلخ) أي وحكمة الكتابة : أنَّ العبد إذا علم بها استحيا وترك المعصية. لا يفارقونه إلا في حالة الجماع والغُسل والخلاء)، والمشهور أنهما ملكان يسمى أحدهما : الرقيب، والثاني: العتيد، كما في سورة (ق). قوله : (لا يفارقونه إلَّا في حالة الجماع ... إلخ) : أي : فإذا فعل في تلك الأحوال الثَّلاث حسنة أو سيئة ؛ فإنَّهم يعرفونها بنتن رائحة السَّيِّئة وطيب رائحة الحسنة . قوله : (يسمى أحدهما : الرَّقيب أي : وهو كاتب الحسنات . وقوله : (والثَّاني: العتيد) : أي : وهو كاتب السَّيِّئات، وقيل : كلُّ يسمى بكل، وجعل الله كاتب الحسنات أميراً على كاتب السَّيِّئات، فإن فعل حسنة كتبت حالاً، وإن فعل سيِّئة يقول كاتب السَّيِّئات : اكتب، فيقول له كاتب الحسنات اصبر لعله يستغفر ويتوب، فإن تاب؛ كتب حسنة، فإن لم يتب بعد ست ساعات فاكتب؛ قال له كاتب الحسنات: اكتب، اراحنا الله منه. وتعرض صحائف الأعمال صباحاً ومساءً على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ؛ فإن رأى خيراً ؛ حمد الله وشكر لصاحبه، وإن رأى غير ذلك ؛ استغفر لفاعله.
And the guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓah): they are angels entrusted with guarding humans – even if a child or disbeliever – and from the jinn, for example, Allah said: 'For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of Allah.' And the recording angels (al-katabah): they are angels who write down for the accountable person (al-mukallaf) all that issues from him of speech, even if inward, and action and belief. His statement: (like the bearers of the Throne, and they in the world are four, and in the Hereafter eight). His statement: (entrusted with guarding humans): i.e., as an honor for them, Allah said: 'And We have certainly honored the children of Adam.' His statement: (from) the jinn for example: i.e., and afflictions and calamities. His statement: (by the command of Allah): i.e., from the harm of His creation, jinn and humans and others, and it is said: 'from' in the sense of 'with'; i.e., by His command from every disliked thing, so when the decree comes they abandon him. Kaʿb al-Aḥbār said: 'Were it not that Allah has appointed guardian angels for you to defend you in your food and drink, the jinn would snatch you away.' His statement: (they write... etc.): i.e., the wisdom of the writing is that when the servant knows about it, he feels shy and leaves disobedience. They do not leave him except in the state of intercourse, bathing, and relieving oneself, and the well-known is that they are two angels, one called al-Raqīb and the second al-ʿAtīd, as in Sūrat Qāf. His statement: (they do not leave him except in the state of intercourse... etc.): i.e., so if he does in those three states a good deed or an evil deed, they know them by the stench of the evil deed's smell and the pleasant smell of the good deed. His statement: (one called al-Raqīb): i.e., he is the writer of good deeds. And his statement: (and the second al-ʿAtīd): i.e., he is the writer of evil deeds, and it is said: each is called by both, and Allah made the writer of good deeds an amir over the writer of evil deeds. So if he does a good deed, it is written immediately; and if he does an evil deed, the writer of evil deeds says: 'Write,' and the writer of good deeds says to him: 'Wait, perhaps he will seek forgiveness and repent.' So if he repents, he writes it as a good deed; but if he does not repent after six hours, then write; the writer of good deeds says to him: 'Write, may Allah give us relief from him.' And the scrolls of deeds are presented morning and evening to the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; and if he sees good, he praises Allah and thanks its doer, and if he sees other than that, he seeks forgiveness for its doer.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the categories of angels, specifically the guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓah) and the recording angels (al-katabah). It begins by defining the guardian angels as those entrusted with protecting humans, including children and disbelievers, and also from the jinn, supporting this with Qur'anic verses (13:11 and 17:70). It explains that this guardianship is an honor from Allah. Then it defines the recording angels as those who write down all deeds, speech (even inner speech), actions, and beliefs of the morally responsible person (al-mukallaf). The commentary elaborates on points in the main text: it notes that the bearers of the Throne are four in this world and eight in the hereafter, that the phrase 'from the jinn' includes afflictions and calamities, and that 'by the command of Allah' means protection from harm until the divine decree arrives, when the angels withdraw. It quotes Kaʿb al-Aḥbār's tradition about the guardian angels warding off jinn. The wisdom of recording deeds is to instill shyness and deter sin. Next, it discusses that the two recording angels do not leave the person except during intercourse, bathing, and relieving oneself; they recognize deeds by smell. It names the angels as al-Raqīb (watcher) and al-ʿAtīd (ready), citing Sūrat Qāf (50:18). There is a tradition that the writer of good deeds is an amir over the writer of evil deeds; if a good deed is done, it is written immediately, but if an evil deed is done, the writer of evil deeds is told to wait six hours in case the person repents; if repentance occurs, it is written as a good deed; otherwise, it is written after six hours. Finally, the passage states that the scrolls of deeds are presented to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) every morning and evening; he thanks Allah for good deeds and seeks forgiveness for bad ones.

Key Terms
الحفظة (al-ḥafaẓah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think guardian angels only protect believers.
Correction: The passage explicitly states they guard humans, even if a child or disbeliever.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the scope of protection by guardian angels?
A) They only guard believers.
B) They guard even children and disbelievers.
C) They only guard adults.
D) They do not guard disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Guardian angels are assigned to all humans as an honor, protecting them from harm until Allah's decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that guardian angels protect you every moment from countless harms. Have you ever thanked Allah for this unseen protection? Will you pause right now and express gratitude for the angels who guard you even as you read this?
?
The angels withdraw when Allah's decree arrives. If your final moment came today, are you prepared to meet your Lord? What is one specific sin you need to repent from, and when will you do it, knowing that protection could end at any instant?
?
The lesson says this guardianship is an honor from Allah. Does your life reflect that you value this honor? What change will you make today to live in a way that shows you are aware of being guarded by angels?

The Recording Angels (al-Katabah)
Al-Sawi explains the recording angels, their names, the delay for repentance, and the presentation of deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of recording angels, their names (Raqib and Atid), the delay for repentance, and the presentation of deeds to the Prophet.

Core Idea
Recording angels write every deed, even inner thoughts, and good deeds are prioritized through a delay for repentance.

Al-Sawi now turns to the recording angels (al-katabah), who document every word, action, and belief of the accountable person. He discusses the wisdom behind their writing, their names (al-Raqib and al-ʿAtīd), and the tradition that the writer of good deeds commands the writer of evil deeds to delay recording sins for six hours, hoping for repentance. Finally, the passage mentions that the scrolls of deeds are presented to the Prophet daily.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage for recording angels, then the translation. Identify the key functions described.
2
Identify the two angels
Note that the two recording angels are named al-Raqib (writer of good deeds) and al-ʿAtīd (writer of evil deeds).
Some traditions say each is called by both names.
3
Understand the delay for repentance
The writer of good deeds instructs the writer of evil deeds to wait six hours before recording a sin, in case the person repents.
If repentance occurs, the sin is written as a good deed.
4
Consider the presentation to the Prophet
The scrolls are presented to the Prophet morning and evening; he responds accordingly.

The Two Angels Raqib and Atid: Recording Deeds with Mercy
Al-Sawi explains the two angels and the delayed recording of sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identities and functions of the two recording angels and how Allah’s mercy delays the recording of sins to encourage repentance.

Core Idea
Allah's mercy delays sin recording for six hours, hoping for repentance.

This lesson delves into the names and functions of the two angels who record every person's deeds. Al-Sawi explains not only their identity but also the remarkable process by which a sin may be transformed into a good deed through repentance. The passage highlights Allah's mercy and the angels' interaction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get its rhythm and flow. Then read the literal translation carefully.
Notice the specific states where the angels are said not to leave (intercourse, bathing, relieving oneself).
2
Identify the two angels
Find the names ar-Raqib and al-Atid and understand their primary roles: one writes good deeds, the other bad deeds.
Also note the alternative opinion that each is called by both names.
3
Understand the process of recording
Observe the hierarchy: the scribe of good deeds is an amir over the scribe of bad deeds. Good deeds are recorded immediately, but bad deeds are delayed for six hours to allow repentance.
If the person repents within that time, the sin is recorded as a good deed.
4
Reflect on the mercy
Consider the mercy in this delay and the phrase 'arāḥanā Allāhu minhu' (may Allah give us relief from him) when the sin is finally recorded.
This emphasizes the angel's desire for the person's repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يفارقونه إلا في حالة الجماع والغُسل والخلاء)، والمشهور أنهما ملكان يسمى أحدهما : الرقيب، والثاني: العتيد، كما في سورة (ق)(٢). استحيا وترك المعصية. قوله : (لا يفارقونه إلَّا في حالة الجماع ... إلخ) : أي : فإذا فعل في تلك الأحوال الثَّلاث حسنة أو سيئة ؛ فإنَّهم يعرفونها بنتن رائحة السَّيِّئة وطيب رائحة الحسنة . قوله : (يسمى أحدهما : الرَّقيب أي : وهو كاتب الحسنات . وقوله : (والثَّاني: العتيد) : أي : وهو كاتب السَّيِّئات، وقيل : كلُّ يسمى بكل، وجعل الله كاتب الحسنات أميراً على كاتب السَّيِّئات، فإن فعل حسنة كتبت حالاً، وإن فعل سيِّئة يقول كاتب السَّيِّئات : اكتب، فيقول له كاتب الحسنات اصبر لعله يستغفر ويتوب، فإن تاب؛ كتب حسنة، فإن لم يتب بعد ست ساعات فلكيَّة ؛ قال له كاتب الحسنات: اكتب، اراحنا الله منه (۳).
They do not leave him except in the state of sexual intercourse, bathing, and relieving oneself. And the well-known [view] is that they are two angels, one of whom is called ar-Raqib and the other al-Atid, as in Surah Qaf (2). Be shy and leave sin. His statement: 'They do not leave him except in the state of sexual intercourse... etc.' meaning: if he does a good deed or a bad deed in those three situations, they know it by the stench of the bad deed and the pleasant smell of the good deed. His statement: 'One of them is called ar-Raqib' meaning he is the scribe of good deeds. And his statement: 'and the second: al-Atid' meaning he is the scribe of bad deeds. And it is said that each is called by both names. And Allah made the scribe of good deeds an amir over the scribe of bad deeds. So if he does a good deed, it is written immediately. And if he does a bad deed, the scribe of bad deeds says: Write. Then the scribe of good deeds says to him: Be patient, perhaps he will seek forgiveness and repent. So if he repents, he writes it as a good deed. If he does not repent after six hours, then [the scribe of bad deeds] has to; the scribe of good deeds says to him: Write, may Allah give us relief from him (3).
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage explains the two guardian angels (al-hafazah) that accompany every person. The author, al-Sawi, comments on a statement from the sharh (commentary) about the angels not leaving except during three specific states: sexual intercourse, bathing, and relieving oneself. He clarifies that even in those states, the angels are aware of good and bad deeds by their scent. He then identifies the two angels by name: ar-Raqib (the observer) is the scribe of good deeds, and al-Atid (the ready) is the scribe of bad deeds, though some say both names apply to each. A significant point is that Allah has made the scribe of good deeds a commander over the scribe of bad deeds, granting him authority to delay recording a sin for up to six hours in hope of repentance. If the person repents, the sin is recorded as a good deed; if not, after six hours the scribe writes it as a sin. The passage emphasizes mercy and encouragement to repent. The final phrase 'arāḥanā Allāhu minhu' (may Allah give us relief from him) is said by the angel of good deeds when finally writing the sin, indicating that the person's persistence is burdensome.

Key Terms
الرقيب
العتيد
كاتب الحسنات
كاتب السيئات
الحفظة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that during states like bathing or relieving oneself, the angels completely leave and are unaware of deeds.
Correction: The passage clarifies that although the angels do not accompany the person in those states, they still perceive good and bad deeds by their scent.

Checkpoint
How does the scribe of good deeds respond when the scribe of bad deeds wants to write a sin?
A) He immediately writes the sin.
B) He tells him to wait six hours in case the person repents.
C) He ignores the request.
D) He forgives the sin regardless.

Key Takeaway
The recording of sins is delayed for six hours to allow for repentance, and if repentance occurs, the sin is recorded as a good deed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that your sins are not recorded immediately but given a six-hour window for repentance. Think back to the last sin you committed: Did you sincerely repent within that window, or did you let it pass, relying on Allah's mercy without action? What will you do differently today to ensure you seize that opportunity?
?
The scribe of good deeds says 'arāhanā Allāhu minhu' (may Allah give us relief from him) when finally recording your unrepented sin after six hours. How does knowing that even the appointed angels feel 'relief' when a sinner is recorded affect your view of your own persistence in sin? Will you let this be a warning that breaks your pattern of delaying repentance?
?
The angels perceive the stench of a sin and the pleasant smell of a good deed. If you could smell the spiritual 'aroma' of your last 24 hours, would it be mostly fragrant or foul? What is one specific deed you can perform right now to change that scent, and how will you ensure you do it before the next six hours pass?

Presentation of Deeds to the Prophet
Al-Sawi states that deeds are shown to the Prophet morning and evening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the deeds of the Muslim community are presented to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and his response.

Core Idea
The Prophet sees our deeds morning and evening, thanking for good and seeking forgiveness for bad.

Al-Sawi begins by describing a unique aspect of the Prophet's connection to his community: he is shown the scrolls of deeds twice daily. This emphasizes his role as an intercessor and the mercy of Allah. In this lesson, we will examine the text that explains this presentation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is concise and directly states the fact.
2
Understand the Prophet's two responses
Identify the two scenarios: if he sees good, he praises Allah and thanks the doer; if otherwise, he seeks forgiveness. This shows his mercy.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about how this knowledge should affect your actions. Knowing that the Prophet sees your deeds twice daily can inspire mindfulness.
This connects to the importance of sincerity and repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتعرض صحائف الأعمال صباحاً ومساءً على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ؛ فإن رأى خيراً ؛ حمد الله وشكر لصاحبه، وإن رأى غير ذلك ؛ استغفر لفاعله (٤). ولكلّ يوم وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصر وصلاة الصبح، وقيل : بل هما ملكان فقط لا يتغيَّران ما دام حيّاً، فإذا مات جَلَسا على قبره يستغفران له، أي: إن كان مؤمناً. قوله : ( ولكلّ يوم وليلة ملكان ... إلخ ) : المعتمد أنَّ الحفظة: عشرة بالليل وعشرة بالنَّهار، ويجتمعون في صلاة الصبح والعصر، فيسألهم الله وهو أعلم بهم، فيقول لهم : كيف تركتم عبادي؟ فيقولون: يا ربَّنا ؛ تركناهم وهم يصلُّون، وأتيناهم وهم يصلُّون، كما ورد بذلك الحديث الصحيح (١).
And the scrolls of deeds are presented morning and evening to the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. If he sees good, he praises Allah and thanks its doer. If he sees other than that, he seeks forgiveness for its doer (4). And for every day and night, there are two angels who take turns at the afternoon prayer and the dawn prayer. And it is said that they are only two angels who do not change as long as one is alive, and when he dies, they sit on his grave asking forgiveness for him, i.e., if he is a believer. His statement: 'And for every day and night, two angels... etc.' The relied-upon view is that the guardian angels are ten at night and ten during the day, and they gather at the dawn and afternoon prayers. Allah asks them, and He knows best about them, 'How did you leave My servants?' They say: 'O our Lord, we left them while they were praying, and we came to them while they were praying,' as is related in the authentic hadith (1).
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage covers two related topics: the presentation of deeds to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and the nature of the guardian angels (hafazah). First, al-Sawi states that the scrolls of deeds are shown to the Prophet in the morning and evening. If the Prophet sees good deeds, he thanks Allah and praises the doer; if he sees bad deeds, he seeks forgiveness for the doer. This emphasizes the Prophet's mercy and intercession for his community. Second, the passage discusses the angels assigned to each person for each day and night. There is a view that two angels take turns, one for the day and one for the night, meeting at Asr and Fajr prayers. Another view says the same two angels remain throughout life and after death sit on the grave to pray for forgiveness (if the person is a believer). Al-Sawi then clarifies the relied-upon opinion: the guardian angels are actually ten by night and ten by day, who gather at Fajr and Asr. At these times, Allah asks them how they found His servants, and they reply that they found them praying. This is based on authentic hadith. The passage highlights the importance of prayer (salat) at these times.

Key Terms
صحائف الأعمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think their deeds are only recorded but not seen by the Prophet.
Correction: The hadith teaches that the Prophet is shown the deeds of his community twice daily, and he reacts accordingly.

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet do when he sees good deeds on the scrolls?
A) He remains silent.
B) He praises Allah and thanks the doer.
C) He seeks forgiveness.
D) He asks for more good deeds.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet is shown the deeds of his community twice daily, and he responds with praise for good and seeking forgiveness for bad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that the Prophet sees your deeds every morning and evening, which deed from today would make him thank you? Which deed would make him seek forgiveness for you? Will you consciously change one action tomorrow to increase the good he sees?
?
If the Prophet saw your actions this morning, would he have praised Allah for them? What about this evening? How does this awareness affect your next decision or habit?
?
The Prophet's response to your bad deeds is to seek forgiveness. Do you truly feel his mercy in that? How will you respond to his mercy today—by repenting, by improving, or by ignoring? What concrete step will you take within the next hour?

The Guardian Angels: Their Attendance and Testimony
Al-Sawi discusses the guardian angels, their times of attendance, and their testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of the guardian angels, their shifts, and their testimony at Fajr and Asr prayers.

Core Idea
Ten angels guard us by day and ten by night, testifying to Allah about our prayers at dawn and afternoon.

Al-Sawi now clarifies a point of difference about the angels assigned to each person. He presents two views and then states the relied-upon opinion, emphasizing the angels' attendance at Fajr and Asr and their testimony about the believers' prayer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the angels
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note that it contains multiple views.
The passage includes a quote from the author's own commentary.
2
Identify the two views
Find the first view (two angels taking turns) and the alternative view (two permanent angels). Understand the difference.
3
Note the relied-upon view
Al-Sawi states that the relied-upon view is ten angels by night and ten by day. Recognize that this is the established position.
4
Understand the testimony
At Fajr and Asr, the angels gather and Allah asks them about the servants. They reply that they found them praying.
This highlights the importance of these two prayers.

The Many Guardian Angels and Their Positions
Al-Sawi enumerates the guardian angels' positions and explains the forelock angel's role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific positions of the guardian angels that accompany a person and the special role of the angel who seizes the forelock.

Core Idea
Angels guard every side of a person, and the forelock angel responds to humility and arrogance.

Al-Sawi provides a vivid description of the guardian angels that never leave a person until death. He lists their exact positions around the body, including a special angel who holds the forelock and reacts to the person's character. This passage gives a concrete image of divine care and accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully.
Read the Arabic text once through, then read the translation. Notice the detailed list of angel positions.
The passage uses specific body parts.
2
Identify each angel's location.
List each angel mentioned: right, left, front, back, eyes, lips, mouth, forelock. Note that some positions have two angels.
The forelock angel has unique behavior.
3
Understand the forelock angel's function.
The angel seizing the forelock responds to the person’s humility or arrogance. This shows that angels are not passive but actively interact.
This angel can raise or lower the person.
4
Reflect on the meaning.
Think about why this detailed description matters for understanding divine care and accountability.
It emphasizes constant divine attention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يفارقون الشَّخص أبداً إلى الممات، فإذا مات؛ فقد فرغ حفظهم وهم واحد عن يمينه وآخر عن شماله وآخر أمامه وآخر خلفه، واثنان على عينيه وواحد على شفتيه واثنان على فمه يحفظان الصَّلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وواحد آخذ بناصيته ؛ فإن تواضع رفعه، وإن تكبر خفضه. إن قلت : إِنَّا نجد تخلف حفظهم له بأن تفقأ عينه مثلاً . يجاب بأنَّ هذا أمر مبرم فلا بدَّ من إنفاذه، وهكذا كلُّ مبرم. قوله : (إن كان مؤمناً ) أي : ويلعنانه إن كان كافراً.
And they never leave the person until death. So when he dies, their guarding ends. And they are: one on his right, one on his left, one in front of him, one behind him, two on his eyes, one on his lips, two on his mouth preserving the prayer upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and one seizing his forelock. If he humbles himself, it raises him; if he is arrogant, it lowers him. If you say: 'We find a failure of their preservation of him, such as when his eye is poked out, for example.' The answer is that this is a decreed matter that must be carried out, and likewise every decreed matter. His statement: 'If he is a believer' means that they curse him if he is a disbeliever.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed description of the guardian angels (hafazah) that accompany a person until death. Al-Sawi lists their positions: one on the right, one on the left, one in front, one behind, two on the eyes, one on the lips, two on the mouth (specifically to preserve the prayer upon the Prophet), and one holding the forelock. The angel holding the forelock rewards humility by raising the person and punishes arrogance by lowering him. The author then addresses an objection: if these angels are supposed to guard the person, why does harm sometimes reach him, such as having an eye poked out? The answer is that such events are divinely decreed (mubram) and must happen; the angels’ preservation does not prevent decreed calamities. This clarifies the scope of the angels’ role: they are guardians of record and intercession, not preventers of divine decrees. Finally, al-Sawi comments on the earlier phrase 'if he is a believer' (regarding the angels at the grave), explaining that if the person is a disbeliever, the angels curse him instead of seeking forgiveness.

Key Terms
حفظة
ناصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many angels are stationed on the eyes?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The guardian angels are positioned all around a person, and the forelock angel actively responds to humility or arrogance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that an angel is seizing your forelock and will lift you if you humble yourself, what specific act of humility have you been avoiding because of pride? Will you perform it today?
?
If the guardian angels never leave you until death, how does that change your awareness of your actions right now? Are you living as if you are always watched?
?
The forelock angel lowers the arrogant person. Is there any area of your life where you feel entitled or superior to others? What would it look like to deliberately humble yourself in that area today?

Objection About Preservation and the Divine Decree
Al-Sawi answers an objection about preservation and clarifies the believers' and disbelievers' treatment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that harm can occur despite the angels' preservation and the answer that such events are divinely decreed.

Core Idea
Angels guard but do not prevent decreed calamities.

Someone might wonder why, if angels are guarding a person, harm can still come to them, such as an eye being poked out. Al-Sawi addresses this by explaining that certain events are divinely determined and must occur. This lesson clarifies the scope of angelic preservation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer.
Read the objection starting with 'إن قلت' and the answer 'يجاب بأن'. Understand the flow.
This is a classical dialectical structure.
2
Identify the objection.
The objection is that we sometimes see a failure of preservation, e.g., an eye being poked out.
The example is 'تفقأ عينه'.
3
Understand the answer.
The answer is that such harm is an 'أمر مبرم' (a decreed matter) that must be executed.
This applies to all decreed matters.
4
Consider the believer/disbeliever comment.
The passage ends with a clarification about the angels' treatment of believers versus disbelievers.
This ties back to earlier mention of the grave.

The Number and Alternation of Guardian Angels
Al-Sawi presents two views on the number of guardian angels and their alternation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two views on the number of guardian angels and how they alternate at prayer times.

Core Idea
Guardian angels are twenty—ten by day and ten by night—alternating at dawn and afternoon prayers.

This lesson focuses on the angels appointed to guard every person. Al-Sawi presents two views: some say two fixed angels, but the relied-upon view is that there are twenty—ten by day and ten by night. They gather at specific prayer times and report to Allah about the worshippers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on angel numbers
Read the Arabic text about the two angels alternating and the relied-upon view of ten by night and ten by day.
The phrase 'المعتمد' signals the authoritative opinion.
2
Understand the alternation at prayer times
Notice that the angels gather at the afternoon (ʿaṣr) and dawn (fajr) prayers. Reflect on why these times are significant for reporting deeds.
Allah asks the angels about His servants, showing His care.
3
Compare the two views
Contrast the first opinion (only two angels that change) with the relied-upon view (twenty angels).
The hadith supports the twenty-angel view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالملائكة والجن
ولكلّ يوم وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصر وصلاة الصبح، وقيل : بل هما ملكان فقط لا يتغيَّران ما دام حيّاً، فإذا مات جَلَسا على قبره يستغفران له، أي: إن كان مؤمناً.
قوله : ( ولكلّ يوم وليلة ملكان ... إلخ ) : المعتمد أنَّ الحفظة: عشرة بالليل وعشرة بالنَّهار، ويجتمعون في صلاة الصبح والعصر، فيسألهم الله وهو أعلم بهم، فيقول لهم : كيف تركتم عبادي؟ فيقولون: يا ربَّنا ؛ تركناهم وهم يصلُّون، وأتيناهم وهم يصلُّون، كما ورد بذلك الحديث الصحيح.
ولا يفارقون الشَّخص أبداً إلى الممات، فإذا مات؛ فقد فرغ حفظهم
وهم واحد عن يمينه وآخر عن شماله وآخر أمامه وآخر خلفه، واثنان على عينيه وواحد على شفتيه واثنان على فمه يحفظان الصَّلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وواحد آخذ بناصيته ؛ فإن تواضع رفعه، وإن تكبر خفضه.
إن قلت : إِنَّا نجد تخلف حفظهم له بأن تفقأ عينه مثلاً .
يجاب بأنَّ هذا أمر مبرم فلا بدَّ من إنفاذه، وهكذا كلُّ مبرم.
قوله : (إن كان مؤمناً ) أي : ويلعنانه إن كان كافراً.
حياتي خير لكم تحدثون ويحدث لكم ووفاتي خير لكم تعرض علي أعمالكم فما رأيت من خير؛ حمدت الله عليه وما رأيت من شر؛ استغفرت الله لكم».
صحيح البخاري (٥٥٥) ، صحيح مسلم (٦٣٢) عن أبي هريرة الله
ومحلُّهما من الإنسان عاتقاه، وقيل: ذقنه، وقيل: شفتاه، وقيل: عنقه، وقيل: الناجذان ، وقيل : إنّ الكَتَبَة هم الحَفَظَة، وبالجملة الواجبُ اعتقاده أنّ على الإنسان حَفَظة وكتبة على سبيل الإجمال.
Belief in angels and jinn. And for every day and night there are two angels who alternate at the time of the afternoon prayer and the dawn prayer, and it is said: rather they are only two angels who do not change as long as he lives, and when he dies they sit on his grave seeking forgiveness for him, that is, if he was a believer. His statement: (And for every day and night there are two angels... etc.): The relied-upon view is that the guardians (al-ḥafaẓa) are ten at night and ten during the day, and they gather at the dawn and afternoon prayers, and Allah asks them—and He knows best about them—saying: 'How did you leave My servants?' They say: 'Our Lord, we left them while they were praying, and we came to them while they were praying,' as is related in the authentic hadith. And they never leave the person until death, and when he dies, their guard duty ends. And they are: one on his right, another on his left, another in front of him, another behind him, two on his eyes, one on his lips, two on his mouth preserving the prayer upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and one holding his forelock; if he humbles himself, he raises him, and if he becomes arrogant, he lowers him. If you say: Indeed we find a failure of their preservation of him, for example when his eye is gouged out. The answer is: This is a predetermined matter, and it must be carried out, and so is every predetermined matter. His statement: (if he was a believer) meaning: and they curse him if he was a disbeliever. 'My life is good for you: you talk and things happen, and my death is good for you: your deeds are presented to me; whatever good I see, I praise Allah for it, and whatever evil I see, I ask Allah's forgiveness for you.' (Sahih al-Bukhari (555), Sahih Muslim (632) from Abu Hurairah may Allah be pleased with him). And their place on the human is his collarbones, and it is said: his chin, and it is said: his lips, and it is said: his neck, and it is said: the back teeth (al-nājidhān), and it is said: indeed the scribes (al-kataba) are the guardians. In summary, what must be believed is that upon every human there are guardians and scribes in a general way.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on belief in angels. It begins by stating that for every day and night there are two angels who alternate at the two specific prayer times (afternoon and dawn). Some say these are only two fixed angels who do not change during the person's life; after death they sit on the grave and seek forgiveness for the believer. The commentator then clarifies the relied-upon view: the guardians (ḥafaẓa) are twenty in total—ten by night and ten by day. They gather at the dawn and afternoon prayers, and Allah asks them about the state of His servants, to which they reply that they found them praying. The passage then describes the locations of these angels on the human body: one on the right, one on the left, one in front, one behind, two on the eyes, one on the lips, two on the mouth (to record blessings on the Prophet), and one holding the forelock, who raises the humble and lowers the arrogant. An objection is raised: if angels preserve the person, how can harm like a gouged eye occur? The answer is that such matters are divinely preordained and must occur regardless of the angels' protection. The commentary then notes that if the person is a believer, the angels seek forgiveness; if a disbeliever, they curse. A hadith is cited showing the Prophet's life and death benefit the community. Finally, there is discussion about the exact location of the two recording angels (some say collarbones, chin, lips, neck, or back teeth) and a note that some consider the scribes (kataba) to be the same as the guardians, but the summary obligation is to believe that there are guardians and scribes over each person in general terms.

Key Terms
الحفظة
ملكان
التعاقب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think there are only two guardian angels that never change.
Correction: The relied-upon view is that there are twenty—ten by day and ten by night.

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in this passage, how many guardians are there for each person?
A) Two
B) Ten
C) Twenty
D) Four

Key Takeaway
There are twenty guardian angels for each person—ten by day and ten by night—who alternate at dawn and afternoon prayers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels will report to Allah at Fajr and Asr that they found you doing such-and-such. What will they say about you this very day? Are you prepared for that report? If not, what will you change before those prayers?
?
You are never alone—ten angels by day and ten by night watch you. Does this knowledge make you more careful in private? Think of a specific sin you commit when no one sees you. Will you leave it now, knowing you are seen?
?
The angels gather at Fajr and Asr. If these prayers are missing from your day, you are not present when the angels witness and Allah asks. What is more important than being with the angels at those times? Will you commit to praying Fajr and Asr on time starting today?

Locations and Functions of the Guardian Angels
Al-Sawi enumerates the locations of the guardian angels on the human body and their respective functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific placement of guardian angels on the human body and their specific functions, including recording prayers and humbling the arrogant.

Core Idea
Angels are placed on specific body parts—right, left, front, back, eyes, lips, mouth, and forelock—each with a distinct duty.

This lesson details where the guardian angels are positioned on a person's body and what each does. Al-Sawi describes nine angels with precise locations, including one on the forelock that raises the humble and lowers the arrogant. This vivid picture deepens our understanding of divine surveillance and care.

Guided Path
1
Learn the positions
Read the list of angel positions: on the right, left, front, back, on each eye, on the lips, two on the mouth, and one on the forelock.
Notice the symmetry and the special role of the forelock angel.
2
Understand each function
For each position, reflect on what the angel does. The mouth angels preserve prayers upon the Prophet, and the forelock angel responds to humility or arrogance.
The forelock angel's action links directly to one's character.
3
Reflect on divine care
Think about how these detailed placements show Allah's complete awareness and care for every moment and action of a person.
This complements the belief in accountability.

الإيمان بالملائكة والجن
ولكلّ يوم وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصر وصلاة الصبح، وقيل : بل هما ملكان فقط لا يتغيَّران ما دام حيّاً، فإذا مات جَلَسا على قبره يستغفران له، أي: إن كان مؤمناً.
قوله : ( ولكلّ يوم وليلة ملكان ... إلخ ) : المعتمد أنَّ الحفظة: عشرة بالليل وعشرة بالنَّهار، ويجتمعون في صلاة الصبح والعصر، فيسألهم الله وهو أعلم بهم، فيقول لهم : كيف تركتم عبادي؟ فيقولون: يا ربَّنا ؛ تركناهم وهم يصلُّون، وأتيناهم وهم يصلُّون، كما ورد بذلك الحديث الصحيح.
ولا يفارقون الشَّخص أبداً إلى الممات، فإذا مات؛ فقد فرغ حفظهم
وهم واحد عن يمينه وآخر عن شماله وآخر أمامه وآخر خلفه، واثنان على عينيه وواحد على شفتيه واثنان على فمه يحفظان الصَّلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وواحد آخذ بناصيته ؛ فإن تواضع رفعه، وإن تكبر خفضه.
إن قلت : إِنَّا نجد تخلف حفظهم له بأن تفقأ عينه مثلاً .
يجاب بأنَّ هذا أمر مبرم فلا بدَّ من إنفاذه، وهكذا كلُّ مبرم.
قوله : (إن كان مؤمناً ) أي : ويلعنانه إن كان كافراً.
حياتي خير لكم تحدثون ويحدث لكم ووفاتي خير لكم تعرض علي أعمالكم فما رأيت من خير؛ حمدت الله عليه وما رأيت من شر؛ استغفرت الله لكم».
صحيح البخاري (٥٥٥) ، صحيح مسلم (٦٣٢) عن أبي هريرة الله
ومحلُّهما من الإنسان عاتقاه، وقيل: ذقنه، وقيل: شفتاه، وقيل: عنقه، وقيل: الناجذان ، وقيل : إنّ الكَتَبَة هم الحَفَظَة، وبالجملة الواجبُ اعتقاده أنّ على الإنسان حَفَظة وكتبة على سبيل الإجمال.

Objection about Harm and the Angels' Afterlife Role
Al-Sawi addresses an objection about angelic protection and explains the angels' role in the grave and the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to reconcile the angels' protective function with worldly harm, and what happens after death regarding forgiveness or curse.

Core Idea
Worldly harm is divinely predestined and does not contradict angelic protection; after death, angels seek forgiveness for believers or curse disbelievers.

This lesson tackles a common theological objection: if angels guard a person, how can harm occur? Al-Sawi answers that predetermined events override protection. It also explains the angels' role after death—seeking forgiveness for believers or cursing disbelievers—and includes a hadith about the Prophet's intercession for his community.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the question about a gouged eye and the answer that it is a predetermined matter that must happen.
This shows the principle of qadr in relation to angelic functions.
2
Understand the afterlife role
After death, the angels sit on the grave and either seek forgiveness (for believers) or curse (for disbelievers).
This applies if the angels are the two fixed angels from the first view.
3
Reflect on the hadith
Read the hadith where the Prophet says his life and death benefit the community because his deeds are presented to him.
This reinforces the concept of intercession and divine mercy.

The Location of Recording Angels and Distinction from Guardians
Al-Sawi discusses the location of recording angels and rejects equating scribes with guardians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various scholarly opinions on the physical location of the recording angels and the correct distinction between the scribes (كتبة) and the guardians (حفظة).

Core Idea
The recording angels sit on the shoulders, but scribes and guardians are distinct groups.

Al-Sawi presents multiple views on where the two recording angels are located in the human body, ranging from shoulders to teeth. He then addresses a common misunderstanding that the scribes and guardians are the same, clarifying that they are separate angelic groups with different numbers and roles.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the continuous Arabic passage once without pausing on each variant. Then compare with the translation to ensure full understanding of the opinions listed.
The passage contains several 'قيل' (it is said) phrases listing different locations.
2
Identify the location opinions
List all five locations mentioned: shoulders, chin, lips, neck, and molars. Note that the molars opinion includes additional details about pen and ink.
The text elaborates on the molars opinion in a separate commentary line.
3
Recognize the weak opinion and the correction
Notice the weak opinion that scribes equal guardians. The correct view distinguishes them: guardians are 20, scribes are the two angels Raqib and Atid.
This is the key doctrinal point: they are distinct groups.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومحلُّهما من الإنسان عاتقاه، وقيل: ذقنه، وقيل: شفتاه، وقيل: عنقه، وقيل: الناجذان، وقيل: إنّ الكَتَبَة هم الحَفَظَة، وبالجملة الواجبُ اعتقاده أنّ على الإنسان حَفَظة وكتبة على سبيل الإجمال. قوله : (وقيل : النَّاجذان) هما مؤخّر أضراسه اليمين واليسار، وقلمهما لسانه ومدادهما ريقه. قوله : (وقيل : إنَّ الكتبة هم الحفظة: هذا ضعيف، والمعتمد أنَّهم غيرهم، فالحفظة عشرون بالليل والنَّهار، والكتبة ملكان رقيب وعتيد كما علمت.
And their location in man is his shoulders, and it is said: his chin, and it is said: his lips, and it is said: his neck, and it is said: the two molars, and it is said: indeed the scribes are the guardians, and in summary what must be believed is that man has guardians and scribes in general. He said: '(And it is said: the two molars)'—they are the back molars on the right and left, and their pen is his tongue and their ink is his saliva. He said: '(And it is said: indeed the scribes are the guardians): this is weak, and the relied-upon view is that they are other than them, for the guardians are twenty by night and day, and the scribes are two angels—Raqib and Atid—as you know.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a previous statement about the location of the two recording angels (the scribes). It begins by enumerating various opinions on where these angels are located in the human body: shoulders, chin, lips, neck, molars. Then it mentions a weak opinion that the scribes (كتبة) are the same as the guardians (حفظة). The author then clarifies the required belief: one must believe in general that there are guardians and scribes, without needing to specify the exact location. The subsequent commentary refutes the weak opinion, stating that the correct view is that the guardians are twenty angels (ten by night, ten by day) while the scribes are two specific angels named Raqib and Atid. The author emphasizes that this distinction is based on what is known.

Key Terms

الناجذان

Correction: They are distinct: guardians are twenty angels, while scribes are two angels named Raqib and Atid.

Checkpoint

A) Guardians: 20, Scribes: 2

C) Guardians: 10, Scribes: 4

Key Takeaway
The scribes (Raqib and Atid) are two specific angels, while the guardians are twenty; they are not the same group.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
Knowing that twenty guardians protect you while only two record your deeds, does your gratitude for Allah's protection increase? How will you show that appreciation in a tangible action before the day ends?

Belief in the Maidens of Paradise (Hur al-Ayn)
Sawi defines 'Hur al-Ayn' and states the obligation to believe in them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the Hur al-Ayn is obligatory and the linguistic meaning of the term 'Hawra'.

Core Idea
Belief in the Hur al-Ayn is obligatory; their name comes from the contrast of their eyes.

This lesson begins a discussion of the sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation) concerning the inhabitants of Paradise. The author affirms the obligation to believe in the existence of the Hur, and provides a linguistic explanation of the term. Understanding this foundation is essential before exploring further descriptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

The passage is incomplete but still conveys a clear point.
2

3
Understand the linguistic definition
The commentator defines 'Hawar' as extreme whiteness of the eye with extreme blackness. Reflect on how this physical description fits the beauty of Paradise.
This definition helps distinguish the Hur from ordinary beings.
4
Recognize the literal belief
The passage treats the Hur as real created entities, not mere symbols. This literal affirmation is a standard Sunni position.

Source Text

The passage is incomplete in this window, but it establishes that these are actual beings in Paradise that believers must affirm.

Faith in al-Hur al-'Ayn
Sanusi explains the nature and creation of al-Hur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature, creation, and characteristics of al-Hur al-'Ayn as described in the Islamic tradition and the importance of believing in them.

Core Idea
Al-Hur are created from mercy, yet believing women surpass them seventy thousand fold.

This lesson explores the eschatological reality of al-Hur, the beautiful maidens of Paradise. The passage clarifies their linguistic meaning, their creation from drops of mercy, their dwellings, and notably their superiority over the believing women of this world. It also emphasizes the obligation to believe in them.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Hur
Read the Arabic text that defines al-Hur linguistically and states their characteristics. Notice the obligation to believe in their existence.
The word 'Hawra' denotes intense white and black of the eye.
2
Understand the creation tradition
Read the tradition about their creation from drops of mercy and their tents. Reflect on the symbolic meaning of the tent splitting open.
The Quranic verse 'Hur, secluded in pavilions' is referenced.
3
Note the correct view on superiority
Pay attention to the final statement that the believing women of this world are superior to al-Hur. This is a key theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالحور والولدان
(و) يجب الإيمان بوجود (الحور) جمع حَوْراء، والحَوَر : شدَّة بياض العين مع شدة سوادها.
وهنَّ نساء الجنَّة، ووُصِفْن بالدمين لاتساع أعينهنَّ .
(والولدان) أي : العلمان [؟]، وهم على صورة علمان [؟] الدُّنيا، وهم تقدمة أهل الجنة ، وقيل : إنَّهم أولاد الكفَّار الذين يموتون قبل البلوغ ؛ فقد ورد أنهم خَدَمَة أهل الجنة .
قوله: (وهنَّ نساء الجنَّة) روي أن سحابة أمطرت من العرش فخلقت الحور من قطرات الرَّحمة، ثمَّ ضرب على كلِّ واحدة منهنَّ خيمة على شاطئ الأنهار سعتها أربعون ميلاً، وليس لها باب حتَّى إذا حلَّ ولي الله الجنة التصدعت الخيمة عن باب ؛ ليعلم وليُّ الله أنَّ أبصار المخلوقين من الملائكة والخدم لم تأخذها، فهي مقصورة قد قصر بها عن أبصار المخلوقين ) ، وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: حُورٌ مَّقْصُورَاتٌ فِي القِيَامِ ) (٢) ، (١) والصَّحيح أنَّ نساء الدُّنيا يكن أفضل من الحور العين بسبعين ألف ضعف
قوله :((والولدان) بكسر الواو، جمع وليد بمعنى مولود وسموا أولاداً ؛ لكونهم على شكلهم وصورتهم.
قوله: (وهم خدمة أهل الجنَّة أي فهم مخلوقون في الجنَّة ابتداء؛ كالحور العين، ليسوا من أولاد الدُّنيا، وهو الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، وقيل : هم أولاد المؤمنين الذين ماتوا صغاراً.
Faith in al-Hur and al-Wildan. (And) it is obligatory to believe in the existence of al-Hur, plural of Hawra', and al-Hawar is intense whiteness of the eye with intense blackness of it. And they are the women of Paradise, and they are described as having wide eyes due to the width of their eyes. (And al-Wildan) meaning the servants [?], and they are in the form of the servants [?] of this world, and they are the advance gift of the people of Paradise, and it is said that they are the children of the disbelievers who die before puberty; for it has been reported that they are the servants of the people of Paradise. His saying: (And they are the women of Paradise): It is related that a cloud rained from the Throne and the Hur were created from drops of mercy, then for each one of them a tent was pitched on the bank of rivers, its width forty miles, and it has no door until when a friend of God enters Paradise, the tent splits open into a door, so that the friend of God knows that the eyes of creatures, angels and servants, did not behold them; so they are secluded, having been secluded from the eyes of creatures. And this is the meaning of His saying: 'Hur, secluded in pavilions' (Quran 55:72). And the correct view is that the women of this world are better than the Hur al-'Ayn by seventy thousand fold. His saying: (And al-Wildan) with a kasra on the waw, plural of walid meaning newborn, and they are called children because they are in their form and shape. His saying: (And they are the servants of the people of Paradise) meaning they are created in Paradise from the beginning, like the Hur al-'Ayn; they are not from the children of this world. This is the correct view among many opinions. And it is said: they are the children of the believers who died young.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a definition and description of two eschatological realities: al-Hur al-'Ayn and al-Wildan. It begins with the obligation to believe in both. The commentary first explains the linguistic meaning of 'Hur': the plural of 'Hawra'', which denotes intense whiteness of the eye with intense blackness. The Hur are described as having wide eyes. Then it mentions that they are the women of Paradise. Next, 'al-Wildan' are defined: they are servants (likely 'ghilman') in the form of the servants of this world, and they are an advance gift for the people of Paradise. There is an opinion that they are the children of disbelievers who die before puberty, but the report states they are servants. The commentary then elaborates on the Hur: a tradition says they were created from drops of mercy from a cloud that rained from the Throne. Each Hur has a large tent (forty miles wide) on the bank of rivers, with no door until a friend of God enters Paradise, at which point the tent splits to reveal a door. This shows that the Hur are secluded from the sight of all creatures, which is the meaning of the Quranic verse 'Hur, secluded in pavilions' (55:72). Importantly, the correct view is that the believing women of this world are superior to the Hur by seventy thousand fold. Finally, the commentary returns to al-Wildan: the word is a plural of 'walid' (newborn), so they are called 'children' because they resemble children in form. The correct view is that they are created directly in Paradise as servants, not from the children of this world—though some say they are the children of believers who died young.

Key Terms
الحور
الحَوَر
مقصورة
الحور العين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Houris are superior in rank to believing women in Paradise.
Correction: The passage states clearly: 'the correct view is that the women of this world are better than the Hur al-'Ayn by seventy thousand fold.'

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in this passage, how do the believing women of this world compare to the Hur al-'Ayn?
A) They are equal in rank.
B) They are inferior by seventy thousand fold.
C) They are superior by seventy thousand fold.
D) No comparison is made.

Key Takeaway
The believing women of this world are superior to the Houris, and the Houris are created from mercy and secluded for the saints.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine Paradise, do you focus more on its physical delights like the Hur, or on the pleasure of being near Allah? The Hur are a mercy, but are they the ultimate goal?
?
If a believing woman surpasses the Hur by 70,000 fold, then what does that imply about the spiritual potential of your own faith and actions? Are you living up to that potential?
?
The Hur are secluded and only revealed to the friends of Allah. Are you striving to become one of those friends, or are you content with lesser pursuits?

Faith in al-Wildan
Sanusi defines al-Wildan and clarifies their origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who the Wildan are in Paradise, their role as servants, and the correct view about their origin.

Core Idea
The Wildan are created directly in Paradise as servants, not from the children of this world.

This lesson focuses on al-Wildan, the youthful servants of Paradise. The passage explains their linguistic meaning, their form, and the different opinions about their origin. The correct view establishes that they are specially created for service, not derived from any human children.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Wildan
Read the Arabic text identifying al-Wildan as servants in the form of children. Note the linguistic meaning: plural of 'walid' meaning newborn.
The word 'wildan' is related to 'walad' (child).
2
Understand the two opinions
The passage mentions two opinions: one says they are children of disbelievers who died young, another says they are children of believers who died young. Read carefully which one is cited and corrected.
3
Note the correct view
The passage concludes that the correct view is that they are created directly in Paradise as servants, like the Hur. This clarifies their origin.

The Hur al-Ayn: Women of Paradise
Al-Sawi describes the Hur al-Ayn and their superiority relative to worldly women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature, origin, and confinement of the Hur al-Ayn, as well as the superiority of worldly women over them.

Core Idea
The Hur al-Ayn are created from mercy, but worldly women are better by 70,000 times.

Al-Sawi begins by describing the Hur al-Ayn as women of Paradise with wide eyes, then narrates their miraculous creation from drops of mercy and their confinement in pavilions. A striking comparison follows, elevating the women of this world above them. This lesson unpacks the beautiful description and the doctrinal point about their rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the Hur al-Ayn
Read the Arabic passage describing the Hur al-Ayn, noting their wide eyes and the initial mention of the Wildan in parentheses. Then read the translation to grasp the full meaning.
The Wildan are mentioned briefly here, but the focus is on the Hur.
2
Understand the creation from mercy
Pay attention to the narration: a cloud rained from the Throne, and the Hur were created from drops of mercy. This highlights their blessed origin.
3
Grasp the tent narrative and its symbolism
Each Hur has a vast tent without a door, which splits open only when a saint enters, showing that no creature has seen her. This illustrates the verse 'Hur, confined in pavilions.'
4
Learn the superiority of worldly women
The passage states that the women of this world are better than the Hur by seventy thousand times. This is a key doctrinal point that clarifies their relative status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهنَّ نساء الجنَّة، ووُصِفْن بالدَّمَين لاتساع أعينهنَّ . (والولدان) أي : العِلْمان، وهم على صورة عِلْمان الدُّنيا، وهم تقدمة أهل الجنة ، وقيل : إنَّهم أولاد الكفَّار الذين يموتون قبل البلوغ ؛ وورد أنهم خَدَمَة أهل الجنة . قوله: (وهنَّ نساء الجنَّة) روي أن سحابة أمطرت من العرش فخلقت الحور من قطرات الرَّحمة، ثمَّ ضرب على كلِّ واحدة منهنَّ خيمة على شاطئ الأنهار سعتها أربعون ميلاً، وليس لها باب حتَّى إذا حلَّ ولي الله الجنة التصدعت الخيمة عن باب ؛ ليعلم وليُّ الله أنَّ أبصار المخلوقين من الملائكة والخدم لم تأخذها، فهي مقصورة قد قصرت بها عن أبصار المخلوقين ، وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: حُورٌ مَّقْصُورَاتٌ فِي الخِيَامِ) ، (1) والصَّحيح أنَّ نساء الدُّنيا يكن أفضل من الحور العين بسبعين ألف ضعف (2) قوله :((والولدان) بكسر الواو، جمع وليد بمعنى مولود وسموا أولاداً ؛ لكونهم على شكلهم وصورتهم. قوله: (وهم خدمة أهل الجنَّة) أي فهم مخلوقون في الجنَّة ابتداءً؛ كالحور العين، ليسوا من أولاد الدُّنيا، وهو الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، وقيل : هم أولاد المؤمنين الذين ماتوا صغاراً.
And they are the women of Paradise, described as having wide eyes. (And the wildan) i.e., the servant boys, and they are in the form of the servant boys of this world, and they are the advance gifts of the people of Paradise. And it is said: They are the children of disbelievers who die before puberty, and it is reported that they are the servants of the people of Paradise. His statement: (And they are the women of Paradise): It is narrated that a cloud rained from the Throne and created the hur from drops of mercy, then a tent was pitched for each of them on the bank of the rivers, its width forty miles, and it has no door, until when a saint of Allah enters Paradise, the tent splits open at a door, so that the saint of Allah knows that the eyes of creatures, angels and servants, have not taken her; so she is confined, having been confined from the eyes of creatures. And this is the meaning of His statement, exalted: 'Hur, confined in pavilions.' (1) And the correct view is that the women of this world are better than the hur al-ayn by seventy thousand times. (2) His statement: (And the wildan) with kasrah on the waw, plural of walid meaning born, and they are called 'wildan' because they are in their shape and form. His statement: (And they are the servants of the people of Paradise), i.e., they are created in Paradise initially, like the hur al-ayn, not from the children of this world, and this is the correct among many sayings. And it is said: They are the children of the believers who died young.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a descriptive commentary on two categories of Paradise's inhabitants: the hur al-ayn (the women of Paradise) and the wildan (servant boys). It begins by stating that the women of Paradise are described as having wide eyes. Then it mentions the wildan: they are servant boys in the form of the servant boys of this world, and they are presented as gifts to the people of Paradise. There is a view that they are the children of disbelievers who die before puberty, but it is also reported that they are the servants of the people of Paradise. The commentary then expands on the hur al-ayn: it narrates a tradition that a cloud rained from the Throne, and from drops of mercy the hur were created. Each hur has a tent on the riverbank, forty miles wide, without a door. When a saint of Allah enters Paradise, the tent splits open at a door to show that no creature—angel or servant—has seen her; she is completely confined from the eyes of creatures. This illustrates the verse 'Hur, confined in pavilions.' The passage then declares that the correct view is that the women of this world are superior to the hur al-ayn by seventy thousand times. Finally, it returns to the wildan: they are called 'wildan' because they are in the shape and form of children. They are created directly in Paradise, like the hur, not from the children of this world; this is the correct opinion among several. An alternative view holds they are the children of believers who died young.

Key Terms
حور عين
قطرات الرحمة
مقصورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Hur al-Ayn are superior to worldly women.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that worldly women are better by 70,000 times.

Checkpoint

A) They are equal in rank.
B) They are better by seventy thousand times.
C) They are lesser in rank.
D) They are not mentioned.

Key Takeaway
The Hur al-Ayn are created from mercy and confined, but worldly women hold a higher rank by seventy thousand times.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Hur are created from pure mercy and confined until their destined companion arrives. How does this shape your understanding of divine mercy and patience? Are you willing to wait for Allah's mercy with the same patience?
?
If the women of this world are superior to the Hur by 70,000 times, what does that demand from you in terms of gratitude and responsibility toward the women in your life? Will you commit today to honoring them as the precious souls they are?

The Wildan: Servant Boys of Paradise
Al-Sawi explains correct view on the origin of the Wildan and refutes other opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct view regarding the origin and nature of the Wildan (servant boys) in Paradise.

Core Idea
The Wildan are created directly in Paradise, not from children of this world.

Al-Sawi devotes a separate section to the Wildan, clarifying their identity and origin. He presents multiple opinions and endorses the view that they are created in Paradise from the beginning, similar to the Hur al-Ayn. This lesson resolves common confusion about who the Wildan are.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Wildan
Read the Arabic passage, from the second 'qawl' (His statement) to the end. Notice the linguistic note about the word 'wildan'.
The passage begins with 'His statement: (And the wildan)'.
2
Identify the different opinions
The passage lists several opinions: 1) They are children of disbelievers who die before puberty, 2) They are servants of Paradise, 3) They are created in Paradise (correct), 4) They are children of believers who died young.
3
Understand the correct view
Al-Sawi states that the correct view is that they are created in Paradise initially, like the Hur al-Ayn. This distinguishes them from the children of this world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهنَّ نساء الجنَّة، ووُصِفْن بالدَّمَين لاتساع أعينهنَّ . (والولدان) أي : العِلْمان، وهم على صورة عِلْمان الدُّنيا، وهم تقدمة أهل الجنة ، وقيل : إنَّهم أولاد الكفَّار الذين يموتون قبل البلوغ ؛ وورد أنهم خَدَمَة أهل الجنة . قوله: (وهنَّ نساء الجنَّة) روي أن سحابة أمطرت من العرش فخلقت الحور من قطرات الرَّحمة، ثمَّ ضرب على كلِّ واحدة منهنَّ خيمة على شاطئ الأنهار سعتها أربعون ميلاً، وليس لها باب حتَّى إذا حلَّ ولي الله الجنة التصدعت الخيمة عن باب ؛ ليعلم وليُّ الله أنَّ أبصار المخلوقين من الملائكة والخدم لم تأخذها، فهي مقصورة قد قصرت بها عن أبصار المخلوقين ، وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: حُورٌ مَّقْصُورَاتٌ فِي الخِيَامِ) ، (1) والصَّحيح أنَّ نساء الدُّنيا يكن أفضل من الحور العين بسبعين ألف ضعف (2) قوله :((والولدان) بكسر الواو، جمع وليد بمعنى مولود وسموا أولاداً ؛ لكونهم على شكلهم وصورتهم. قوله: (وهم خدمة أهل الجنَّة) أي فهم مخلوقون في الجنَّة ابتداءً؛ كالحور العين، ليسوا من أولاد الدُّنيا، وهو الصحيح من أقوال كثيرة، وقيل : هم أولاد المؤمنين الذين ماتوا صغاراً.
And they are the women of Paradise, described as having wide eyes. (And the wildan) i.e., the servant boys, and they are in the form of the servant boys of this world, and they are the advance gifts of the people of Paradise. And it is said: They are the children of disbelievers who die before puberty, and it is reported that they are the servants of the people of Paradise. His statement: (And they are the women of Paradise): It is narrated that a cloud rained from the Throne and created the hur from drops of mercy, then a tent was pitched for each of them on the bank of the rivers, its width forty miles, and it has no door, until when a saint of Allah enters Paradise, the tent splits open at a door, so that the saint of Allah knows that the eyes of creatures, angels and servants, have not taken her; so she is confined, having been confined from the eyes of creatures. And this is the meaning of His statement, exalted: 'Hur, confined in pavilions.' (1) And the correct view is that the women of this world are better than the hur al-ayn by seventy thousand times. (2) His statement: (And the wildan) with kasrah on the waw, plural of walid meaning born, and they are called 'wildan' because they are in their shape and form. His statement: (And they are the servants of the people of Paradise), i.e., they are created in Paradise initially, like the hur al-ayn, not from the children of this world, and this is the correct among many sayings. And it is said: They are the children of the believers who died young.
